Conditions for Accepting Reports and the Second Division of Discontinuity
Explains conditions for accepting narrations and defines apparent/hidden discontinuity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for accepting a narrator's report, differentiate between acceptance of narration and testimony, and define apparent and hidden discontinuity in hadith, including the preferred Hanafi position on narrations from innovators.

Core Idea
Narrator acceptance requires four conditions; discontinuity can be apparent or hidden, and innovators' narrations are accepted unless they permit lying.

This passage from the chapter on categories of Sunnah establishes foundational usul principles for evaluating hadith. It first lists the four conditions for narrator acceptance (Islam, justice, intellect, memory) and then explains exceptions where narrations are accepted despite testimony rejection. The passage then defines the second division of discontinuity (inqita') as either apparent or hidden, with hidden discontinuity occurring due to contradiction with stronger sources or narrator deficiency. Finally, it addresses a key ikhtilaf regarding narrations from innovators, concluding that acceptance is the relied-upon position if the innovator does not permit lying.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four conditions for narrator acceptance
From the opening statement, list the four conditions: Islam, justice, intellect, and memory. Note which narrators are excluded for each condition (disbeliever, sinner, child/mentally deficient, heedless).
These are the basic requirements for a narrator to be considered reliable (thiqa) in Hanafi usul.
2
Distinguish between riwayah and shahadah
The text states that the blind, the one punished for slander (after repentance), woman, and slave have their narrations accepted despite their testimony being rejected. Understand the reason: testimony requires extra discernment (tamyiz za'id) that is absent in these individuals, while narration only requires the four conditions.
This distinction is crucial; many students mistakenly think that if testimony is rejected, narration is also rejected.
3
Define the second division: discontinuity (inqita')
The second division concerns discontinuity of the chain. It is of two types: apparent (zahir) and hidden (batin). Apparent discontinuity includes mursal and munqati'. Hidden discontinuity arises either from the report itself (contradiction with Quran, mutawatir, mashhur, or being anomalous in common afflictions) or from the narrator (deficiency in intellect, memory, justice, Islam, or other issues like fainting of Companions).
Hidden discontinuity is a more subtle defect that requires in-depth critical analysis.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf on innovators' narrations
The text presents two opinions: some reject innovators' narrations absolutely because innovation is a worse sin and makes them unjust; others distinguish between those who permit lying (like Ghulat al-Shi'a) and those who do not, accepting the latter due to preponderance of truthfulness. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is the second, supported by the fact that the Sahihain contain narrations from innovators.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both sides have evidence, but the relied-upon Hanafi position favors acceptance when the innovator is not known for lying.
5
Apply the principles to evaluate a hadith
Given a hypothetical hadith, use the four conditions to check the narrator's eligibility, then examine for hidden discontinuity by checking for contradiction with stronger sources or narrator deficiencies.
This step synthesizes the lesson into a practical skill for ijtihad.

Source Text

باب أقسام السنة بيان التقسيم الثاني ولهذا لا يقبل خبر الكافر والفاسق والصبي والمعتوه والذي اشتدّت غفلته، تفريع على الشروط الأربعة على غير ترتيب اللف، فالكافر راجع إلى الإسلام والفاسق إلى العدالة، والصبي والمعتوه إلى كمال العقل والذي اشتدّت غفلته إلى الضبط، وأما الأعمى والمحدود في القذف والمرأة المراد بعد توبته والعبد فتقبل روايتهم في الحديث لوجود الشرائط وإن لم تقبل شهادتهم في المعاملات هكذا قيل [بيان التقسيم الثاني] أي الأربعة المعتبرة والتقسيم الثاني في الانقطاع، أي عدم اتصال الحديث بنا من رسول الله . وهو نوعان: ظاهر وباطن. من كاف بناءً على أن الحرج مدفوع في الدين قلنا: إن الواجب الاستيصاف، وليس المراد بالاستيصاف أن يسأله عن صفات الله تعالى أو يسأله عن الإيمان وما هو وما صفاته، فإن هذا بحر عميق يغرق فيه العقول بل المراد أن يذكر صفات الله تعالى التي يجب أن يعرفها المؤمنون، ويسأله هو كذلك أي تشهد أن الله تعالى موصوف بالصفات المذكورة فيقول نعم فيكمل إيمانه، وهذا هو المراد، والله أعلم بقوله تعالى: فامتحنوهن. والمعتوه إلخ هو من عته عنها وعتاها نقص عقله غير جنون. (السنبلي) لا يقبل خبر الكافر إلخ وأما المبتدع ذو العقائد الباطلة، فقيل: لا يقبل روايته أصلاً، فإنه فاسق بها فوق فسق أعمال الجوارح، فهو ساقط العدالة، وقيل: إن أباح الكذب كغُلاة الشيعة فإنهم يبيحون الكذب بالتقية، فلا تقبل روايته لشبهة الكذب، وإن لم يبح الكذب فهو مقبول الرواية بعد تحقق الشرائط لرجحان جانب الصدق فيه، كذا أفاد بحر العلوم مولانا عبد العلي بالله والقول الأول غير صحيح، فإنه وردت الروايات من المبتدعين في "الصحيحين" كذا قال النووي في "شرح صحيح مسلم". (القمر) والذي اشتدّت إلخ بأن كان هواه ونسيانه أغلب من حفظه . (القمر) على الشروط الأربعة أي العدالة والضبط والإسلام والعقل. (القمر) وإن لم تقبل شهادتهم إلخ: لأن الشهادة في حقوق الناس تحتاج إلى تمييز زائد وهو معدوم في الأعمى، وإلى ولاية فإن للشاهد ولاية على المشهود عليه؛ إذ هو يلزم عليه شيئا وهي معدومة بالرق وقاصرة بالأنوثة وأما المحدود بالقذف فعدم قبول الشهادة من تمام حده قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَقْبَلُوا لَهُمْ شَهَادَةً أَبدا﴾ (النور: ٤) كذا في "التوضيح". (القمر) التقسيم الثاني: أي مما يختص بالسنن.(القمر) وباطن وذلك إما لأمر يرجع إلى نفس الخبر بكونه معارضا للكتاب أو للخبر المتواتر أو للمشهور، أو بكونه شاذا فيما يعم به البلوى، وإما لأمر يرجع إلى نفس الناقل كنقصان في العقل كخبر المعتوه والصبي، أو في الضبط، أو في العدالة، أو في الإسلام أو لأمر غير ذلك كأعراض الصحابة ، كذا في "التلويح". (السنبلي)
Chapter: Categories of Sunnah. Explanation of the second division. For this reason, the report of the disbeliever, the sinner, the child, the mentally deficient, and the one whose heedlessness is intense is not accepted, as a branching of the four conditions without following the order of the letters. So the disbeliever goes back to Islam, the sinner to justice, the child and mentally deficient to completeness of intellect, and the one whose heedlessness is intense to memory. As for the blind, the one punished for slander after his repentance, the woman, and the slave, their narration is accepted in hadith due to the existence of the conditions, even if their testimony is not accepted in transactions. Thus it is said. [Explanation of the second division] i.e., the four considered conditions. And the second division is concerning discontinuity, i.e., the lack of connection of the hadith to us from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. It is two types: apparent and hidden. ... (continues with various comments) ... And that is either for a matter relating to the report itself, such as being contradictory to the Book, or to the mutawatir report, or to the well-known report, or being anomalous in matters of general necessity; or for a matter relating to the narrator himself, such as a deficiency in intellect like the report of the mentally deficient and the child, or in memory, or in justice, or in Islam, or for another matter like the faintings of the Companions, as in al-Talwih. (al-Sanbali)
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on categories of Sunnah (باب أقسام السنة) and immediately proceeds to the second division (بيان التقسيم الثاني). The first division is not shown here, but the second division concerns discontinuity (انقطاع) of the hadith chain. The text first lists the conditions for accepting a report: Islam, justice (عدالة), complete intellect, and good memory. It explains that the report of a disbeliever is rejected due to lack of Islam; of a sinner due to lack of justice; of a child or mentally deficient due to lack of intellect; and of one with intense heedlessness due to lack of memory. Then it notes that a blind person, one who has been punished for false accusation of adultery (after repentance), a woman, and a slave have their narrations accepted because they meet the four conditions, even though their testimony in legal transactions is not accepted. The text then gives the definition of the second division: discontinuity, which is either apparent (ظاهر) – such as mursal, munqati' – or hidden (باطن), which includes defects in the text or narrator. The rest of the passage consists of marginal notes (e.g., from al-Sanbali, al-Qamar) discussing whether innovaters' narrations are accepted, the meaning of 'istisaf' (testing faith with questions about Allah's attributes), and the reasoning for not accepting testimony of certain individuals with Quranic evidence. The hidden discontinuity is explained as conflicting with the Quran, mutawatir, or well-known hadith, or being anomalous in matters of common affliction, or due to a narrator deficiency in intellect, memory, justice, Islam, or even companionship issues like fainting.

Key Terms
الانقطاع (al-inqita'): Discontinuity in the chain of transmission, i.e., the hadith not being directly connected to the Prophet.
الشروط الأربعة (al-shurut al-arba'a): The four conditions for accepting a narrator's report: Islam, justice, sanity, and memory.
المبتدع (al-mubtadi'): An innovator in religious matters, one who holds beliefs contrary to the mainstream Sunni creed.
التمييز الزائد (al-tamyiz al-za'id): Extra discernment required for testimony (shahadah) that is not required for narration (riwayah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the testimony of a blind person not accepted in transactions, even though his hadith narration is accepted?
A) Because blindness indicates lack of intellect.
B) Because testimony requires extra discernment and authority, which are absent in the blind.
C) Because blind people cannot see witnesses.
D) Because the Quran explicitly rejects blind testimony.

Key Takeaway
A narrator's hadith is accepted if they meet the four conditions (Islam, justice, intellect, memory); testimony requires additional factors; discontinuity can be apparent or hidden, and innovators' narrations are accepted if they do not permit lying.

Mursal Hadith: Definition and Hanafi Perspective
Defines Mursal, its four types, and discusses acceptance with consensus on Sahabi Mursal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi usul definition of Mursal from the Muhaddithun definition and evaluate the acceptance of a Companion's Mursal by consensus.

Core Idea
Hanafi usul: any omission in chain is Mursal; Companion's Mursal accepted by consensus.

This passage defines the Mursal hadith and its categories, contrasting the terminology of usul scholars and hadith scholars. Understanding this distinction is crucial for evaluating hadith evidence in Hanafi legal methodology, especially when deriving rulings from reports that lack a fully connected chain.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of Mursal in usul
According to the text, the usul definition is that a narrator deletes any number of links between himself and the Prophet, saying directly 'The Messenger of Allah said...'. This includes omitting the Companion, a middle narrator, or even the entire chain.
Note the contrast with hadith scholar terminology.
2
List the four categories of Mursal
The text divides Mursal into four types based on who performs the irsal: (1) a Companion sends it, (2) a Tabi'i sends it, (3) a Taba' al-Tabi'i sends it, (4) it is mursal from one angle but not another.
These categories help determine the level of potential weakness.
3
Analyze the acceptance of a Companion's Mursal
The passage states it is accepted by consensus. Initially, the reason given is that a Companion usually heard directly from the Prophet. However, a corrected reasoning is that the Companion omits another trustworthy Companion intermediary, ensuring reliability.
This corrected reasoning is more precise and avoids circularity.
4
Contrast usul and muhaddithun terminologies
Usul scholars call any omission 'Mursal'. Hadith scholars differentiate: missing Companion = Mursal, missing middle link = Munqati', missing beginning/whole chain = Mu'allaq. The passage acknowledges both as valid within their disciplines.
This ikhtilaf affects how hadiths are classified and used in istinbat.
5
Determine practical implication for istinbat
In Hanafi usul, a Mursal hadith (broadly defined) may be accepted if the missing narrator is known to be trustworthy, especially if it comes from a Companion. This allows more flexibility in deriving rulings compared to hadith scholars who may reject certain categories outright.
For example, a Tabi'i Mursal might be considered for istihsan if corroborated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان الحديث المرسل أما الظاهر فالمرسل من الأخبار بأن لا يذكر الراوي الوسائط التي بينه وبين رسول الله ، بل يقول: قال الرسول : كذا ، وهو أربعة أقسام؛ لأنه إما أن يرسله الصحابي له، أي الأرسال أو يرسله القرن الثاني والثالث، أو يرسله من دونهم، أو هو مرسل من وجه دون وجه. أي الإرسال أي قرن التابعين " أي قرن تبع التابعين بنفسه وهو: إن كان من الصحابي الله فمقبول بالإجماع؛ لأن غالب حاله أن يسمع منه عليها، وإن كان يحتمل أن يسمع من صحابي آخر ولم يكن هو بنفسه حاضرًا حينئذ، فإن أرسل الصحابي الله يقول: قال رسول الله : كذا ، وإن أسند يقول: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أو حدثني رسول الله عليها كذا. صل الله أما الظاهر فالمرسل في الكلام مسامحة، والتقدير إما لانقطاع الظاهر، فإرسال المرسل من الأخبار. (القمر) الوسائط التي إلخ والمراد أن يحذف الراوي من السند سواء كان المحذوف الصحابي السامع منه أو من هو بعده، وسواء كان المحذوف واحدًا أو أكثر أو جميع الرواة، فهذه الأقسام كلها من المرسل، هذا على اصطلاح أهل الأصول، وأما أهل الحديث فقالوا: إنه لو حذف الصحابي السامع منه وقال التابعي السامع منه، قال رسول الله فهو مرسل ولو حذف الراوي فيما بين السند فهو المنقطع كأن يقول تبع التابعي: قال أبو هريرة، ولو حذف أول السند أو تمام السند فهو المعلّق كأن نقول: قال رسول الله : كذا. هكذا قال الشيخ عبد الحق الدهلوي في مقدمة مصطلحات علم الحديث. (القمر) القرن الثاني: وفي المرقاة شرح المشكاة"، وفي شرح السنة" القرن كل طبقة مقترنين في وقت قيل: سمي "قرنًا"؛ لأنه يقرن أمة بأمة وعالما بعالم، وهو مصدر قرنت، وجعل اسما للوقت أو لأهله. (القمر) بالإجماع: أي إجماع المتقدمين فلا يضره خلاف بعض المتأخرين، كذا قيل. (القمر) لأن غالب حاله أن يسمع إلخ: لتحقق الصحبة معه اعلم أن ذكر هذه الجملة في غير محلها، فإن الكلام في إرسال الصحابي ، وهذا لا يتحقق إلا أن يتحقق أن الصحابي له ترك الراوي الذي بينه وبين النبي ، وحينئذ فكيف يمكن حمل هذا الحديث المرسل على السماع من النبي ، فالأصوب أن يقال في وجه مقبولية إرسال الصحابي: إن إرساله يكون بإسقاط صحابي آخر متوسط، فهذا الصحابي عليه الآخر هو المسقط في المرسل، والصحابة كلهم عدول فليس ههنا جهالة المسقط، بل معلوم ،عدالته فهذا الحديث المرسل المقبول؛ إذ ليس فيه شبهة. (القمر)
Explanation of the Mursal Hadith. As for the apparent, it is the mursal from reports, i.e., the narrator does not mention the links between him and the Messenger of Allah, but says: 'The Messenger of Allah said such and such.' It has four divisions: either the Companion sends it, i.e., the sending; or the second century (i.e., the generation of Tabi'un) sends it; or the third century (i.e., the generation of Tabi' al-Tabi'in) sends it; or it is sent from one aspect and not another. ... If it is from a Companion, it is accepted by consensus, because usually he hears directly from the Prophet, even though it is possible he heard from another Companion and was not himself present at that time. ... As for the apparent, mursal is used loosely, and the estimation is for apparent discontinuity, so sending is from mursal reports. (al-Qamar) 'The links' etc. means that the narrator deletes from the chain, whether the deleted is the Companion he heard from or someone after him, whether one or more or all narrators. All these categories are considered mursal according to usul scholars. As for hadith scholars, they said: If the hearing Companion is deleted and the hearing Tabi'i says 'The Messenger of Allah said...', it is mursal; if a narrator in the middle is deleted, it is munqati'; if the beginning or entire chain is deleted, it is mu'allaq. ... (al-Qamar) 'Second century'... 'By consensus' means consensus of the early scholars; disagreement of some later ones does not harm it. ... The more correct view for the acceptance of a Companion's mursal is that he is omitting another Companion intermediary, and all Companions are trustworthy, so there is no unknown transmitter.
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage is a thorough explanation of the Mursal Hadith (الحديث المرسل), which is a type of apparent discontinuity (الانقطاع الظاهر). It begins with a definition: a narrator drops all links between himself and the Prophet, saying directly 'The Messenger of Allah said such and such.' The text then divides Mursal into four categories based on the generation of the one who sends (yursil): (1) a Companion sends it, (2) a second-century narrator (Tabi'i) sends it, (3) a third-century narrator (Tabi' al-Tabi'in) sends it, or (4) it is mursal from one angle but not another (e.g., when a narrator reports a hadith sometimes with a full chain and sometimes without). The key ruling is that when a Companion sends a hadith (i.e., says 'The Prophet said...' without naming his source), it is accepted by consensus of the early scholars. The reasoning given initially is that a Companion usually heard directly from the Prophet. However, a marginal note (from al-Qamar) finds this reasoning problematic because the Companion is already omitting a link; the more correct reason is that the Companion is omitting another Companion intermediary, and all Companions are reliable, so there is no unknown transmitter. The passage also contrasts the terminology of usul scholars with that of hadith scholars: according to usul, any omission in the chain is 'mursal', whereas hadith scholars differentiate: deletion of a Companion is 'mursal', deletion of a middle link is 'munqati', and deletion of the beginning or whole chain is 'mu'allaq'. This distinction is important for understanding the classification of hadith. The marginal notes also discuss the meaning of 'qarn' (century/generation) and confirm that the consensus on Companion's mursal is from the early scholars, so later disagreement does not affect the ruling.

Key Terms
الحديث المرسل (al-hadith al-mursal): A hadith where the narrator omits one or more links in the chain, often saying 'The Messenger of Allah said...' without mentioning the intermediary.
الصحابي (al-sahabi): A Companion of the Prophet. When a Companion says 'The Prophet said...', it is considered Mursal if he did not hear directly, but accepted by consensus.
المنقطع (al-munqati'): According to hadith scholars, a hadith where a middle link in the chain is missing, but according to Hanafi usul this is still considered mursal.
المعلق (al-mu'allaq): According to hadith scholars, a hadith where the beginning or the entire chain is omitted, but according to Hanafi usul this is also considered mursal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the usul definition in this passage, which of the following would be considered a Mursal hadith?
A) A hadith where a Tabi'i says 'The Prophet said...' without mentioning a Companion.
B) A hadith where a Companion says 'The Prophet said...' without mentioning his source.
C) A hadith where a Taba' al-Tabi'i says 'The Prophet said...' omitting all previous narrators.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, Mursal is any hadith with omitted links; a Companion's Mursal is accepted by consensus because the omitted link is another trustworthy Companion.

The Mursal Hadith: Definition and Hanafi Acceptance
Defines the mursal hadith and the inter-madhhab dispute over its acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the mursal hadith according to Hanafi usul, distinguish its categories, and explain why Hanafis accept mursal from the Tabi'un while the Shafi'i school rejects it.

Core Idea
Mursal hadith is accepted by Hanafis because the omitted reporter is presumed trustworthy.

The mursal hadith is a key category of transmitted reports where the narrator skips the intermediaries and directly attributes a statement to the Prophet. This lesson explains the definition and four categories of mursal according to Hanafi usul, and then delves into the classical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over the acceptance of mursal from the second and third generations. By understanding the arguments on both sides, you will grasp a foundational point in Hanafi hadith methodology.

Guided Path
1
Define the Mursal Hadith
Read the definition carefully: the narrator says 'The Prophet said' without mentioning the chain. Note that Hanafi usul includes any omission (one or more narrators), while hadith specialists use narrower terms like munqati' and mu'allaq.
The term 'mursal' is used broadly by usul scholars; be aware of terminological differences.
2
Identify the Four Categories
The passage lists four types based on who omits the chain: a Companion, a second-century narrator (Tabi'i), a third-century narrator (Atba' al-Tabi'in), or someone later. Recognize that the ruling varies by category.
Mursal from a Companion is accepted by consensus; the dispute concerns later generations.
3
Analyze the Dispute
Contrast the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions. The Hanafi reason: the omitting narrator is trustworthy and would not drop a weak reporter. The Shafi'i reason: the omitted person is unknown, so the hadith is unreliable.
The dispute has practical consequences: Hanafis use mursal as evidence in fiqh, Shafi'is require a connected chain.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi counter-argument: the mursal narrator is an expert who vouches for the omitted reporter's reliability, so there is no real ignorance. This reasoning is consistent with the principle of accepting trustworthy narrators.
This reflects the Hanafi principle that the 'adalah (trustworthiness) of the narrator extends to those he omits.
5
Consider the Limitation
Note that even Hanafis do not allow using mursal to add to the Quran; the established text (Quran and mutawatir) is stronger than ijtihad-based reports.
This shows the hierarchy of evidence in Hanafi usul.

Source Text

باب أقسام السنة
بيان الحديث المرسل
أما الظاهر فالمرسل من الأخبار بأن لا يذكر الراوي الوسائط التي بينه وبين رسول الله ، بل يقول: قال الرسول : كذا ، وهو أربعة أقسام؛ لأنه إما أن يرسله الصحابي له، أي الأرسال أو يرسله القرن الثاني والثالث، أو يرسله من دونهم، أو هو مرسل من وجه دون وجه.
أي الإرسال
أي قرن التابعين " أي قرن تبع التابعين
بنفسه
وهو: إن كان من الصحابي الله فمقبول بالإجماع؛ لأن غالب حاله أن يسمع منه عليها، وإن كان يحتمل أن يسمع من صحابي آخر ولم يكن هو بنفسه حاضرًا حينئذ، فإن أرسل الصحابي الله يقول: قال رسول الله : كذا ، وإن أسند يقول: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أو حدثني رسول الله عليها كذا.
صل الله
أما الظاهر فالمرسل في الكلام مسامحة، والتقدير إما لانقطاع الظاهر، فإرسال المرسل من الأخبار. (القمر) الوسائط التي إلخ والمراد أن يحذف الراوي من السند سواء كان المحذوف الصحابي السامع منه أو من هو بعده، وسواء كان المحذوف واحدًا أو أكثر أو جميع الرواة، فهذه الأقسام كلها من المرسل، هذا على اصطلاح أهل الأصول، وأما أهل الحديث فقالوا: إنه لو حذف الصحابي السامع منه وقال التابعي السامع منه، قال رسول الله فهو مرسل ولو حذف الراوي فيما بين السند فهو المنقطع كأن يقول تبع التابعي: قال أبو هريرة، ولو حذف أول السند أو تمام السند فهو المعلّق كأن نقول: قال رسول الله : كذا. هكذا قال الشيخ عبد الحق الدهلوي في مقدمة مصطلحات علم الحديث. (القمر) القرن الثاني: وفي المرقاة شرح المشكاة"، وفي شرح السنة" القرن كل طبقة مقترنين في وقت قيل: سمي "قرنًا"؛ لأنه يقرن أمة بأمة وعالما بعالم، وهو مصدر قرنت، وجعل اسما للوقت أو لأهله. (القمر)
بالإجماع: أي إجماع المتقدمين فلا يضره خلاف بعض المتأخرين، كذا قيل. (القمر) لأن غالب حاله أن يسمع إلخ: لتحقق الصحبة معه اعلم أن ذكر هذه الجملة في غير محلها، فإن الكلام في إرسال الصحابي ، وهذا لا يتحقق إلا أن يتحقق أن الصحابي له ترك الراوي الذي بينه وبين النبي ، وحينئذ فكيف يمكن حمل هذا الحديث المرسل على السماع من النبي ، فالأصوب أن يقال في وجه مقبولية إرسال الصحابي: إن إرساله يكون بإسقاط صحابي آخر متوسط، فهذا الصحابي عليه الآخر هو المسقط في المرسل، والصحابة كلهم عدول فليس ههنا جهالة المسقط، بل معلوم ،عدالته فهذا الحديث المرسل المقبول؛ إذ ليس فيه شبهة. (القمر)
ومن القرن الثاني والثالث كذلك عندنا، أي مقبول عند الحنفية بأن يقول التابعي أو تبع التابعي: قال رسول الله : كذا، وعند الشافعي له لا يقبل؛ لأنه إذا جهلت صفات الراوي لم يكن الحديث حجة، فإذا جهلت صفاته وذاته فبالطريق الأولى إلا إذا تؤيد بحجة قطعية، أو قياس صحيح، أو تلقته الأمة بالقبول، أو ثبت اتصاله بوجه آخر.
كالعدالة
كالكتاب والسنة المشهورة
أو قول الصحابة
ونحن نقول: إن كلامنا في إرسال من لو أسنده إلى شخص آخر يقبل، ولا يُظن به الكذب، فلئلا يظن به الكذب على رسول الله الله ، أولى، بل هو فوق المسند؛ لأن العدل إذا اتضح له طريق الإسناد يقول بلا وسوسة قال علي: كذا، وإذا لم يتضح له ذلك يذكر أسماء الراوي ليحمله ما تحمل عنه، ويفرغ ذمته ذلك.

أي لذلك العبدل أي مقبول إلخ فإن الإرسال إن كان من القرن الثاني أي التابعين فالمسقط الصحابي ، وإن من تبع التابعين فالمسقط هو التابعي، وعلى كلا التقديرين فالمسقط ليس بكاذب؛ لأنه أخبر النبي بخيرية قرن الصحابة والتابعين وتبعهم. (القمر) بالطريق الأولى ونحن نقول: إن المسقط مجهول الذات معلوم العدالة؛ لأن المرسل العدل العالم بشأن الحديث اعتمد عليه، فلا حرج في قبول روايته. (القمر) إلا إلخ استثناء من قوله: لا يقبل.(القمر) أو ثبت اتصاله إلخ بأن أسنده غير مرسله أو أسنده مرسله مرة أخرى كذا قيل. (القمر) به: الضمير راجع إلى "من". (القمر) فلئلا يظن به الكذب إلخ : أي فعدم ظن الكذب به على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أولى. (القمر) بل هو : أي المرسل فوق المسند، فيرجّح هذا المرسل على المسند عند التعارض، وهو مذهب عيسى بن أبان، إلا أنه لا يجوز به الزيادة على الكتاب؛ لأن هذه فضيلة تثبت للمرسل ،بالاجتهاد فلو جاز به الزيادة على الكتاب لزم إثبات الزيادة على الكتاب بالرأي وهو لا يجوز ، وأما قوّة المشهور" فثابتة بالنص، وما يثبت بالنص فهو فوق ما ثبت بالرأي، فيجوز به الزيادة على الكتاب. (القمر)
لأن العدل إلخ الحاصل أن من أرسل فهو عادل، وهو يعلم أن المسقط عدل مقبول الرواية فكيف لا يقبل الحديث المرسل، ولذا قيل: إن من أرسل فقد تكفل الصحة، ومن أسند فقد أحال على غيره. (القمر) يقول بلا وسوسة إلى ألا ترى إلى ما قال الحسن: متى قلت لكم: حدثني "فلان" فهو حديثه لا غير، ومتى قلت: "قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم " سمعته من سبعين أو أكثر. (القمر) ليحمله ما تحمّل عنه: أي ليحمل ذلك العدل الراوي ما تحمله ذلك العدل عن ذلك الراوي. في "الصراح" حملته الرسالة أي كلّفته حملها، وتحمّل الحمالة أي حملنا. (القمر)
Chapter on the Divisions of the Sunnah. Explanation of the Mursal Hadith. As for the apparent, the mursal from reports is that the narrator does not mention the intermediaries between him and the Messenger of Allah, but rather says: The Messenger said such and such. It is of four types: either the Companion sends it, or the second or third century sends it, or someone after them sends it, or it is mursal from one aspect but not another. ...
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the mursal hadith according to Hanafi usul. It begins by defining mursal as a hadith where the narrator omits the chain between himself and the Prophet, saying directly 'the Prophet said.' Four categories are given based on who omits the chain (a Companion, a second-century narrator, a third-century narrator, or someone later). The commentary then addresses the acceptance of mursal hadith, noting that mursal from a Companion is accepted by consensus. The Hanafi position is that mursal from the second and third centuries (Tabi'un and Atba' al-Tabi'un) is also accepted, whereas the Shafi'i school rejects it unless supported by a decisive proof or accepted by the ummah. The reasoning is that the omitted reporter (musqit) is trustworthy; since the earlier generations are known for reliability, there is no suspicion of lying. The passage also clarifies terminology differences between usul scholars and hadith scholars regarding mursal, munqati', and mu'allaq. It concludes by mentioning the view of ‘Isa ibn Aban that a mursal hadith can be preferred over a musnad hadith when conflicting, but it cannot be used to add to the Quran because that would be based on ijtihad, whereas the established text is stronger.

Key Terms
المرسل (al-mursal): A hadith where a narrator omits the chain between him and the Prophet, saying directly 'The Prophet said.'
المسقط (al-musqit): The reporter who omits the chain (the one who 'drops' the intermediate narrators).
القرن الثاني (al-qarn al-thani): The second generation after the Prophet, i.e., the Tabi'un.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a mursal hadith from a Tabi'i (second generation) accepted?
A) Because the Tabi'i is a Companion.
B) Because the omitted reporter (musqit) is known to be trustworthy.
C) Because the hadith is supported by Quran.
D) Because all hadith are acceptable.

Key Takeaway
Mursal hadith from trustworthy narrators is accepted by Hanafis as valid proof, provided the omitted reporter is presumed reliable.

The Hanafi Acceptance of Mursal Hadith from the Early Generations
Explains Hanafi acceptance of mursal from first three generations versus Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on mursal hadith from the first three generations and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
A mursal from the first three generations is accepted because the mursil's integrity and the virtue of the era guarantee the omitted link's trustworthiness.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the mursal hadith—where a Successor or later narrator directly attributes to the Prophet—is a contested source of law. This passage presents the Hanafi position that mursal from the first three generations (Companions, Successors, and their followers) is accepted as proof, and contrasts it with the Shafi'i rejection. The core argument rests on the reliability of the mursil and the inherent virtue of those early generations, as testified by the Prophet himself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State that Hanafis accept mursal from the second and third centuries (Successors and their followers) as proof (hujja).
The text says 'مقبول عند الحنفية'.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i rejects such mursal because the omitted narrator's attributes and identity are unknown, making the hadith unreliable.
He allows it only if supported by a definitive proof, accepted by the ummah, etc.
3
Trace the Hanafi proof
The mursil is upright and knows the omitted link is trustworthy. Also, the Prophet testified to the virtue of these generations, so the omitted link is known to be upright.
The source cites the hadith about 'خيرية قرن الصحابة والتابعين وتبعهم'.
4
Understand the superiority of mursal
The Hanafi view holds that a mursal is stronger than a musnad because the mursil takes full responsibility, while the musnid refers to others.
This is attributed to Isa ibn Aban, with the caveat that mursal cannot be used to add to the Quran.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis use mursal from early generations as legal evidence; Shafi'is require additional support.
This affects rulings in many fiqh chapters where only mursal reports exist.

Section on the divisions of the Sunnah. Explanation of the mursal hadith. And from the second and third centuries similarly in our view, i.e., it is accepted according to the Hanafis when the Successor or the follower of the Successor says: 'The Messenger of Allah said such-and-such.' According to al-Shafi'i, it is not accepted because if the attributes of the narrator are unknown, the hadith is not a proof; if his attributes and identity are unknown, it is even more so, unless it is supported by a definitive proof, a valid analogy, the nation has received it with acceptance, or its continuity is established by another means. Like justice, like the Book and the well-known Sunnah, or the statement of the Companions. And we say: Our discussion concerns the sending of someone who, if he had attributed it to another person, would be accepted, and lying is not suspected of him, so it is even more fitting that lying about the Messenger of Allah not be suspected of him. Rather, it is above the musnad because the upright person, when the chain of transmission is clear to him, says without hesitation: 'Ali said such-and-such.' And when it is not clear to him, he mentions the names of the narrator so that he may bear what was transmitted from him, and thus discharge his responsibility. That is, someone who was such-and-such, i.e., accepted, etc. For if the sending is from the second century, i.e., the Successors, then the omitted one is the Companion; if from the followers of the Successors, then the omitted one is the Successor. In both cases, the omitted one is not a liar because he reported from the Prophet about the virtue of the generation of the Companions and the Successors and their followers. (al-Qamar) A fortiori, and we say: The omitted one is unknown in identity but known in justice because the upright mursil, knowledgeable about the matter of hadith, relied on him, so there is no harm in accepting his narration. (al-Qamar) 'Except' etc. is an exception from his statement 'is not accepted.' (al-Qamar) 'Or its continuity is established' etc., such as if someone other than the mursil attributes it with a chain, or the mursil himself attributes it with a chain another time, as has been said. (al-Qamar) 'To him': the pronoun refers to 'whoever'. (al-Qamar) 'So that lying not be suspected' etc.: i.e., the absence of suspicion of lying about the Messenger of Allah is more appropriate. (al-Qamar) 'Rather, he': i.e., the mursil is above the musnid, so this mursal is given precedence over the musnad when they conflict, and this is the school of Isa ibn Aban, except that it is not permissible to add to the Qur'an through it because this virtue is established for the mursal through ijtihad; if addition to the Qur'an were permitted through it, it would necessitate establishing an addition to the Qur'an by opinion, which is not permissible. As for the strength of the well-known (mashhur), it is established by textual proof, and what is established by textual proof is above what is established by opinion, so addition to the Qur'an is permitted through it. (al-Qamar) 'Because the upright person' etc.: the conclusion is that whoever sends (mursil) is upright, and he knows that the omitted one is upright and acceptable in narration, so how can a mursal hadith not be accepted? Hence it was said: 'Whoever sends has taken responsibility for authenticity, and whoever attributes a chain has referred to others.' (al-Qamar) 'He says without hesitation' etc.: Do you not see what al-Hasan said: 'Whenever I say to you: "So-and-so narrated to me," it is his hadith only; and whenever I say: "The Messenger of Allah said," I have heard it from seventy or more.' (al-Qamar) 'So that he may bear what was transmitted from him': i.e., so that that upright narrator may bear what that upright person transmitted from that narrator. In al-Sirah, 'I charged him with the message' means I imposed its bearing upon him, and 'he bore the responsibility' means he carried it. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage begins with a section heading 'Explanation of the mursal hadith' and then presents the central dispute: Hanafis accept mursal hadith from the second and third generations (Successors and their followers), while al-Shafi'i rejects them unless supported by a definitive proof, valid analogy, acceptance by the ummah, or another means of establishing continuity. The Hanafi reasoning rests on two foundations: first, the mursil (the one who omits the link) is an upright person not suspected of lying, and his omission is based on knowledge that the omitted link is also upright; second, the virtue of the early generations guarantees the trustworthiness of the omitted link, as the Prophet testified to the goodness of the Companions, Successors, and their followers. The text further argues that a mursal hadith is actually stronger than a musnad one because the mursil takes personal responsibility, whereas the musnid merely refers to others. Isa ibn Aban's view is cited: in case of conflict, the mursal is preferred over the musnad, but this preference does not allow adding to the Qur'an through it because that would be using opinion to add to the Qur'an. However, the well-known (mashhur) hadith, being textually proven, does allow such addition. The passage concludes by illustrating with al-Hasan's practice and linguistic notes from al-Sirah.

Key Terms
الحديث المرسل (al-ḥadīth al-mursal): A hadith where a Successor or later narrator says 'The Messenger of Allah said' without mentioning the Companion or intermediate narrator.
المسقط (al-musqaṭ): The omitted narrator in a mursal hadith, i.e., the Companion or Successor whose name is not mentioned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, why is mursal from the first three generations accepted as a proof?
A) Because the omitted link is always a Companion.
B) Because the mursil is upright and knows the omitted link is trustworthy.
C) Because al-Shafi'i also accepts it.
D) Because the chain is never missing.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts mursal from the first three generations as hujja, based on the mursil's integrity and the prophetic testimony to the virtue of those generations.

Mursal from Later Generations: Conditions and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on later mursal and resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on accepting mursal from after the third century and distinguish the conditions under which such mursal is accepted or rejected.

Core Idea
Mursal from later generations is accepted only if the sender is a qualified hadith scholar.

Having discussed mursal from the early generations, this passage turns to mursal transmitted after the third Islamic century. It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between al-Karakhi, who rejects all later mursal due to the corruption of later times, and the preferred view that conditions acceptance on the sender's expertise. Understanding this nuance is key to applying the Hanafi methodology for evaluating mursal hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The passage asks whether a mursal hadith from a narrator who lived after the second or third century is acceptable. The text initially states it is 'accepted' (مقبول), but then introduces a contrary view.
The 'sending' (mursal) refers to a hadith where the narrator omits the Companion or Successor and directly attributes to the Prophet.
2
Understand al-Karakhi's objection
Al-Karakhi argues that the time after the three virtuous centuries is a time of corruption (زمان فسق), so the omitted link cannot be assumed trustworthy. Therefore, such mursal should not be accepted.
The three centuries refer to the period of the Companions, Successors, and their successors.
3
Trace the Hanafi response and refinement
The text then provides a more nuanced view: the same cause (justice and precision) that justifies accepting mursal from early generations applies to later generations if the mursil is a hadith scholar who can distinguish authentic from weak. Thus acceptance depends on the mursil's qualification, not the era.
The refined position reconciles the principle with al-Karakhi's concern.
4
Analyze the dual transmission example
The passage illustrates with the hadith 'لا نكاح إلا بولي' transmitted as musnad by Isra'il ibn Yunus and as mursal by Shu'ba. It explains that when a hadith is both musnad and mursal, the musnad version prevails because the chain is complete.
This example shows how to resolve conflict between complete and incomplete chains.
5
Define 'batin' defects
Finally, the passage introduces 'al-batin' defects — where the chain appears connected but the defect lies in the narrator's character or contradiction to a higher proof. The conditions of a narrator (intelligence, Islam, precision, justice) must be met; otherwise the narration is rejected.
This completes the discussion on mursal by addressing hidden defects.

خلافا
كذلك عند الكرخي النبي عليه بعد التهم فلا يقبل.
لابن أبان؛ لأن الزمان بعد القرون الثلاثة زمان فسق، ولم يشهد

And the sending (mursal) of those other than these, i.e., when someone after the second and third centuries says: 'The Prophet said such-and-such at night,' is accepted. Source pages p. 529

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on mursal hadith, now focusing on senders from after the third century. It presents three distinct issues. First, the acceptance of mursal from later generations: contrary to the earlier ruling of Isa ibn Aban, al-Karakhi held that such mursal is not accepted because the time after the three virtuous centuries is a time of corruption. However, the preferred view is that acceptance depends on whether the mursil is a recognized hadith scholar who can distinguish authentic from weak; if so, his mursal is accepted, otherwise not. Second, the passage examines a hadith transmitted both as musnad (by Isra'il ibn Yunus) and mursal (by Shu'ba). The generality (al-amma) holds that the musnad version prevails over the mursal, because the chain of transmission is complete. An opposing view analogizes musnad to ta'dil (validation) and mursal to jarh (impugnment), and argues that when jarh and ta'dil conflict, jarh prevails; thus the mursal would take precedence. But the text does not adopt this view. Third, the passage defines the 'internal' (batin) category of hadith, where the chain appears connected but the defect lies in the narrator's character or in contradiction to a stronger proof. The conditions for a narrator are intelligence, Islam, precision, and justice; loss of any of these renders the narration rejected. The example of the marriage hadith illustrates the preference for musnad over mursal when both exist.

Key Terms
الباطن (al-bāṭin): A type of hadith defect where the chain appears connected but the defect is in the narrator's conditions or contradiction to a stronger proof.
مرسل (mursal): A hadith where a Successor (or later narrator) omits the Companion and directly attributes to the Prophet.
مسند (musnad): A hadith with a complete chain of transmission going back to a Companion or the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for accepting mursal from after the three centuries?
A) The mursil must be a Companion.
B) The mursil must be a hadith scholar who distinguishes authentic from weak.
C) The mursil must be a Successor.
D) It is never accepted.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of later mursal in the Hanafi school depends on the sender's qualification as a hadith scholar, not on the era of transmission.

When Musnad and Mursal Conflict: Preferring the Full Chain
Resolves conflict between musnad and mursal using the marriage hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when a hadith is transmitted both as musnad and mursal, the musnad version prevails, and evaluate the qiyas argument that compares this to the principle of jarh wa ta'dil.

Core Idea
When a hadith is both musnad and mursal, the musnad prevails over the mursal.

A hadith may reach us through multiple chains: one complete (musnad) and one with a missing link (mursal). Which one should be given priority? The majority of scholars, including the Hanafis, hold that the musnad version takes precedence, because its full chain compensates for the deficiency of the mursal. This lesson examines that rule through the famous marriage hadith and considers an alternative view that analogizes the situation to conflicting narrator evaluations.

Guided Path
1
Define musnad and mursal
Identify the two types of hadith transmission: musnad has a continuous chain to the Prophet; mursal has a missing link (usually a tabi'i omitting the Companion).
Know that mursal is generally considered weaker, but not automatically rejected.
2
Identify the conflict
When the same hadith is reported both ways by different narrators, a conflict arises: should we accept the musnad (full) or the mursal (broken)?
In the example, Isra'il ibn Yunus gave a musnad version, Shu'ba a mursal version.
3
Apply the majority rule
The majority (al-amma) rule: the musnad prevails. The complete chain compensates for the disconnection in the other narration.
This is based on the principle that weakness due to interruption can be overcome by a stronger, connected chain.
4
Analyze the qiyas argument
Some scholars argue that mursal should prevail because musnad is like ta'dil (validation) and mursal like jarh (impugnment), and when they conflict, jarh takes precedence. Evaluate this analogy.
The majority rejects this qiyas because the musnad and mursal are not about narrator reliability but about chain completeness; the musnad provides direct evidence that the mursal lacks.
5
Recognize internal defects
Even if the chain is connected (musnad), internal defects may exist, such as the narrator lacking conditions (intelligence, Islam, precision, justice) or contradicting a stronger proof.
These defects can render even a musnad hadith unacceptable if demonstrated.

Source pages p. 529

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where a hadith is transmitted both with a full chain (musnad) and with a missing link (mursal). The example is the famous hadith 'No marriage except with a guardian'. Isra'il ibn Yunus transmitted it with a full chain (from Abu Ishaq from Abu Burda from Abu Musa from the Prophet), while Shu'ba transmitted it as mursal (from Abu Ishaq from Abu Musa from the Prophet, omitting Abu Burda). The ruling of the majority (al-amma) is that the musnad version prevails over the mursal, because the chain is complete and compensates for the deficiency in the other narration. An alternative view compares this to the principle of jarh wa ta'dil: musnad is like ta'dil (validating the chain) and mursal is like jarh (impugning it), and when they conflict, jarh takes precedence. However, this view is not adopted. The passage also reiterates that internal defects (batin) may exist even in a connected chain, such as violation of narrator conditions or contradiction to a stronger proof. The four narrator conditions are intelligence, Islam, precision, and justice. The passage concludes with references to the hadith in the major collections.

Key Terms
تعديل (taʿdīl): Validation of a narrator's reliability
جرح (jarḥ): Impugnment of a narrator's reliability
مسند (musnad): A hadith with a complete chain of narration reaching the Prophet
مرسل (mursal): A hadith where a tabi'i narrates directly from the Prophet, omitting the Companion

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of the majority (al-amma) when a hadith is narrated both as musnad and mursal?
A) The mursal prevails because it implies jarh.
B) Both are rejected as contradictory.
C) The musnad prevails over the mursal.
D) The mursal is preferred because it has fewer narrators.

Key Takeaway
When a hadith is transmitted both with a full chain (musnad) and with a missing link (mursal), the musnad is preferred because its complete chain compensates for the disconnection.

Acceptance of Mursal Hadith from Later Generations
Explains conditions for accepting Mursal from later narrators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for accepting a Mursal hadith from narrators after the second and third centuries, and distinguish the positions of al-Karkhi and the preferred view.

Core Idea
A Mursal from a later narrator is accepted if he is a reliable hadith scholar; otherwise rejected.

In previous lessons, we learned that Hanafis accept Mursal hadith from reliable narrators of the first three Islamic centuries. This lesson extends that analysis to later periods. You will see an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether the same reasoning applies, and the final position that allows acceptance only when the narrator is a recognized expert in hadith criticism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text opens by saying that a Mursal from a narrator after the second and third centuries is 'accepted' (maqbul) – but immediately qualifies it with a condition.
This is the default ruling from the perspective of the preferred opinion.
2
Understand the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Al-Karkhi argues that after the three centuries, the era is one of transgression (fisq), so such Mursal reports are rejected. The refutation (attributed to Ibn Aban) states that the cause (illah) for accepting early Mursal – reliability and precision – applies to all times.
The disagreement is about whether the cause is temporally limited.
3
Apply the condition of reliability
The text then gives the final criterion: if the later narrator is a hadith scholar (mumayyiz) who can distinguish sahih from da'if, his Mursal is accepted; otherwise not.
This balances the general cause with the reality of later narrators.
4
Handle mixed chains (Musnad vs Mursal)
When a hadith is reported as Mursal from one chain and Musnad from another, the Musnad prevails – as in the example of 'No marriage except with a guardian' narrated by Isra'il (Musnad) and Shu'bah (Mursal).
The connected chain compensates for the disconnection in the other.
5
Differentiate from hidden defects
The passage briefly distinguishes this case from 'hidden' defects in a hadith that arise from narrator conditions or contradiction to a higher proof; those are separate issues.
This reminds us that our discussion is about the outward disconnection (irsal), not internal criticism.

(al-Qamar) 'And was supported from one aspect' i.e., from another narrator, and from that Mursil narrator in another time. (al-Qamar) 'Accepted, etc.' because the deficiency of disconnection is compensated by connection. (al-Qamar) 'Musnad': Indeed Isra'il narrated from Abu Ishaq from Abu Barzah from Abu Musa, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'No marriage except with a guardian.' Thus in Jami' al-Tirmidhi. (al-Qamar) 'Shu'bah' narrated from Abu Ishaq from Abu Musa from the Prophet: 'No marriage except with a guardian' omitting Abu Barzah. Thus in Jami' al-Tirmidhi. (al-Qamar) 'So his Musnad prevails, etc.': So the Musnad is a proof then, unlike the Mursal. (al-Qamar) 'Conditions of the narrator': intelligence, Islam, precision, and reliability. (al-Qamar) 'Due to a deficiency' i.e., by the loss of one of the four mentioned conditions. (al-Qamar) It was transmitted by al-Tirmidhi no. 1101, chapter: 'There is no marriage except with a guardian', and Abu Dawud no. 2085, chapter: 'Concerning the guardian', and Ibn Majah no. 1881, chapter: 'No marriage except with a guardian', from Abu Musa.
Source pages p. 529

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul discussion on the acceptance of Mursal hadith (a hadith where the narrator omits the Companion and directly attributes to the Prophet). It begins by stating the general rule: Mursal from narrators after the second and third Islamic centuries is accepted. It then presents a disagreement: al-Karkhi rejects such Mursal reports because the later era is one of transgression (fisq), while the preferred Hanafi position (attributed to Ibn Aban) accepts them if the narrator is a reliable hadith scholar who can distinguish sahih from da'if. The rationale is that the cause for accepting Mursal from the early centuries—namely, the narrators' reliability and precision—applies to all centuries. The passage then addresses a special case: a hadith narrated as Mursal from one chain and as Musnad (with complete continuous chain) from another. The example given is the hadith 'No marriage except with a guardian,' narrated by Isra'il as Musnad and by Shu'bah as Mursal. The Hanafi position is that the Musnad version prevails because the deficiency of disconnection is compensated by the connected chain. Some argue that isnad is like ta'dil and irsal is like jarh, and jarh prevails, but the accepted view is that the Musnad is given preference. The passage also briefly mentions 'hidden' defects (batin) in a hadith, which can be due to missing conditions of the narrator or contradiction to a higher proof.

Key Terms
مرسل (Mursal): A hadith where a narrator omits the Companion and directly ascribes to the Prophet
مسند (Musnad): A hadith with a complete continuous chain of narrators reaching the Prophet
جرح وتعديل (Jarh wa Ta'dil): The discipline of impugning and declaring narrators reliable; jarh impugns, ta'dil declares reliability

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what condition makes a Mursal hadith from a narrator after the second and third centuries acceptable?
A) It must be supported by a Musnad chain
B) The narrator must be a hadith scholar who distinguishes sahih from da'if
C) It is always acceptable
D) It is never acceptable

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts Mursal hadith from later generations only if the narrator is a recognized hadith scholar, due to the ongoing applicability of the cause of reliability.

When a Hadith Contradicts the Qur'an: The Hanafi Approach
Usul rule with dispute examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for evaluating hadith that appear to contradict the Qur'an, distinguishing between qat'i and zanni texts and deriving the correct fiqh ruling.

Core Idea
A hadith is rejected only if it contradicts a definitive (qat'i) Qur'anic text; otherwise, the hadith may specify or interpret the Qur'an.

This passage addresses a critical usul principle: how to handle a hadith that seems to conflict with the Qur'an. The Hanafi school does not automatically reject such hadith; rather, the level of the Qur'anic text's indication (qat'i or zanni) determines whether the hadith can be accepted or must be set aside. Two classic examples—the obligation of Fatiha and the nullification of wudu by touching the penis—illustrate how this rule produces different rulings between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Qur'anic text and its level of indication
Determine whether the Qur'anic verse in question has a definitive meaning (qat'i al-dalala) or leaves room for interpretation (zanni).
The passage gives two examples: the command 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' (general, qat'i for Hanafis in this context) and the praise of men who purify themselves (also qat'i).
2
Identify the hadith and its transmission category
Classify the hadith as mutawatir, mashhur, or khabar al-wahid. Hanafis consider khabar al-wahid insufficient to specify or abrogate a qat'i text.
Both hadith here ('No prayer without Fatiha' and 'Whoever touches his penis') are ahad.
3
Assess the contradiction
If the hadith opposes a qat'i Qur'anic text, it is rejected (or interpreted away). If the Qur'anic text is zanni, the hadith can specify or modify it.
The hadith on Fatiha contradicts the general command; the touch-wudu hadith contradicts the praise of those who purify themselves.
4
Apply the Hanafi principle
Khabar al-wahid cannot add a restriction (takhsis) to a qat'i text. At most, the hadith indicates a recommended or obligatory (wajib) element.
For the Fatiha, the hadith makes it wajib, not fard. For touch-wudu, the hadith of Talq ibn Ali (no wudu) is preferred.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i rulings based on this usul rule.
Hanafi: prayer valid without Fatiha (but deficient); Shafi'i: prayer invalid. Hanafi: touching penis does not break wudu; Shafi'i: it does.

And the hadith of Busra may be interpreted as a metonymy for emitting something from it, as in al-Subh al-Sadiq. So praising a person for purification while in a state of hadath is reprehensible. It can be said that the praise is for istinja' due to removing real impurity, and the hadath here is incidental, so it does not harm the praise. Contemplate. (al-Qamar) Narrated by Bukhari no. 723...
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rule for mursal hadith: one sign of discontinuity is that the hadith contradicts the Qur'an. The commentator explains that contradiction only causes rejection if the Qur'anic text is definitive (qat'i al-dalala). If the Qur'anic text is not definitive (like general verses), a sound hadith can specify it. Two examples illustrate Hanafi positions: (1) Hadith requiring Fatiha vs. Qur'anic command to recite what is easy: Hanafis say the Qur'anic command is for absolute recitation, so the hadith only makes Fatiha obligatory (wajib) not fard. (2) Hadith requiring wudu from touching penis vs. Qur'anic praise of those who purify themselves with water: Hanafis prefer the hadith of Talq ibn Ali (no wudu) because it is from a male companion and stronger. The commentary also discusses the art of interpreting contradicting texts, such as considering the hadith on marriage with aunts as specifying the general Qur'anic permission.

Key Terms
الحديث المرسل (al-hadith al-mursal): A hadith whose chain is missing the Companion link; considered weak unless supported by other evidence.
خبر الآحاد (khabar al-wahid): A non-mass transmitted report; does not provide certainty and cannot abrogate or specify a definitive text.
قطعي الدلالة (qat'i al-dalala): A text with definitive meaning, leaving no room for interpretation or specification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is wajib (necessary) but not fard; any Quranic recitation suffices.
C) It is sunnah, not required.
D) It is only required in the first two rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
A hadith that contradicts a definitive Qur'anic text is rejected; otherwise, a sound hadith may specify or interpret a non-definitive text.

The Four Indicators of a Mursal Hadith
Defining mursal hadith and listing four indicators of disconnection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four indicators of a mursal hadith and explain why a khabar wahid is rejected in each case.

Core Idea
A mursal hadith is recognized by four signs: contradicting a definitive text, known sunnah, a well-known incident, or rejection by early imams.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar defines a mursal hadith not merely as an incomplete chain, but as any hadith that exhibits one of four specific indicators of disconnection. Understanding these indicators is crucial for evaluating the authenticity and applicability of khabar wahid in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first indicator: contradiction of a definitive text
When a khabar wahid contradicts a Quranic verse that is qat'i in both text and transmission (matn and sanad), the hadith is considered mursal and rejected. The Quran is definitive, while khabar wahid is speculative.
Example: the hadith of judgment with a witness and an oath contradicts the general Quranic principle that proof is on the claimant.
2
Identify the second indicator: contradiction of a well-known sunnah
If a khabar wahid contradicts a sunnah that is mutawatir or mashhur (widely known), the hadith is rejected because the well-known sunnah is definitive in transmission.
The well-known sunnah takes precedence over isolated reports.
3
Identify the third indicator: contradiction of a well-known incident witnessed by many
When a single narrator reports something that contradicts the common knowledge of a large group who were present, the report is considered unreliable. The example given is the audible basmala: thousands attended prayers, yet only Abu Huraira reported hearing it.
This indicates the report is likely a mistake or fabrication.
4
Identify the fourth indicator: rejection by early Companions or imams
If the early Companions, who are the foundations of the religion, debated a matter and did not rely on a particular hadith, this indicates the hadith is not authentic or is abrogated.
The example of zakat on a minor's wealth: the Companions did not act on the hadith 'Seek in the wealth of orphans that which is good, lest charity consumes it.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان الحديث المرسل
باب أقسام السنة أو السنة المعروفة كحديث القضاء بشاهد ويمين يخالف قوله عليا: "البينة على المدعي واليمين على من أنكر" وهو مشهور، أو الحادثة المشهورة كحديث الجهر بالتسمية في الصلاة الذي رواه أبو هريرة. فإن حادثة الصلاة مشهورة مستمرة كان يحضرها ألوف من الرجال ولم يسمع التسمية إلا أبو هريرة، وهذا شيء عجيب.
أي الحديث يعني أي عادة أن الصحابة تم إذ تكلموا فيما بينهم أو أعرض عنه الأئمة من الصدر الأول بالرأي ولم يلتفتوا إلى الحديث كان ذلك دليل انقطاعه مثل ما رُوي أن الصحابة اختلفوا فيما بينهم في وجوب الزكاة على الصبي بالرأي، ولم يلتفتوا إلى قوله عليه السلام: "ابتغوا في مال اليتامى خيرا كيلا تأكله الصدقة"، فعلم أنه غير ثابت أو مؤوّل بتأويل أي تجارة.
والسنة المعروفة متواترة كانت أو مشهورة (القمر) يخالف قوله إلخ فجعل في هذه القول جنس المدعى عليه وليس وراء الجنس شيء حتى يكون على المدعي. (القمر) كحديث الجهر بالتسمية إلخ قال الترمذي: إن الخلفاء الأربعة لا يجهرون ببسم الله في الصلاة. وفي رسائل "الأركان ما ملخصه: أن الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله قال بجهر البسملة في الجهرية بما عن نعيم المجمر قال صليت خلف أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه فقرأ بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم الحمد لله إلى آخر السورة وقال: ثم يقول إذا سلم: والذي نفسي بيده إني لأشبهكم صلاةً برسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، وقال في "فتح القدير": أخرجه النسائي وابن حبان وأبو خزيمة وبما عن ابن عباس قال: كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يفتتح صلاته بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم، رواه الترمذي، ولا يلزم من هذين الحديثين الجهر بالبسملة فافهم، وأما الأحاديث التي فيها جهر البسملة صريحًا، فلم يصح منها شيء وعليه المحققون من أهل الحديث، وقال الفيروز آبادي الشافعي: إنه ما يثبت في الجهر بالبسملة شيء. (القمر) ألوف من الرجال وكانوا طالبين لقول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وفعله. (القمر) من الصدر الأول: أي صدر الصحابة منه. (القمر)
وهو حديث ابن عباس لما قضى بيمين وشاهد أخرجه مسلم رقم 1712 باب القضاء باليمين والشاهد، وأبو داود رقم: 3608، باب القضاء باليمين والشاهد. لا نعرف حديث أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه في الجهر سوى ما أخرجه النسائي رقم 905، باب قراءة بسم الله الرحمن عن نعيم المجمر قال صليت وراء أبي هريرة، فقرأ بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم، ثم قرأ بأم القرآن إلخ. هذا اللفظ وروى الترمذي رقم: 641، باب ما جاء في زكاة مال اليتيم عن عمرو بن شعيب أن عن جده النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم خطب الناس فقال: ألا من ولّى يتيما له مال فليتجر فيه، ولا يتركه حتى تأكله الصدقة، قال الترمذي وإنما روى هذا الحديث من هذا الوجه، وفي إسناده مقال.
أن المراد بالصدقة النفقة عليه كما قال علي: نفقة المرء على نفسه صدقة. كان مردودًا منقطعًا أيضًا جواب إن أي يكون الخبر في كل من هذه المواضع الأربعة أي غير جائز العمل مردودًا كما في النوع الأول. Statement on the Mursal Hadith. Section on the divisions of the Sunnah, or the well-known Sunnah, like the hadith of judgment with a witness and an oath, which contradicts his saying: 'The burden of proof is on the claimant and the oath is on the one who denies.' This is well-known. Or the well-known incident like the hadith of audible pronouncement of the basmala in prayer narrated by Abu Huraira. For the incident of prayer is a continuous well-known event; thousands of men used to attend it, yet no one heard the basmala except Abu Huraira. This is something strange. Meaning the hadith, meaning that the Companions, when they discussed among themselves, or the early imams turned away from it by opinion and did not pay attention to the hadith, that was evidence of its disconnection, such as what is narrated that the Companions differed among themselves concerning the obligation of zakat on a minor by opinion, and they did not pay attention to his saying: 'Seek in the wealth of orphans that which is good, lest charity consumes it.' So it was known that it is not established or is interpreted. And the well-known Sunnah, whether mutawatir or mashhur. (Al-Qamar) It contradicts his saying etc. He made in this saying the genus of the defendant, and there is nothing beyond the genus so that it would be upon the claimant. (Al-Qamar) Like the hadith of audible basmala etc. Al-Tirmidhi said: The four caliphs do not pronounce 'Bismillah' audibly in prayer. And in 'Rasa'il al-Arkan' the summary is that Imam al-Shafi'i said that the basmala is said audibly in audible prayers based on Na'im al-Mujmir who said: I prayed behind Abu Huraira, and he recited 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim, al-Hamdulillah...' to the end of the surah, and he also said when he said the taslim: 'By Him in whose hand is my soul, I am the one whose prayer most resembles the prayer of the Messenger of Allah.' And it is said in 'Fath al-Qadir': Al-Nasa'i, Ibn Hibban, and Abu Khuzayma narrated it, and also from Ibn Abbas who said: The Prophet used to begin his prayer with 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim', narrated by al-Tirmidhi. But these two hadiths do not necessitate audible basmala, so understand. As for those hadiths that explicitly include audible basmala, none of them are authentic, and this is the position of the verifiers among the hadith scholars. Al-Fayruzabadi al-Shafi'i said: Nothing has been established regarding audible basmala. (Al-Qamar) Thousands of men were present and they were seekers of the saying and action of the Messenger of Allah. (Al-Qamar) From the early generation: i.e., the early generation of the Companions. (Al-Qamar). And it is the hadith of Ibn Abbas when he judged with an oath and a witness, narrated by Muslim no. 1712, chapter on judgment with oath and witness, and Abu Dawud no. 3608, chapter on judgment with oath and witness. We do not know any hadith from Abu Huraira regarding audible basmala except what is narrated by al-Nasa'i no. 905, chapter on reciting 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' from Na'im al-Mujmir who said: I prayed behind Abu Huraira, and he recited 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim', then he recited 'Umm al-Qur'an' etc. This wording. And al-Tirmidhi narrated no. 641, chapter on what has come regarding zakat on the wealth of an orphan from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his grandfather that the Prophet addressed the people and said: 'Behold, whoever is guardian of an orphan who has wealth, let him trade with it, and not leave it so that charity consumes it.' Al-Tirmidhi said: This hadith is only narrated from this chain, and there is some criticism in its chain. That the intended meaning of 'sadaqa' is the expenditure on him, as 'Ali said: 'A person's spending on himself is charity.' It is rejected and disconnected as well. The answer: that the report in each of these four situations is not permissible to act upon, rejected as in the first type. (Al-Qamar) Rejected: As for the first, because khabar wahid is speculative while the Book is definitive in text and chain, so it is not considered in opposition to it. As for the second, because the well-known Sunnah is definitive in transmission and is above khabar wahid, so it is given consideration. As for the third, because many people were present at that incident, and one of them contradicts them, and they were, with purity of belief, seekers of the saying and action of the Messenger of Allah, so their contradiction is not paid attention to due to suspicion. As for the fourth, because the Companions among them are the foundations in religion and are not accused of abandoning proof with evidence. So the Companions' abandonment of arguing with it when difference appeared among them is a clear indication that this hadith is a mistake from the narrator after them, or abrogated, or has another defect, so it is not acted upon. (Al-Qamar) As in the first type, which is when there is a defect in the transmitter. This is an explanation of the author's statement also. (Al-Qamar) The first: that the defect is in the transmitter. (Al-Muhashshi) In the explanation of the place, i.e., the incident in which it occurred. (Al-Qamar) The concessions etc., because the discussion is the discussion of the report of the one who has access and his companions, not the report of the common people. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage from Noor al-Anwar defines mursal hadith and provides four indicators that a hadith is disconnected (munqati'). The author begins by stating that a well-known Sunnah (like the hadith of judgment with a witness and an oath) may contradict a general statement, or a well-known incident (like the audible basmala) may have only one narrator among thousands, indicating that the hadith is not authentic. The four indicators are: (1) contradiction of a definitive text (like the Quran); (2) contradiction of a well-known Sunnah (mashhur or mutawatir); (3) a well-known incident where many witnesses contradict the solitary narration; (4) rejection by early Companions or imams, implying the hadith is either a mistake, abrogated, or has another defect. The passage also includes a lengthy discussion on the basmala debate, noting that the Hanafi position (based on practice of the four caliphs) differs from the Shafi'i view. The author concludes that a khabar wahid is rejected in these four cases. This is a core usul principle for evaluating hadith authenticity.

Key Terms
الحديث المرسل (al-hadith al-mursal): A hadith that is disconnected (munqati'), indicated by one of four signs: contradiction of a definitive text, a known sunnah, a well-known incident, or rejection by early imams.
السنة المعروفة (al-sunnah al-ma'rufah): A well-known sunnah, either mutawatir (widely transmitted) or mashhur (famous), that is definitive in transmission and takes precedence over khabar wahid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the four indicators that a hadith is mursal (disconnected)?
A) Contradicting a known sunnah
B) Being narrated by a single transmitter
C) Contradicting a definitive Quranic text
D) Being rejected by early imams or Companions

Key Takeaway
A khabar wahid is considered mursal (disconnected) and rejected if it contradicts a definitive text, a known sunnah, a well-known incident, or is abandoned by the early imams.

Classifying the Subject Matter of Khabar Wahid
Classification of subject matter for khabar wahid as hujjah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the subject matter of khabar wahid into rights of Allah and rights of people, and state the two opinions regarding the condition of number for its acceptance in rights of Allah.

Core Idea
Khabar wahid is accepted in rights of Allah; the dispute is whether a condition of number is required.

In this passage, the author explains the third division of khabar wahid: on what subject matter does it become a legal proof? He divides it into rights of Allah and rights of people, then focuses on rights of Allah. There are two views on whether a single narrator suffices or multiple narrators are needed. This lesson clarifies the classification and the two positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories
The passage divides the locus of khabar wahid into rights of Allah (huquq Allah) and rights of people (huquq al-ibad). Note the subcategories: rights of Allah include punishments and non-punishments; rights of people include pure obligation, no obligation, and mixed obligation.
This classification determines when khabar wahid is a hujjah.
2
Understand the scope of khabar wahid
The division applies to any khabar wahid, whether from the Prophet, his Companions, or common people, though the discussion focuses on the first two.
The text notes this is a famous overbreadth (musamahah) of the Salaf.
3
Learn the general rule for rights of Allah
Khabar wahid is hujjah in rights of Allah, including acts of worship, punishments, and mixed types (e.g., kaffarah, 'ushr, kharaj).
This is the majority Hanafi position.
4
Contrast the two views on condition of number
Some say no condition of number, citing Aisha's single report of the hadith 'When the two circumcised parts meet'. Others require multiple narrators, citing the Prophet's non-acceptance of Dhu al-Yadain's report until corroborated.
The passage presents both views without settling the tarjih here.
