Reliance on Written Notes (Khatt) in Hadith Narration
Explains the first type of rukhsah: reliance on written notes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi positions on the validity of relying on written notes for hadith narration and apply the condition of tadhakkur (remembering the hearing).

Core Idea
Relying on one’s own handwriting requires remembering the hearing; otherwise, according to Abu Hanifa, it is not a proof.

This lesson explores the first rukhsah in sunnah narration: using written notes. The scholars differed on whether a narrator may rely solely on his handwriting without recalling the hearing. We will analyze the views of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and others, and see the practical implications for witnesses and judges.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rukhsah
The passage begins by defining rukhsah as reliance on the written book. Note the condition: the narrator must look into it and remember his hearing and the study session at the time of performance.
2
Locate the Dispute
Abu Hanifa requires tadhakkur (remembering) for the notes to be a proof. The Sahibayn and al-Shafi'i allow it if the handwriting is recognized, even without memory. Note the additional positions of Anas and Muhammad.
Anas requires possession; Muhammad is more liberal.
3
Extend to Analogous Cases
The passage compares this to a witness testifying based on his handwriting in a document (sakk) and a judge acting on his record (sijill). This shows the practical application of the same principle in judicial settings.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
While the text presents Abu Hanifa's view as a precaution, it records the Sahibayn's view as a facilitation. The later commentary suggests reliance on the Sahibayn's position as a concession for ease.

باب أقسام السنة بيان التقسيم الرابع والرخصة أن يعتمد الكتاب، فإن نظر فيه وتذكر سماعه ومجلس درسه وما جرى فيه أي في وقت الأداء يكون حجة وإلا فلا أي إن لم يتذكر ذلك، فلا يكون حجة عند أبي حنيفة سواء أي السماع كان خطه أو خط غيره، وعندهما وعند الشافعي له : يجوز له الرواية ويجب العمل بها، وعند أنس له: يجوز الاعتماد على الخطّ إن كان في يده أو في يد أمينه، ولا يجوز إن كان في يد غيره؛ لأنه لا يؤمن عن التغيّر، وعن محمد يجوز العمل بالخط وإن الغير المعتمد عليه لم يكن في يده فذهب إليه رخصة تيسيرًا على الناس. والثالث طرف الأداء، والعزيمة فيه أن يؤدّي على الوجه الذي سمع بلفظه ومعناه أي الراوي والرخصة أن ينقله بمعناه ، أي بلفظ آخر يؤدي معنى الحديث، وهذا صحيح عند العامة؛ لأن الصحابة لهم كانوا يقولون : قال عليه كذا، أو قريبًا منه أو نحوا منه، وعند البعض: لا يجوز ذلك؛ لأنه عليه السلام مخصوص بجوامع الكلم؛ أي النقل بالمعنى يكون حجة لأنه إذا تذكره فكأنه حفظه إلى وقت الأداء. (القمر) فلا يكون حجة إلخ إذ لما لم يتذكر فلا عبرة فيه، والخط يكون مشابهاً بالخط، وهذا تضيق من الإمام احتياطاً في أمر السنن ولئلا يتساهلوا في الحفظ. (القمر) وعندهما إلخ وعلى هذا الخلاف رؤية الشاهد خطه في الصَّكَ، فيجوز الشهادة عند معرفة خطه وعدم تذكر ما فيه عند الأكثر خلافا له، ورؤية القاضي خطه في السجل، فلا يجوز عنده العمل دون الأكثر، وروي عن أبي يوسف الله الجواز في الرواية والسجل دون الصَّكَ. (السنبلي) يجوز له إلخ وهذا تيسير لئلا يذهب أكثر السنن، قال أبو يوسف يليه: إنه إن كان تحت يده يقبل للأمن عن التزوير وإن لم يكن في يده يقبل إذا كان خطا معروفا ولا يُخاف عليه التبديل عادةً، كذا في "التوضيح". (القمر) يجوز العمل إلخ : أي إذا علم يقينًا أنه خطه؛ لأن التغير غير متعارف.(القمر) وهذا : أي النقل بالمعنى صحيح عند العامة، وما نقل عن الإمام مالك لله أنه لا يجوز إقامة التاء القسميّة مقامَ الباء القسميّة فهو محمول على التشديد في أخذ العزيمة كذا قال تابعوه وأما القرآن فلا يجوز نقله بالمعنى بالاتفاق، وإن كان تفسير القرآن بجميع اللغات جائزاً، وقد مرّ هذه المسألة فتذكر. (القمر) بجوامع الكلم : أي الكلمات الجامعات للمعاني الكثيرة. (المحشي) أخرج مسلم رقم: ٥٢٣ ، كتاب المساجد ومواضع الصلاة عن أبي هريرة الله أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: فضّلْتُ الأنبياء بست أُعطِيتُ جوامع الكلم، ونُصرت بالرعب، وأحلت لي الغنائم، وجعلت لي الأرض طهورا و مسجدا، وأرسلتُ إلى الخلق كافة، ختم بي النبيون.

بيان التقسيم الرابع باب أقسام السنة فلا يؤمن في النقل بالمعنى من الزيادة والنقصان والحق هو التفصيل الذي ذكره المصنف عليه بقوله : فإن كان محكمًا لا يحتمل غيره يجوز نقله بالمعنى لمن له بصر في وجوه اللغة؛ إذ لا يشتبه معناه عليه بحيث يحتمل الزيادة والنقصان. وإن كان ظاهرًا يحتمل غيره بأن يكون عامًا يحتمل التخصيص أو حقيقةً يحتمل المجاز، فلا يجوز نقله بالمعنى إلا للفقيه المجتهد؛ لأنه يقف على المراد، فلا يقع الخلل في نقله بمعناه مثلاً قوله: "من بدل دينه فاقتلوه" كلمة "من" عامة تخص منها المرأة، فإن نقله ناقل ويقول: "كل من بدل دينه فاقتلوه" يشمل المرأة أيضًا، فيقع الخلل في الأحكام. وما كان من جوامع الكلم بأن كان لفظًا وجيزا تحته معانٍ جَمّة كقوله عليه: "الغُرم بالغُنم"، من الكلم الجامعة هو التفصيل إلخ ثم اعلم أن هذا التفصيل في جواز النقل بالمعنى وعدم جوازه، أما المنقول بالمعنى الذي رواه راقٍ فقيها كان أو غيره، فهو حجة، ويُحمل على أن أصل الحديث كان من جنس الحديث الذي يجوز نقله بالمعنى، فإن الناقل بالمعنى عدل، فلو لم يكن الحديث من ذلك الجنس لما ينقله ذلك العدل بالمعنى، كذا قيل. (القمر) محكما أي في الدلالة على المعنى (القمر) لا يحتمل إلخ إيماء إلى أن المراد بالمحكم ههنا ما لا يحتمل غيره، أي يكون متضح المعنى لا يشتبه معناه وليس المراد ما لا يحتمل النسخ في ذاته على ما هو المصطلح سابقا. (القمر) بصر : أي علمٌ لا البصر الظاهري. (القمر) ظاهراً أي في الدلالة على المعنى (القمر) يشمل إلخ لأن الكل نص في العموم. (القمر) جَمّة من الجموم، وهو الكثرة (القمر) الغرم بالغنم والغرم بضم الغين المعجمة الضمانُ والمؤنة، والغنم بضم الغين المعجمة النفعُ، والمعنى أن الضمان بعوض المنفعة، فمن له الغُنم فعليه الغُرم كمن غصب شيئًا واستهلكه فصار له الغنم فعليه غرمه والراهن فإن له منفعة المرهون فعليه غرمه ونفقته، وقس عليه صورًاً كثيرة، في "المشكاة" عن سعيد بن المسيب له أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: "لا يغلق الراهن الرهن من صاحبه الذي رهنه له غنمه، وعليه غُرمه" رواه الشافعي له مرسلاً. (القمر) أخرجه البخاري رقم: ۲۸٥٤ ، باب لا يُعذِّب بعذاب الله، وأبو داود رقم: ٤٣٥۱، باب الحكم فيمن ارتد، عن ابن عباس ها. ** هذا مشهور بين الفقهاء في "المشكاة" عن سعيد بن المسيب بالله مرفوعا: "لا يغلق الراهن الرهن من صاحبه الذي رهنه له غنمه وعليه غُرمه. رواه الشافعي له مرسلاً. [إشراق الأبصار : ۲۲]
Chapter: Categories of Sunnah. Explanation of the fourth division: Rukhsah is to rely on the written book. So if he looks into it and remembers his hearing and the study session and what occurred therein at the time of performance, it is a valid proof; otherwise not. That is, if he does not remember that, then it is not a valid proof according to Abu Hanifa, regardless whether the hearing was in his own handwriting or another's. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and according to al-Shafi'i, he is allowed to narrate and must act upon it. According to Anas, he may rely on the handwriting if it is in his hand or in the hand of his trustee, but not if in another's hand, because it is not safe from alteration. And from Muhammad: he may act upon the handwriting even if it is not in his hand—he held this as a concession for the ease of people. The third aspect is the mode of performance: 'Azimah is that he performs according to the manner he heard, with its wording and meaning. And rukhsah is that he transmits it by meaning, i.e., with another wording that conveys the meaning of the hadith. This is correct according to the generality of scholars because the Companions used to say: 'The Prophet said such and such, or something close to it, or similar to it.' According to some, it is not allowed because he (peace be upon him) was distinguished by Jawami' al-Kalim...
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the fourth division of sunnah regarding 'azimah and rukhsah in narration. It first discusses rukhsah in relying on written notes: Abu Hanifa requires that the narrator recall the hearing at the time of narration; otherwise the notes are not a proof. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and al-Shafi'i allow it as long as the handwriting is recognized. Anas allows it only if the notes are in the narrator's possession or a trustee's. Muhammad (al-Shaybani) further allows it even if not in hand, as a concession. This difference is compared to a witness testifying based on his handwriting in a document (sakk) and a judge relying on his record (sijill). The second part discusses narrating by meaning: it is permissible generally because the Companions did so, but it requires caution. The passage provides a detailed criterion: if the hadith is muhkam (clear, not open to interpretation), even a non-expert may transmit by meaning; if it is zahir (ambiguous, e.g., general terms or metaphorical), only a faqih mujtahid may do so, to avoid error. Example: the hadith 'Man baddala dīnahu faqtulūhu' uses 'man' (whoever) which is general, but the ruling excludes women; a lay narrator might use 'kullu man' (everyone who) which would wrongly include women. The hadith 'al-ghurm bi al-ghunm' is given as an example of Jawami' al-Kalim (concise speech). The passage also confirms that the Quran cannot be transmitted by meaning by consensus, and that a reliable narrator's transmission by meaning is accepted assuming the original was of a type that allows it.

Key Terms
العزيمة (al-‘azīmah): The strict obligation to perform the narration exactly as heard; here used in contrast to rukhsah.
الرخصة (al-rukhṣah): A concession allowing reliance on written notes or narrating by meaning, for ease.
التذكر (al-tadhakkur): Remembering the hearing and study session at the time of performance.
الخط (al-khatt): Handwriting, particularly of the narrator himself.
الصَّكّ (al-sakk): A legal document or contract.
السجل (al-sijill): A court record or register.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is required for a written note to be a valid proof in hadith narration?
A) The handwriting must be recognized.
B) The narrator must remember the hearing at the time of performance.
C) The note must be in the narrator's hand.
D) The note must be witnessed.

Key Takeaway
The condition of tadhakkur (remembering the hearing) is crucial for Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn allow reliance on recognized handwriting as a concession.

Al-Sunnah as Source

Narrating Hadith by Meaning (Naql bi al-Ma‘na): Conditions and Qualifications
Explains the second type of rukhsah: narrating by meaning and the conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between muhkam and zahir texts for the purpose of narrating by meaning, and identify who is qualified to do so.

Core Idea
Narrating by meaning is permissible only when the text is clear (muhkam) or, if ambiguous (zahir), only by a mujtahid faqih.

This lesson covers the second rukhsah: transmitting the meaning of a hadith rather than its exact words. The passage explains that this is generally permitted, but with a crucial distinction: simple texts can be transmitted by anyone, while ambiguous texts require a jurist capable of ijtihad to avoid error. We will analyze the example of the hadith 'Man baddala dīnahu faqtulūhu' and the concise hadith 'al-ghurm bi al-ghunm'.

Guided Path
1
State the Two Modes
The passage defines 'azimah as performing the narration exactly as heard, and rukhsah as transmitting by meaning. Note that rukhsah is generally accepted.
2
Identify the Basis of Permissibility
The Companions used to say 'the Prophet said such and such, or something close to it.' This practice is the primary evidence for permissibility.
3
Recognize the Objection
Some scholars object based on the Prophet's gift of Jawami' al-Kalim (concise speech). They argue that his exact words are precise and should not be altered.
4
Apply the Distinction: Muhkam vs. Zahir
The passage provides a detailed criterion: if the hadith is muhkam (clear, not open to interpretation), anyone with knowledge of Arabic may transmit by meaning. If it is zahir (ambiguous, e.g., general or metaphorical), only a mujtahid faqih may do so. This is the key usul rule.
Example: the hadith 'Man baddala dīnahu faqtulūhu' uses the general word 'man'; a lay narrator might include women erroneously.
5
Consider Jawami' al-Kalim
The passage gives the hadith 'al-ghurm bi al-ghunm' as an example of concise speech. Such texts, despite their brevity, fall under the zahir category and require a mujtahid to transmit by meaning correctly.

Chapter: Categories of Sunnah. Explanation of the fourth division: Rukhsah is to rely on the written book. So if he looks into it and remembers his hearing and the study session and what occurred therein at the time of performance, it is a valid proof; otherwise not. That is, if he does not remember that, then it is not a valid proof according to Abu Hanifa, regardless whether the hearing was in his own handwriting or another's. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and according to al-Shafi'i, he is allowed to narrate and must act upon it. According to Anas, he may rely on the handwriting if it is in his hand or in the hand of his trustee, but not if in another's hand, because it is not safe from alteration. And from Muhammad: he may act upon the handwriting even if it is not in his hand—he held this as a concession for the ease of people. The third aspect is the mode of performance: 'Azimah is that he performs according to the manner he heard, with its wording and meaning. And rukhsah is that he transmits it by meaning, i.e., with another wording that conveys the meaning of the hadith. This is correct according to the generality of scholars because the Companions used to say: 'The Prophet said such and such, or something close to it, or similar to it.' According to some, it is not allowed because he (peace be upon him) was distinguished by Jawami' al-Kalim...
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the fourth division of sunnah regarding 'azimah and rukhsah in narration. It first discusses rukhsah in relying on written notes: Abu Hanifa requires that the narrator recall the hearing at the time of narration; otherwise the notes are not a proof. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and al-Shafi'i allow it as long as the handwriting is recognized. Anas allows it only if the notes are in the narrator's possession or a trustee's. Muhammad (al-Shaybani) further allows it even if not in hand, as a concession. This difference is compared to a witness testifying based on his handwriting in a document (sakk) and a judge relying on his record (sijill). The second part discusses narrating by meaning: it is permissible generally because the Companions did so, but it requires caution. The passage provides a detailed criterion: if the hadith is muhkam (clear, not open to interpretation), even a non-expert may transmit by meaning; if it is zahir (ambiguous, e.g., general terms or metaphorical), only a faqih mujtahid may do so, to avoid error. Example: the hadith 'Man baddala dīnahu faqtulūhu' uses 'man' (whoever) which is general, but the ruling excludes women; a lay narrator might use 'kullu man' (everyone who) which would wrongly include women. The hadith 'al-ghurm bi al-ghunm' is given as an example of Jawami' al-Kalim (concise speech). The passage also confirms that the Quran cannot be transmitted by meaning by consensus, and that a reliable narrator's transmission by meaning is accepted assuming the original was of a type that allows it.

Key Terms
النقل بالمعنى (al-naql bi al-ma‘nā): Transmitting the meaning of a hadith using one's own words instead of the exact wording.
محكم (muḥkam): A clear, unambiguous text that does not admit alternative interpretations.
ظاهر (ẓāhir): A text that is apparent but susceptible to alternative interpretations (e.g., general, metaphorical).
جوامع الكلم (jawāmi‘ al-kalim): Concise speech that encompasses many meanings in few words, a quality specific to Prophet Muhammad.
الفقيه المجتهد (al-faqīh al-mujtahid): A jurist capable of ijtihad, i.e., independent legal reasoning, who can correctly identify the intended meaning of ambiguous texts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is allowed to narrate a hadith by meaning if the hadith is ẓāhir (apparent but ambiguous)?
A) Any Muslim who understands Arabic
B) Any faqīh mujtahid only
C) Only the Sahābah
D) Only Imām Abu Hanīfah

Key Takeaway
Narrating by meaning is a concession, but ambiguous texts require a mujtahid to ensure accurate transmission.

Al-Sunnah as Source

Narrating Hadith by Meaning: Muhkam and Zahir Texts
Classification of sunna texts for riwayat bi al-ma'na: muhkam and zahir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between muhkam and zahir texts and apply the Hanafi rule on who may narrate each by meaning.

Core Idea
Muhkam texts are clear; any linguist can paraphrase them. Zahir texts require a mujtahid to avoid error.

The classification of prophetic texts into categories like muhkam and zahir is crucial for determining the permissibility of narrating hadith by meaning. The Hanafi school holds that not every text can be safely paraphrased; the clarity of the text determines who is qualified to do so. This lesson unpacks the first part of the classification from Noor al-Anwaar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two textual categories
Locate where the author defines muhkam (unequivocal) and zahir (apparent). Note that muhkam admits no other meaning, while zahir admits another possibility (e.g., general or figurative).
2
Determine the permissibility for each
For muhkam, any person with 'basar fi wujuh al-lugha' (insight into language) may narrate it by meaning. For zahir, only a faqih mujtahid may do so. Understand why: a mujtahid can ascertain the intended meaning and avoid error.
3
Analyze the example: 'man baddala dinahu faqtuluhu'
The word 'man' is general (amm) and includes women, but the hadith actually excludes women by specification (takhsis). If a non-mujtahid narrates it by meaning, they might say 'everyone who changes his religion' and thereby include women, causing error.
This illustrates the danger of paraphrasing a zahir text without proper ijtihad.
4
Reflect on the underlying principle
The permissibility hinges on whether the text's dalala is clear enough to avoid distortion. Muhkam is safe; zahir requires expertise. This classification protects the integrity of the sunna.

باب أقسام السنة

والخراج بالضمان والعجماء جُبَارٌ . **
أو المشكل أو المشترك أو المجمل لا يجوز نقله بالمعنى للكل أي لا للمجتهد ولا لغيره، أما في جوامع الكلم فلأنه عليه لما كان مخصوصا به فلا يقدر أحد على نقله، وأما في المشكل والمشترك؛ فلأنه إنما ينقله بتأويل مخصوص لا يكون حجة على غيره، وأما في المجمل فلعدم الوقوف على معناه بدون الاستفسار من المجمل.
والخراج بالضمان: رواه في شرح السنة عن عائشة أنها قالت: قال رسول الله : الخراج بالضمان. قيل: إن الخراج بالفتح ما خرج من شيء، فخراج الشجرة ثمرتها، وخراج الحيوان دَرّه ونسله، والباء في قوله" "بالضمان" للسبية، والمعنى أن الخراج مستحق لأجل الضمان أي ما يدخل في ضمان الشخص فخراجه له كالمشتري المردود بالعيب؛ لأنه لو هلك قبل الردّ هلك من مال المشتري، فهو داخل في ضمان المشتري، فخراجه وغلته قبل الرد بالعيب يطيب له.
وههنا بحث، وهو أنه ليس تحت هذا القول معان كثيرة بل تحته معنى واحد، فليس هو من جوامع الكلم.(القمر) والعَجْماء جُبار إلخ والعجماء بفتح العين المهملة وسكون الجيم بالمدّ مؤنث أعْجَم، وهو الذي لا يقدر على الكلام، والمراد ههنا البهيمة، والجبار بضم الجيم وتخفيف الباء الموحدة الهدرُ ، أي لا شيء فيه، والمعنى أنه إذا أتلفت البهيمة شيئًا أو جرحت جرحًا ولم يكن معها قائد ولا سائق، وكان نهارًا فلا ضمان، وإن كان معها أحد فهو ضامن الحصول الإتلاف حينئذ بتقصيره، أو كذا إذا كان ليلاً لقصور المالك عن ربطها، فإن العادة أن الدابة تُربط ليلاً وتُسرح نهارًا . (القمر) أو المجمل وكذا المتشابه فإنه فوق المجمل في الخفاء.(القمر)

(القمر) على نقله : أي على نقل المعنى بجوامع الكلم. (القمر) بتأويل مخصوص : أي لتعيين معنى المشترك والمجمل. جبار وفي الركاز الخمس.
العجماء
Explanation of the fourth division: Chapter on types of Sunnah. One cannot be safe from addition and omission when narrating by meaning. The truth is the detailed explanation mentioned by the author in his statement: 'If it is muhkam (unequivocal) that does not admit of any other meaning, it is permissible to narrate it by meaning for one who has insight into the aspects of language; because its meaning is not ambiguous to him such that it would admit of addition or omission. And if it is zahir (apparent) that admits of another meaning, such as being general (amm) that admits of specification, or a literal expression that admits of figurative interpretation, then it is not permissible to narrate it by meaning except for a faqih mujtahid; because he can ascertain the intended meaning, so no error occurs in his narration by meaning. For example, his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him.' The word 'whoever' (man) is general, from which women are excluded. If a narrator relates it and says: 'Everyone who changes his religion, kill him,' that would include women as well, causing error in rulings. And whatever is from jawami' al-kalim (comprehensive expressions) such as a concise phrase containing many meanings, like his statement (peace be upon him): 'al-ghurm bil-ghunm' (liability corresponds with profit). ... Then know that this detailed discussion pertains to the permissibility or impermissibility of narration by meaning. As for what is narrated by meaning by a reliable narrator, whether he is a jurist or not, it is considered proof (hujja), and it is assumed that the original hadith was of the type that permits narration by meaning. So it is said: ... (al-Qamar comments) ... The explanation of al-ghurm bil-ghunm: al-ghurm (with damma on ghayn) means liability and expense, and al-ghunm (with damma on ghayn) means benefit. The meaning is that liability is in return for benefit: whoever has the benefit must bear the liability. ... (Hadith: 'The lien does not free the pledge from its owner; he who pledges it has its benefit and bears its liability.') ... Or (the hadith is) mushkil, mushtarak, or mujmal: it is not permissible to narrate it by meaning for anyone—neither for the mujtahid nor others. As for jawami' al-kalim, because he (the Prophet) was uniquely endowed with them and no one can reproduce them. As for mushkil and mushtarak, because one would only narrate them with a particular interpretation that is not binding on others. As for mujmal, because one cannot ascertain its meaning without asking the one who uttered it. ... (Then discussion of 'al-kharaj bi al-daman' and 'al-ajma' jubar' with hadith references.)
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of the types of prophetic texts (sunnah) regarding the permissibility of narrating them by meaning (riwayat bi al-ma'na). The author (the commentator al-Qamar) explains the matn's division: muhkam (unequivocal) hadith can be narrated by meaning by anyone knowledgeable in language, because its meaning is clear and unambiguous. Zahir (apparent) hadith, which can admit other interpretations (like general terms or figurative meanings), can only be narrated by meaning by a mujtahid faqih who can grasp the intended meaning and avoid error. The example given is the hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him'—the word 'man' is general but excludes women by specification; a non-mujtahid might incorrectly include them. Jawami' al-kalim (comprehensive expressions) are so concise and pregnant with meaning that no one can render them by paraphrase; hence they cannot be narrated by meaning at all. Similarly, mushkil (ambiguous), mushtarak (homonym), and mujmal (unclear) hadith cannot be narrated by meaning because they require special interpretation or clarification. However, if a Companion learned the intended meaning from the Prophet himself, he may then narrate it by meaning. The passage also discusses specific examples like 'al-ghurm bil-ghunm' (liability follows profit) and 'al-ajma' jubar' (animals causing damage are without liability), explaining their meanings and providing hadith references. The commentary follows the Hanafi usul framework, emphasizing the importance of textual clarity and the qualifications required for accurate transmission. Note that the distinction between muhkam and zahir here is based on clarity of meaning, not on abrogation as in other contexts.

Key Terms
محكم (muhkam): A text that is unequivocal in its meaning and does not admit of any other interpretation; in this passage, it refers to clarity in dalala (indication), not immunity from abrogation.
ظاهر (zahir): A text that is apparent in meaning but admits of another possible interpretation (e.g., general or literal).
جوامع الكلم (jawami' al-kalim): Comprehensive expressions; concise prophetic phrases that contain many meanings in few words (e.g., 'al-ghurm bil-ghunm').
مشكل (mushkil): A text that is ambiguous and requires external interpretation to resolve its difficulty.
مشترك (mushtarak): A homonym; a word with multiple possible meanings requiring contextual or external specification.
مجمل (mujmal): An ambiguous or summary text whose meaning cannot be known without clarification from the speaker.
الغرم بالغرم (al-ghurm bil-ghunm): A legal maxim meaning 'liability corresponds with profit' or 'one who benefits must bear the risk'.
العجماء جبار (al-'ajma'u jubar): A hadith stating that injuries caused by an animal (without a handler) are without liability (hollowed).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who may narrate a muhkam hadith by meaning?
A) Any Muslim
B) Anyone with linguistic insight
C) Only a mujtahid faqih
D) Only a Companion

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of narrating hadith by meaning depends on the text's clarity: muhkam texts are safe for anyone, zahir texts require a mujtahid.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate

Narrating Hadith by Meaning: Jawami' al-Kalim, Mushkil, Mushtarak, Mujmal
Classification of sunna texts for riwayat bi al-ma'na: prohibited categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify texts that are jawami' al-kalim, mushkil, mushtarak, or mujmal, and state why they cannot be narrated by meaning by anyone.

Core Idea
Jawami' al-kalim are inimitable; mushkil/mushtarak require tafsir; mujmal needs clarification. None can be safely paraphrased.

In this lesson, we continue the classification of hadith texts for narration by meaning. Beyond muhkam and zahir, there are categories that are entirely off-limits for paraphrase: the comprehensive expressions (jawami' al-kalim) unique to the Prophet, ambiguous texts (mushkil and mushtarak), and summary statements (mujmal). Understanding why is essential for preserving the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four prohibited categories
Locate in the text: jawami' al-kalim, mushkil, mushtarak, mujmal. Note that they are grouped together as texts that cannot be narrated by meaning by anyone, regardless of their level of ijtihad.
2
Understand why jawami' al-kalim are excluded
These are concise phrases packed with meanings (e.g., 'al-ghurm bil-ghunm'). The Prophet was uniquely gifted with them; no one can reproduce their exact import through paraphrase.
The commentary notes that some scholars debated whether 'al-ghurm bil-ghunm' is really jawami' al-kalim, since it has only one meaning.
3
Understand why mushkil and mushtarak are excluded
A mushkil text is ambiguous; a mushtarak is a homonym with multiple meanings. Narrating by meaning would impose the narrator's own interpretation, which may not be authoritative. Only the original wording preserves the intended meaning.
If a Companion learned the intended meaning from the Prophet, he could narrate it by meaning, as the text mentions.
4
Understand why mujmal is excluded
A mujmal text is too vague to be understood without explanation from the speaker. Paraphrase would be guesswork. The only safe transmission is verbatim.
Mujmal is even more ambiguous than mushkil; it requires the speaker’s own clarification.
5
Reflect on the assumption about reliable narrators
The text adds that if a trustworthy narrator transmits a hadith by meaning, we assume the original was of a permissible type. This protects the authority of transmitted proofs.

بصر : أي علمٌ لا البصر الظاهري. (القمر) ظاهراً أي في الدلالة على المعنى (القمر)
يشمل إلخ لأن الكل نص في العموم. (القمر) جَمّة من الجموم، وهو الكثرة (القمر) الغرم بالغنم والغرم بضم الغين المعجمة الضمانُ والمؤنة، والغنم بضم الغين المعجمة النفعُ، والمعنى أن الضمان بعوض المنفعة، فمن له الغُنم فعليه الغُرم كمن غصب شيئًا واستهلكه فصار له الغنم فعليه غرمه والراهن فإن له منفعة المرهون فعليه غرمه ونفقته، وقس عليه صورًاً كثيرة، في "المشكاة" عن سعيد بن المسيب له أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: "لا يغلق الراهن الرهن من صاحبه الذي رهنه له غنمه، وعليه غُرمه" رواه الشافعي له مرسلاً. (القمر) أخرجه البخاري رقم: ۲۸٥٤ ، باب لا يُعذِّب بعذاب الله، وأبو داود رقم: ٤٣٥۱، باب الحكم فيمن ارتد، عن ابن عباس ها.
** هذا مشهور بين الفقهاء في "المشكاة" عن سعيد بن المسيب بالله مرفوعا: "لا يغلق الراهن الرهن من صاحبه الذي رهنه له غنمه وعليه غُرمه. رواه الشافعي له مرسلاً. [إشراق الأبصار : ۲۲]

باب أقسام السنة
٥٤٣
بيان التقسيم الرابع
والخراج بالضمان والعجماء جُبَارٌ . **
أو المشكل أو المشترك أو المجمل لا يجوز نقله بالمعنى للكل أي لا للمجتهد ولا لغيره، أما في جوامع الكلم فلأنه عليه لما كان مخصوصا به فلا يقدر أحد على نقله، وأما في المشكل والمشترك؛ فلأنه إنما ينقله بتأويل مخصوص لا يكون حجة على غيره، وأما في المجمل فلعدم الوقوف على معناه بدون الاستفسار من المجمل.
والخراج بالضمان: رواه في شرح السنة عن عائشة أنها قالت: قال رسول الله : الخراج بالضمان. قيل: إن الخراج بالفتح ما خرج من شيء، فخراج الشجرة ثمرتها، وخراج الحيوان دَرّه ونسله، والباء في قوله" "بالضمان" للسبية، والمعنى أن الخراج مستحق لأجل الضمان أي ما يدخل في ضمان الشخص فخراجه له كالمشتري المردود بالعيب؛ لأنه لو هلك قبل الردّ هلك من مال المشتري، فهو داخل في ضمان المشتري، فخراجه وغلته قبل الرد بالعيب يطيب له.
وههنا بحث، وهو أنه ليس تحت هذا القول معان كثيرة بل تحته معنى واحد، فليس هو من جوامع الكلم.(القمر) والعَجْماء جُبار إلخ والعجماء بفتح العين المهملة وسكون الجيم بالمدّ مؤنث أعْجَم، وهو الذي لا يقدر على الكلام، والمراد ههنا البهيمة، والجبار بضم الجيم وتخفيف الباء الموحدة الهدرُ ، أي لا شيء فيه، والمعنى أنه إذا أتلفت البهيمة شيئًا أو جرحت جرحًا ولم يكن معها قائد ولا سائق، وكان نهارًا فلا ضمان، وإن كان معها أحد فهو ضامن الحصول الإتلاف حينئذ بتقصيره، أو كذا إذا كان ليلاً لقصور المالك عن ربطها، فإن العادة أن الدابة تُربط ليلاً وتُسرح نهارًا . (القمر) أو المجمل وكذا المتشابه فإنه فوق المجمل في الخفاء.(القمر)
لا يجوز إلخ إلا إذا علم الصحابي الا الله المعنى المراد من المشكل أو المشترك أو المجمل بالاستفسار من النبي فحينئذٍ يجوز له النقل بالمعنى؛ فإنه حينئذٍ صار مُتضح المعنى في حكم المحكم. (القمر) على نقله : أي على نقل المعنى بجوامع الكلم. (القمر) بتأويل مخصوص : أي لتعيين معنى المشترك والمجمل. (القمر) أخرجه الترمذي رقم: ۱۲۸۵، باب ما جاء فيمن يشتري العبد ويستغله، ثم يجد فيه عيبا، قال الترمذي: هذا حديث حسن صحيح، والنسائي رقم: ٤٤٩٠ ، باب الخراج بالضمان وأبو داود رقم: ٣٥٠۸، باب فيمن اشترى عبدا فاستعمله ثم وجد به عيبا وابن ماجه رقم ٢٢٤٣ باب الخراج بالضمان، وابن حبان في "صحيحه" ، رقم: ٤٩٢٧ ، باب خيار العيب، وأحمد في "مسنده" رقم: ٢٤٢٧، عن عائشة لها . ** أخرج البخاري رقم ٦٥١٤ ، باب المعدن جبار والبئر جبار. ومسلم رقم: ۱۷۱۰، باب جرح والمعدن والبئر جبار، عن أبي هريرة له أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : العجماء وجرحها جبار، والبئر جبار، والمعدن
جبار وفي الركاز الخمس.
العجماء
Explanation of the fourth division: Chapter on types of Sunnah. One cannot be safe from addition and omission when narrating by meaning. The truth is the detailed explanation mentioned by the author in his statement: 'If it is muhkam (unequivocal) that does not admit of any other meaning, it is permissible to narrate it by meaning for one who has insight into the aspects of language; because its meaning is not ambiguous to him such that it would admit of addition or omission. And if it is zahir (apparent) that admits of another meaning, such as being general (amm) that admits of specification, or a literal expression that admits of figurative interpretation, then it is not permissible to narrate it by meaning except for a faqih mujtahid; because he can ascertain the intended meaning, so no error occurs in his narration by meaning. For example, his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him.' The word 'whoever' (man) is general, from which women are excluded. If a narrator relates it and says: 'Everyone who changes his religion, kill him,' that would include women as well, causing error in rulings. And whatever is from jawami' al-kalim (comprehensive expressions) such as a concise phrase containing many meanings, like his statement (peace be upon him): 'al-ghurm bil-ghunm' (liability corresponds with profit). ... Then know that this detailed discussion pertains to the permissibility or impermissibility of narration by meaning. As for what is narrated by meaning by a reliable narrator, whether he is a jurist or not, it is considered proof (hujja), and it is assumed that the original hadith was of the type that permits narration by meaning. So it is said: ... (al-Qamar comments) ... The explanation of al-ghurm bil-ghunm: al-ghurm (with damma on ghayn) means liability and expense, and al-ghunm (with damma on ghayn) means benefit. The meaning is that liability is in return for benefit: whoever has the benefit must bear the liability. ... (Hadith: 'The lien does not free the pledge from its owner; he who pledges it has its benefit and bears its liability.') ... Or (the hadith is) mushkil, mushtarak, or mujmal: it is not permissible to narrate it by meaning for anyone—neither for the mujtahid nor others. As for jawami' al-kalim, because he (the Prophet) was uniquely endowed with them and no one can reproduce them. As for mushkil and mushtarak, because one would only narrate them with a particular interpretation that is not binding on others. As for mujmal, because one cannot ascertain its meaning without asking the one who uttered it. ... (Then discussion of 'al-kharaj bi al-daman' and 'al-ajma' jubar' with hadith references.)
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of the types of prophetic texts (sunnah) regarding the permissibility of narrating them by meaning (riwayat bi al-ma'na). The author (the commentator al-Qamar) explains the matn's division: muhkam (unequivocal) hadith can be narrated by meaning by anyone knowledgeable in language, because its meaning is clear and unambiguous. Zahir (apparent) hadith, which can admit other interpretations (like general terms or figurative meanings), can only be narrated by meaning by a mujtahid faqih who can grasp the intended meaning and avoid error. The example given is the hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him'—the word 'man' is general but excludes women by specification; a non-mujtahid might incorrectly include them. Jawami' al-kalim (comprehensive expressions) are so concise and pregnant with meaning that no one can render them by paraphrase; hence they cannot be narrated by meaning at all. Similarly, mushkil (ambiguous), mushtarak (homonym), and mujmal (unclear) hadith cannot be narrated by meaning because they require special interpretation or clarification. However, if a Companion learned the intended meaning from the Prophet himself, he may then narrate it by meaning. The passage also discusses specific examples like 'al-ghurm bil-ghunm' (liability follows profit) and 'al-ajma' jubar' (animals causing damage are without liability), explaining their meanings and providing hadith references. The commentary follows the Hanafi usul framework, emphasizing the importance of textual clarity and the qualifications required for accurate transmission. Note that the distinction between muhkam and zahir here is based on clarity of meaning, not on abrogation as in other contexts.

Key Terms
محكم (muhkam): A text that is unequivocal in its meaning and does not admit of any other interpretation; in this passage, it refers to clarity in dalala (indication), not immunity from abrogation.
ظاهر (zahir): A text that is apparent in meaning but admits of another possible interpretation (e.g., general or literal).
جوامع الكلم (jawami' al-kalim): Comprehensive expressions; concise prophetic phrases that contain many meanings in few words (e.g., 'al-ghurm bil-ghunm').
مشكل (mushkil): A text that is ambiguous and requires external interpretation to resolve its difficulty.
مشترك (mushtarak): A homonym; a word with multiple possible meanings requiring contextual or external specification.
مجمل (mujmal): An ambiguous or summary text whose meaning cannot be known without clarification from the speaker.
الغرم بالغرم (al-ghurm bil-ghunm): A legal maxim meaning 'liability corresponds with profit' or 'one who benefits must bear the risk'.
العجماء جبار (al-'ajma'u jubar): A hadith stating that injuries caused by an animal (without a handler) are without liability (hollowed).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why cannot a mushkil hadith be narrated by meaning?
A) Because it is too long to paraphrase
B) Because any interpretation would be the narrator's own and not authoritative
C) Because it contains unknown words
D) Because it is a homonym

Key Takeaway
Jawami' al-kalim, mushkil, mushtarak, and mujmal texts must be transmitted verbatim; only original wording preserves their intended meanings.

Liability Hadiths and Transmitting Ambiguous Texts
Explains two liability hadiths and transmission rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two hadiths on liability, explain their legal maxims, and apply the rule that ambiguous texts cannot be transmitted by meaning unless clarified by the Prophet.

Core Idea
Profit accompanies liability; an animal's daytime harm without attendant is irrecoverable.

In this lesson, we examine two foundational hadiths that establish liability rules: 'Profit is due with liability' and 'The dumb animal is irrecoverable.' We also learn a key principle for transmitting ambiguous texts: narrators cannot alter the wording of prophetic concise expressions or ambiguous hadiths unless the meaning was explicitly clarified. Understanding these rules is essential for proper istidlal (proof derivation).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its textual basis
The passage presents two hadiths as primary sources for liability. Identify each hadith and the legal maxim derived from it (e.g., al-kharaj bi al-daman means profit is a consequence of bearing risk).
Both hadiths are ahad (solitary) but have strong application.
2
Analyze the linguistic elements
Examine the key words: 'al-kharaj' (profit), 'al-daman' (liability), 'al-ajma' (dumb animal), 'jubar' (irrecoverable). Note the grammatical function of the ba in 'bi al-daman' indicating causality.
The commentator emphasizes the ba as sababiyyah (causative).
3
Understand the transmission rule
The passage explains that ambiguous texts (mushtarak, mujmal) cannot be transmitted by meaning because they require specific interpretation. However, if a Companion knew the intended meaning by asking the Prophet, transmission by meaning becomes permissible.
Jawami' al-kalim (concise expressions) are uniquely prophetic and cannot be paraphrased.
4
Apply to fiqh scenarios
The first hadith is applied: a buyer who uses a defective item before return keeps the profit because he bore the liability. The second: an animal causing damage during daytime without an attendant incurs no liability; nighttime or presence of attendant shifts liability.
These applications are based on the maxims derived from the hadiths.

Chapter on Divisions of Sunnah 543. Explanation of the Fourth Division: 'Profit is for liability' and 'The dumb animal is irrecoverable.' ** Or the ambiguous, or the common, or the summary: it is not permissible to transmit it by meaning for everyone, i.e., neither for the mujtahid nor for others. As for concise expressions (jawami' al-kalim), because he (the Prophet) was uniquely given them, no one can transmit them. As for the ambiguous and common, because he transmits them with a specific interpretation that is not binding on others. As for the summary, because its meaning cannot be known without asking the one who summarized. 'Profit is for liability': narrated in Sharh al-Sunnah from Aisha that she said: The Messenger of God said: 'Profit is for liability.' It is said: 'al-kharaj' (profit) with fath is what comes out of something; the profit of a tree is its fruit, and the profit of an animal is its milk and offspring. The ba in the statement 'for liability' is for causality. The meaning is that profit is entitled due to liability; i.e., whatever comes under a person's liability, its profit is for him, like the buyer of a defective item who returns it; because if it perishes before return, it perishes from the buyer's wealth, so it is under his liability, and its profit and yield before return due to defect are permissible for him. Here there is a discussion: that this statement does not have many meanings, but only one meaning, so it is not among concise expressions. (al-Qamar) And 'the dumb animal is irrecoverable etc.' 'al-jama' with fatha on the important 'ayn, sukun on the jim, and madd, feminine of a'jam, which is one who cannot speak. What is meant here is the animal. 'al-jubar' with damm on the jim and tashdid on the ba, meaning wasted, i.e., nothing is due. The meaning is that if an animal destroys something or causes a wound, and there is no attendant or driver with it, and it is daytime, then no liability. But if someone is with it, then he is liable for the destruction due to his negligence. Similarly, if it is night, due to the owner's failure to tie it, for the custom is that the animal is tied at night and let loose during the day. (al-Qamar) Or the summary, and likewise the ambiguous, which is more obscure than the summary. (al-Qamar) 'It is not permissible etc.' except if the Companion knows the intended meaning of the ambiguous, common, or summary by asking the Prophet; then it is permissible for him to transmit by meaning, for then it has become clear in meaning, in the ruling of the clear. (al-Qamar) 'upon its transmission': i.e., upon transmission of meaning by concise expressions. (al-Qamar) 'with a specific interpretation': i.e., to specify the meaning of the common and summary. (al-Qamar) It was narrated by al-Tirmidhi no. 1285, chapter on one who buys a slave and uses him then finds a defect: al-Tirmidhi said: this hadith is hasan sahih; al-Nasa'i no. 4490; Abu Dawud no. 3508; Ibn Majah no. 2243; Ibn Hibban in his Sahih no. 4927; Ahmad in his Musnad no. 2427 from Aisha. ** Al-Bukhari no. 6514, chapter on the mine is irrecoverable and the well is irrecoverable; Muslim no. 1710, chapter on wound, mine, well are irrecoverable, from Abu Huraira that the Messenger of God said: 'The dumb animal and its wound are irrecoverable, the well is irrecoverable, the mine is irrecoverable, and in buried treasure one-fifth.' The dumb animal.
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the fourth division of Sunnah within a larger usul work (likely Noor al-Anwar). It explains two key hadiths: 'Profit is for liability' (al-kharaj bi al-daman) and 'The dumb animal is irrecoverable' (al-ajma' jubar), along with a rule about transmitting ambiguous hadiths (mushtarak, mujmal) by meaning. The commentator first states that ambiguous texts cannot be transmitted by meaning by anyone, because concise expressions (jawami' al-kalim) are uniquely prophetic, ambiguous texts require a specific interpretation not binding on others, and summaries cannot be understood without clarification. He then explains the hadith 'Profit is for liability': the term kharaj means revenue or yield; the letter ba indicates causality, so profit is due because of liability. An example: a buyer who uses a purchased item and later discovers a defect keeps the profit from his use because the item was under his liability while in his possession. The commentator notes that this hadith is not among jawami' al-kalim because it has only one meaning. Next, he explains 'The dumb animal is irrecoverable': the animal's unintentional harm during daytime without an attendant incurs no liability; if an attendant is present, he is liable due to negligence; at night, the owner is liable for failing to tie it. Finally, he adds an exception: if a Companion knew the intended meaning by asking the Prophet, he could transmit the ambiguous text by meaning, as it then becomes clear. The passage concludes with references to hadith collections for both reports.

Key Terms
الخراج بالضمان (al-kharāj bi al-ḍamān): A legal maxim meaning that any profit or yield from an item under one's liability belongs to the person bearing that liability.
العجماء جبار (al-ʿajmāʾ jubār): An animal causing damage without an attendant in daytime is irrecoverable, i.e., no liability.
جوامع الكلم (jawāmiʿ al-kalim): Concise expressions given to the Prophet that convey many meanings in few words.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, why is 'al-ajma' jubar' not an absolute rule of no liability?
A) Because the Prophet meant only certain animals.
B) Because it applies only when there is no attendant and it is daytime.
C) Because it is abrogated by another hadith.
D) Because it is ambiguous and unclear.

Key Takeaway
Two key hadiths establish that profit follows liability and that animal harm is excused only under specific conditions, and ambiguous texts require verbatim transmission unless meaning was clarified by the Prophet.

Narrator's Refrainment or Contrary Action as a Defect in Hadith
Explaining how narrator's refrainment or contrary action impugns hadith authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a narrator's refrainment or contrary action impugns a hadith when the hadith is apparent (zahir) and distinguish this from other forms of hadith criticism.

Core Idea
A narrator's own practice can reveal a hadith's abrogation or limited application, impugning its authority if the hadith is well-known.

This passage introduces a critical principle in Hanafi hadith criticism: a narrator's failure to act on a hadith he himself transmitted can undermine its legal authority. The principle applies only when the hadith is 'apparent' (zahir) and its meaning would not be hidden from the narrator. Using examples from the Companions Ibn 'Umar and 'Umar, the author illustrates how such contrary practice indicates abrogation or discretionary policy rather than a fixed ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
State the defect (ta'n) introduced: the narrator's refrainment from acting upon a hadith or acting contrary to it.
This is distinct from other defects like chain discontinuity or narrator weakness.
2
Specify the condition
The rule applies only when the hadith is 'apparent' (zahir) and not likely hidden from the narrator. Determine what 'zahir' means in this context.
The Arabic phrase is 'إذا كان الحديث ظاهرا لا يحتمل الخفاء'.
3
Examine the examples
Analyze the examples of Ibn 'Umar (raising hands in prayer) and 'Umar (exile for zina). How does each support the rule?
Ibn 'Umar's abandonment shows abrogation; 'Umar's policy shows discretion not fixed punishment.
4
Contrast with opposing view
Identify the Shafi'i position: al-Shafi'i takes the hadith literally and does not impugn it based on 'Umar's action. Understand the practical difference.
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether exile is part of the hadd for zina.
5
Apply the rule
Given a hypothetical scenario with a narrator's contradictory action, evaluate whether the hadith remains authoritative using the condition from the passage.
Ensure the hadith is clearly apparent and the narrator's action is later and intentional.

والامتناع أي امتناع الراوي عن العمل به مثل العمل بخلافه أي بخلاف ما رواه، فيخرج عن الحجية. وقد صح عن مجاهد أنه قال: صحبت ابن عمر عشر سنين فلم أره رفع يديه إلا في تكبيرة الافتتاح، فترك العمل به دليل على انتساخه. وعمل الصحابي بخلافه يوجب الطعن إذا كان الحديث ظاهرا لا يحتمل الخفاء. ومثاله ما روى عبادة بن الصامت أنه قال: "البكر بالبكر جلد مائة وتغريب عام" فيتمسك به الشافعي، ونحن نقول: إن عمر نفى رجلا فارتد ولحق بالروم فحلف أن لا ينفي أحدا أبدا، فلو كان النفي حدا لما حلف على تركه، فعلم أن النفي منه كان سياسة لا حدا.
And refrainment, meaning the narrator's refrainment from acting upon it, is like acting contrary to it, i.e., contrary to what he narrated, so it removes it from authority. And it is authentically reported from Mujahid that he said: I accompanied Ibn 'Umar for ten years and did not see him raise his hands except at the opening takbir; so abandoning acting upon it is evidence of its abrogation. And the Companion's acting contrary to it obligates impugnment if the hadith is apparent and not likely to be hidden. An example is what 'Ubadah ibn al-Samit narrated: 'The virgin [punishment] is a hundred lashes and exile for a year,' and al-Shafi'i adheres to it. We [Hanafis] say: 'Umar exiled a man who apostatized and joined the Byzantines, then swore never to exile anyone again; if exile were a penal punishment, he would not have sworn to abandon it, so it is known that his exile was policy, not punishment.'
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage discusses a rule in hadith criticism: a narrator's failure to act on a hadith he narrates, or acting against it, can be a defect that removes the hadith's authority (hujjiyya). The key condition is that the hadith must be apparent (zahir) and not likely to have been hidden from the narrator. The text gives two examples: (1) The raising of hands in prayer – Ibn 'Umar narrated the practice but later abandoned it, and Mujahid observed that Ibn 'Umar only raised his hands at the opening takbir. The Hanafis see this abandonment as evidence that the practice was abrogated. (2) The hadith from 'Ubadah ibn al-Samit about the virgin's punishment including exile. Al-Shafi'i takes exile as part of the hadd penalty, but the Hanafis point to 'Umar's practice: he once exiled an apostate but later swore never to exile again, showing that his exile was a political discretionary measure (siyasa), not a fixed punishment. Thus, the narrator's (here, a Sahaba's) action contrary to a hadith can impugn it if the hadith was well-known and not obscure. The Hanafi position distinguishes between cases where the companion's action indicates abrogation or interpretation versus cases where the hadith was not widely known.

Key Terms
امتناع (imtināʿ): The narrator's refrainment from acting upon a hadith he narrated; this can be a defect that removes the hadith's authority.
حديث ظاهر (ḥadīth ẓāhir): A hadith whose meaning is clear and widely known, such that its obscurity from the companion is unlikely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what condition must be met for a companion's acting contrary to a hadith to impugn it?
A) The hadith must be narrated by multiple chains
B) The hadith must be apparent (zahir) and not likely hidden from the companion
C) The companion must be known for piety
D) The hadith must be mutawatir

Key Takeaway
A narrator's own practice can reveal a hadith's abrogation or limited scope, but only when the hadith is apparent (zahir) and not obscure.

Conditions for Accepting Jarh Against a Narrator
States when vague jarh is accepted or rejected

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for accepting jarh (criticism) against a narrator according to the Hanafi school and apply them to distinguish vague from detailed criticism.

Core Idea
Vague jarh is rejected; only detailed, agreed-upon, and unbiased criticism disqualifies a narrator.

In evaluating the reliability of hadith narrators, not all criticism carries the same weight. The Hanafi school maintains a strong default presumption of reliability for every Muslim, especially the early generations. Therefore, vague accusations without details are insufficient. This lesson unpacks the conditions that must be met for jarh to be accepted, including the requirement that the critic be sincere and free from bias, and that the criticism be specific and universally recognized.

Guided Path
1
Define jarh mubham and jarh mufassar
Understand the two categories of criticism: vague (jarh mubham) which lacks specific reasons, and detailed (jarh mufassar) which specifies the defect.
2
State the default principle
Recognize the Hanafi principle that reliability (adala) is the original attribute of every Muslim, especially the early generation.
This default can only be overcome by clear evidence.
3
Identify the conditions for accepting jarh
List the conditions: (a) jarh must be mufassar (detailed), (b) agreed upon by all scholars, (c) from a critic known for sincerity (nasihiyya) and free from bias.
Biased critics, like those who exaggerate, are not considered.
4
Analyze the rationale
Explain why vague or biased jarh is not accepted: the critic may be mistaken or have personal bias, making the criticism unreliable.
The example of Abu Musa not acting on a hadith does not constitute jarh.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a statement about a narrator (e.g., 'he is munkar'), determine whether it qualifies as acceptable jarh according to the Hanafi conditions.
Remember that even 'munkar' may be considered mufassar in some contexts (Bahr al-Ulum).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

From one known, etc., i.e., being free from self-interest and sincere for the religion. Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for accepting jarh (criticism) against a narrator in hadith. The author clarifies that vague jarh (jarh mubham) from hadith imams does not disqualify a narrator according to the Hanafi school. The default is that every Muslim is reliable, especially the early generations. Therefore, a hadith is not rejected based on vague criticism because the critic might believe something to be a defect that is not actually one. Jarh must be detailed (mufassar) and agreed upon by all, not disputed. Furthermore, the critic must be known for sincerity and free from bias. Biased critics, such as those who exaggerate or have a strict tendency, are not considered. Examples include those who make disliked things forbidden and recommended things obligatory. The passage also distinguishes between vague jarh (e.g., 'this hadith is munkar') and explanatory jarh (e.g., 'he is a liar'), with the latter being acceptable. The Hanafi position is that only jarh that is explicit and universally agreed upon is accepted. This principle is based on the default attribute of reliability in Muslims and the possibility that the critic may be mistaken or biased.

Key Terms
جرح مبهم (jarh mubham): Vague criticism without specifying the reason
جرح مفسر (jarh mufassar): Detailed criticism specifying the reason
النصحية (al-nasihiyya): Sincerity and freedom from bias in criticism

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) When it is detailed, agreed upon, and from a sincere critic.

Key Takeaway
Only detailed, agreed-upon, and unbiased criticism can overcome the default reliability of a narrator.

Definition and Types of Tadlis (Concealment)
Narrator concealment definitions and Hanafi position

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tadlis, distinguish it from talbis and irsal, and apply the Hanafi ruling on narrator concealment.

Core Idea
Tadlis (concealing the chain) is only jarh if done deceptively; Hanafis accept the mursal, so its illusion is harmless.

This lesson examines the hadith terminology of tadlis (concealment) as defined by Hanafi usul scholars. You will learn the linguistic root, the technical definition in hadith science, and the subdivisions including talbis and irsal. The Hanafi perspective holds that the illusion of irsal caused by tadlis is not a defect because irsal itself is accepted from trustworthy narrators.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic and technical definitions of tadlis
Tadlis in language means concealing a defect in merchandise. In hadith terminology, it is concealing details of the chain, e.g., saying 'from so-and-so' instead of specifying direct hearing.
2
Distinguish tadlis from talbis and irsal
Talbis is a subtype where the teacher is mentioned by an obscure kunya or attribute. Irsal is dropping the Companion entirely; tadlis drops a contemporary between two contemporaries.
The illusion of irsal from tadlis is not harmful according to Hanafis because irsal itself is not a defect.
3
Understand the conditions for tadlis
Tadlis only occurs when the dropped narrator is a contemporary of both the narrator and the one he allegedly heard from. Otherwise it is inqita' or irsal.
If the dropped narrator is non-contemporary, it is not tadlis.
4
Note the Hanafi ruling on the illusion of irsal
The Hanafi school does not consider the illusion of irsal caused by tadlis as a defect because the reality of irsal is not jarh. Therefore, a hadith with tadlis that merely suggests irsal is still acceptable if the narrator is trustworthy.
5
Recognize the permissibility of tadlis for brevity vs. prohibition for deception
Tadlis done to avoid tedious detail is permissible. If done to obscure a weak narrator or for deceptive purposes, it is disliked or forbidden depending on the intent.
The disagreement is only over tadlis al-isnad (concealment of the chain), not over dropping for brevity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And know that tadlis is only realized when he narrates from a contemporary, and the narrator he dropped in between is also a contemporary, such that the listener understands that he heard from this mentioned narrator, but in reality he did not hear from him. And if he drops the intermediaries between him and a non-contemporary, it is not called tadlis, rather it is inqita' or irsal. And sometimes the narrator drops the one he narrated from because the one dropped is considered trustworthy by him but not by others, so if he mentioned him, research into his validation would occur, thus it is disliked (makruh), and according to some it is forbidden. And sometimes he drops to avoid lengthy boredom, and this type of tadlis is not disputed in its permissibility; the dispute is only about the first type as the author explained. And they do not criticize him because a person may criticize falsely. Al-Hasan al-Basri and al-Kalbi; the first is trustworthy, the second is not trustworthy, as said by al-Qari. Commentary
This passage defines tadlis (concealment) and discusses its types and rulings. Tadlis linguistically means hiding a defect in merchandise. In hadith terminology, it is concealing the details of the chain, such as saying 'so-and-so from so-and-so' without specifying whether it is direct or through an intermediary. This creates an illusion of irsal (a broken chain), which is not itself a defect, so the illusion is even less harmful. The passage then describes talbis, a subtype of tadlis where the narrator mentions his teacher by a kunya or attribute to obscure his identity, so that critics do not attack him. An example is Sufyan al-Thawri saying 'Abu Sa'id' which applies to both al-Hasan al-Basri (trustworthy) and al-Kalbi (untrustworthy). The author clarifies that tadlis only occurs when the narrator drops a contemporary between himself and another contemporary, giving the impression that he heard directly. If the dropped person is not contemporary, it is called inqita' (disconnection) or irsal. Reasons for dropping include avoiding research into the reliability of a narrator (disliked or forbidden) or avoiding tedious details (permissible). The first type (tadlis al-isnad) is the subject of scholarly dispute, while the second type (dropping for brevity) is acceptable. The passage also notes that 'akhbarana' implies direct meeting, whereas 'an' can be ambiguous. The Hanafi position is that the illusion of irsal does not harm because actual irsal is not a defect according to them.

Key Terms
التدليس (al-tadlis): Concealing details in the isnad to create a false impression of direct hearing
التلبيس (al-talbis): A type of tadlis where the narrator mentions his teacher by an obscure name or kunya
الإرسال (al-irsal): Narrating from a successor (tabi'i) without mentioning the companion

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does tadlis (concealment) occur?
A) When a narrator drops a non-contemporary intermediary.
B) When a narrator drops a contemporary intermediary, giving the impression of direct hearing.
C) When a narrator uses the word 'akhbarana'.
D) When a narrator mentions his teacher by his full name.

Key Takeaway
Tadlis is only a defect when done to deceive; the Hanafi school does not reject a hadith merely due to the illusion of irsal.

Hanafi Criteria for Valid Defects in Narrators
Explains which criticisms of narrators are not valid defects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which criticisms of hadith narrators are not considered valid defects according to Hanafi usul, and apply the principle that only actual lying or sin discredits a narrator.

Core Idea
Suspicion does not disqualify: only actual jarh (lie/sin) is a true defect.

Hadith criticism often involves scrutinizing narrators. However, not every criticism actually harms the narrator's credibility. This passage from a Hanafi usul work systematically lists several common criticisms—such as suspicion of irsal, tadlis, youth, joking, and many fiqh questions—and explains why none of these are valid grounds to reject a narrator. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly evaluating hadith and avoiding the rejection of authentic reports based on misunderstandings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the criticism
For each alleged defect mentioned in the text, note the exact accusation (e.g., 'he uses 'an' in isnad', 'he is young', 'he jokes', 'he has many fiqh questions').
The passage lists multiple criticisms; each is addressed separately.
2
Determine the Hanafi position
State whether the criticism is considered a valid defect (jarh) or not according to the Hanafi school as presented in the text.
Most are rejected; only actual lying, sin, or gross negligence are accepted.
3
Analyze the reasoning
Explain the Hanafi rationale for why the criticism is not a defect. For example, irsal itself is not a defect, so its suspicion is even less; youth is acceptable if the narrator is precise; joking is allowed unless it involves falsehood.
The text uses qiyas and the Prophet's example as proof.
4
Recognize exceptions and nuances
Note that some forms of tadlis (with intent to deceive) may be makruh or haram, but still not a full defect affecting acceptance. Also, the Hanafis accept mursal from reliable narrators.
The distinction between tadlis of contemporaries vs. non-contemporaries is crucial.

بيان طعن يلحق الحديث باب أقسام السنة حدثنا فلان قال: أخبرنا فلان إلخ، لأن غايته أنه يوهم شبهة الإرسال، وحقيقة الإرسال ليس بجرح فشبهته أولى. والتلبيس، وهو أن يذكر الراوي شيخه بالكنية لا بالاسم، أو يذكره بصفة غير مشهورة حتى لا يعرف فيما بين الناس، ولا يطعنوا عليه كما يقول سفيان الثوري له: حدثني أبو سعيد، وهو كنية للحسن البصري والكلبي جميعًا، ووقع في بعض النسخ ههنا قوله: والإرسال تبعًا لفخر الإسلام له، وهو ليس بطعن أيضًا على ما قدّمنا. وركض الدابة كما يطعن بعض الأقران على محمد بن الحسن يطلبه بذلك، وهو أمر مشروع قال أخبرنا إلخ لأن قوله: "أخبرنا" تصريح في اللقاء والرواية عنه، بخلاف قوله عن فلان؛ فإنه صادق في صورة رواية عنه بالواسطة أيضا كما هو صادق في صورة عدم الواسطة والحديث في الصورة الأولى يكون مرسلاً، ففي كلمة "عن" شبهة الإرسال حاصلة، ولا الحرج في هذه الشبهة؛ لأن حقيقتها لا تضر عندنا، فالشبهة بالأولى لا تضرّ واعلم أن التدليس إنّما يتحقق إذا روى عن المعاصر، وكان الراوي الذي أسقطه فيما بين معاصرًا له أيضًا تكلّم بحيث يفهم أنه سمع من هذا الراوي الذي ذكره، وفي الحقيقة لم يسمع منه، ولو أسقط الوسائط فيما بينه وبين غير معاصره لا يسمّى تدليسا، بل هو انقطاع أو إرسال، وقد يسقط الراوي المروي عنه من أجل أن المسقط عنده من الثقات وعند غيره لا، فلو ذكره وقع البحث في توثيقه، فهو مكروه، وعند البعض حرام، وقد يسقط لدفع الطول المُمِلَّ، وهذا القسم من التدليس لا كلام في صحته وإنما الكلام في القسم الأول كما بينه المصنف له. (السنبلي) لأن إلخ : دليل لقول المصنف له: لا يقبل إلخ. (القمر) يوهم شبهة إلخ بأن يترك راويًا بينهما (القمر) أو يذكره إلخ معطوف على قوله: يذكر. (القمر) حتى لا يعرف إلخ بيان لثمرة التلبيس نوع من التدليس عند أهل الحديث، ذلك ويسمى عندهم تدليس الشيوخ، والنوع الأول تدليس الإسناد كذا قال ابن الملك. (القمر) ولا يطعنوا عليه لأن الرجل قد يطعن بالباطل. (القمر) للحسن البصري والكلبي والأول ثقة، والثاني غير ثقة كذا قال العلي القاري له. (القمر) على ما قدمنا أي في التقسيم الثاني مما يختص بالسنن . (القمر) ما قدمنا إلخ من أنه إن كان من الصحابي له فمقبول بالإجماع، ومن القرن الثاني والثالث كذلك عندنا وإرسال من دون هؤلاء كذلك أي مقبول عند خلافا لابن أبان إلخ. (السنبلي وركض الدابة: أي الحَثّ على العدو في السير. (القمر) وهو أمر مشروع أي إذا كان بلا شرط أو بشرط المال من جانب واحد لا من الجانبين فإنه قمار. (القمر) الكرخي من أصحاب الجهاد لا يصلح جرحًا، والمزاح وهو لا يصلح جرحًا؛ لأن النبي عليه كان يمازح كثيرًا، ولكن لا يقول إلّا حقا كما قال لعجوزة "إنّ العجائز لا تدخل الجنة" فلما ولت تبكي، قال: أخبروها بقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّا أَنْشَأْنَاهُنَّ إِنْشَاءً فَجَعَلْنَاهُنَّ أَبْكَارًا عُرُبا (الواقعة : 35- 37) وحداثة السنّ أي صغره كما يقول سفيان الثوري لأبي حنيفة له: ما يقول هذا الشاب الحديث السنّ عندي؛ وذلك لأن كثيرًا من الصحابة منهم كانوا يروون في حداثة سنّهم بشرط الإتقان عند التحمّل والعدالة عند الأداء. وعدم الاعتياد بالرواية فإن أبا بكر الله لم يكن معتادًا بالرواية مع أن أحدا لم يُعادله في الضبط والإتقان. واستكثار مسائل الفقه، كما طعن بذلك بعض المحدثين على أصحابنا، فإن ذلك دليل قوة الذهن وجودته، وقد كان أبو يوسف الله يحفظ عشرين ألف حديث من الموضوع فما ظنك بالصحيح؟ ولما فرغ المصنف له عن بيان أقسام السنة شرع في بحث المعارضة المشتركة بين الكتاب والسنة تبعًا لفخر الإسلام له، وكان ينبغي أن يدرجهما في بحث معارضة العقليات في باب الترجيح كما فعله صاحب "التوضيح"، فقال: لا يقول إلا حقا إلخ يعني اشترط في صحة المزاح أن لا يقول كذبًا ولا يقصد به إهانة المسلم؛ لأن هذين الأمرين سببان المعصية وفاعلهما خارج عن العدالة. (القمر) بشرط الإتقان والحداثة في السنّ لا تُضادّ العدالة ولا الضبط. (القمر) على أصحابنا: كأبي يوسف له حيث قال: إنه اشتغل بالفقه وصرف همّته إليه وهذا يوجب القصور في ضبط الحديث وإتقانه. (القمر) فإن ذلك إلخ : أي استكثار مسائل الفقه دليل قوة الذهن، فيستدل به على حسن الضبط والإتقان.(القمر) وكان ينبغي إلخ لأنه ذكر في هذا الفصل معارضة القياسين أيضًا. (القمر) أخرج رزين والبغوي في "شرح السنة" عن أنس الله أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال العجوز : إنه لا تدخل الجنة عجوز، فقالت وما لهن وكانت تقرأ القرآن؟ فقال لها : أما تقرئين القرآن: ﴿إِنَّا أَنشَأْنَاهُنَّ إِنْشَاءُ (الواقعة:35) الآية. [إشراق الأبصار 23]
Statement of defects that affect the hadith. Chapter on divisions of the Sunnah: So-and-so narrated to us, he said: So-and-so informed us, etc., because its ultimate effect is that it suggests the suspicion of irsal (mursal), and the reality of irsal is not a defect, so its suspicion is even less. And talbis (concealment) is that the narrator mentions his shaykh by his kunya rather than his name, or mentions him by an unfamiliar description so that he is not known among people and they do not criticize him, as Sufyan al-Thawri said: Abu Sa'eed narrated to me – and it is a kunya for both al-Hasan al-Basri and al-Kalbi. And in some copies here occurs his saying: 'and irsal', following Fakhr al-Islam, and it is also not a defect, as we have stated. And urging the mount (rakd ad-dabba), as some peers criticized Muhammad ibn al-Hasan by seeking that from him—and it is a lawful matter... (continues) ... And youthfulness of age (hadath as-sinn), i.e., young age, as Sufyan al-Thawri said about Abu Hanifa: 'What does this young man say?' – young in age according to me; and that is because many of the Companions narrated in their youth, provided they had precision at the time of reception and integrity at the time of delivery. And lack of familiarity with narration, for Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) was not accustomed to narration, yet no one equaled him in accuracy and precision. And having many fiqh issues, as some hadith scholars criticized our companions for that—but that is evidence of strength and quality of intellect. Abu Yusuf (may Allah be pleased with him) memorized twenty thousand fabricated hadith, so what do you think of authentic ones? And when the author finished with the divisions of the Sunnah, he began the discussion of conflict common to the Book and the Sunnah, following Fakhr al-Islam...
Source pages p. 550

Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi usul work, explaining various types of criticisms (ta'n) leveled against hadith narrators and why they are not considered valid defects (jarh) according to the Hanafi school. The commentator expands on the base text, addressing each alleged defect systematically. He begins by clarifying that the use of 'an (from) in isnad only suggests irsal but is not a defect, unlike 'akhbarana which indicates direct hearing. He then discusses tadlis (concealment), distinguishing between acceptable and unacceptable forms: dropping a contemporary narrator to create ambiguity is problematic, but dropping non-contemporary narrators is not tadlis but irsal or inqita'. He notes that tadlis may be done for valid reasons (e.g., to avoid questioning the narrator's reliability) but is makruh or haram in some views. Next, he addresses 'talbis' (confusing names/kunyas) as a form of tadlis, then 'rakd ad-dabba' (urging a mount) which was used to criticize Muhammad ibn al-Hasan but is lawful. He then discusses 'muzah' (joking) as not a defect, citing the Prophet's own jesting with an old woman, but clarifying that lying or insulting in jest is prohibited. 'Hadath as-sinn' (youth) is not a defect as many Companions narrated in their youth with precision. 'Lack of familiarity with narration' is not a defect, as Abu Bakr was not a frequent narrator yet unmatched in accuracy. Finally, 'istikthar masa'il al-fiqh' (occupying oneself with many fiqh issues) is not a defect but a sign of strong intellect; Abu Yusuf's vast memory of fabricated hadith demonstrates his expertise. The passage ends with a shift to discussing conflicting evidence. Throughout, the commentator uses Hanafi principles, emphasizing that these criticisms do not undermine a narrator's reliability unless they involve actual lies or sins.

Key Terms
التدليس (al-tadlis): Concealing a narrator in the isnad by mentioning a shaykh in a way that suggests direct hearing when it did not occur.
الإرسال (al-irsal): A hadith where the narrator omits the Companion and reports directly from the Prophet or from a later generation.
التلبيس (al-talbis): A form of tadlis where the narrator mentions his shaykh by a kunya or unfamiliar description to hide his identity.
المزاح (al-muzah): Joking; the Prophet engaged in it but without falsehood or insult.
حداثة السن (hadath al-sinn): Young age of a narrator.
استكثار مسائل الفقه (istikthar masa'il al-fiqh): Having many issues of fiqh; some criticized Hanafi scholars for this.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is considered a valid defect (i.e., grounds to reject a narrator)?
A) The narrator is young.
B) The narrator often jokes without lying.
C) The narrator uses 'an' in isnad.
D) The narrator is known to fabricate hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts valid narrator defects to actual violations of integrity (lying, sin) and rejects baseless suspicions like youth, joking, or the use of 'an'.
