Invalid Grounds for Impugning a Narrator (Jarḥ)
Explaining four invalid reasons for jarh in narrators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify four invalid grounds for impugning a narrator (jarḥ) and apply the Hanafi rule that only substantive defects affecting 'adālah or ḍabṭ constitute valid jarḥ.

Core Idea
Joking, young age, lack of narration habit, and fiqh expertise are not valid jarḥ.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar addresses common misconceptions about narrator criticism. The author clarifies that certain traits—joking, youth, lack of habit, and fiqh expertise—are not valid grounds for rejection, as they do not compromise integrity or precision. Examples from the Prophet and Companions illustrate the principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four invalid grounds
Read the passage and list the four reasons some might consider defects but are actually invalid: joking (muzāḥ), young age (ḥidādat al-sinn), lack of narration habit, and expertise in many fiqh issues.
These are explicitly refuted in the text.
2
Analyze the refutation for each ground
For each ground, note the counterexample or evidence provided: the Prophet's truthful joking, young Companions narrating with precision, Abū Bakr's unmatched precision despite little narration, and Abū Yūsuf's vast memory despite fiqh expertise.
The refutation shows that these traits do not inherently harm 'adālah or ḍabṭ.
3
Examine the dalīl for permissible joking
The author cites the hadith of the old woman and the Quranic verse (al-Wāqi‘ah 35-37) to show the Prophet's joke was truthful and thus permissible. This demonstrates that joking is only blameworthy if it involves lying or disrespect.
The hadith is an example, not the proof itself—the proof is the Prophet's consistent truthfulness.
4
Synthesize the usul rule
From the refutations, derive the principle: jarḥ must be based on a genuine defect in 'adālah (moral integrity) or ḍabṭ (precision). Traits like joking, youth, lack of habit, or fiqh expertise do not amount to such defects unless they lead to lying or carelessness.
This principle governs how Hanafis evaluate narrator criticism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب أقسام السنة
بيان طعن يلحق الحديث
من أصحاب الجهاد لا يصلح جرحًا، والمزاح وهو لا يصلح جرحًا؛ لأن النبي عليه كان يمازح كثيرًا، ولكن لا يقول إلّا حقا كما قال لعجوزة "إنّ العجائز لا تدخل الجنة" فلما ولت تبكي، قال: أخبروها بقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّا أَنْشَأْنَاهُنَّ إِنْشَاءً فَجَعَلْنَاهُنَّ أَبْكَارًا عُرُبا﴾ [الواقعة: ٣٥-٣٧] وحداثة السنّ أي صغره كما يقول سفيان الثوري لأبي حنيفة له: ما يقول هذا الشاب الحديث السنّ عندي؛ وذلك لأن كثيرًا من الصحابة منهم كانوا يروون في حداثة سنّهم بشرط الإتقان عند التحمّل والعدالة عند الأداء.
وعدم الاعتياد بالرواية فإن أبا بكر رضي الله عنه لم يكن معتادًا بالرواية مع أن أحدا لم يُعادله في الضبط والإتقان.
واستكثار مسائل الفقه، كما طعن بذلك بعض المحدثين على أصحابنا، فإن ذلك دليل قوة الذهن وجودته، وقد كان أبو يوسف رضي الله عنه يحفظ عشرين ألف حديث من الموضوع فما ظنك بالصحيح؟ ولما فرغ المصنف رحمه الله عن بيان أقسام السنة شرع في بحث المعارضة المشتركة بين الكتاب والسنة تبعًا لفخر الإسلام عليه، وكان ينبغي أن يدرجهما في بحث معارضة العقليات في باب الترجيح كما فعله صاحب "التوضيح"، فقال:
لا يقول إلا حقا إلخ يعني اشترط في صحة المزاح أن لا يقول كذبًا ولا يقصد به إهانة المسلم؛ لأن هذين الأمرين سببان المعصية وفاعلهما خارج عن العدالة. (القمر) بشرط الإتقان والحداثة في السنّ لا تُضادّ العدالة ولا الضبط. (القمر) على أصحابنا: كأبي يوسف رضي الله عنه حيث قال: إنه اشتغل بالفقه وصرف همّته إليه وهذا يوجب القصور في ضبط الحديث وإتقانه. (القمر) فإن ذلك إلخ : أي استكثار مسائل الفقه دليل قوة الذهن، فيستدل به على حسن الضبط والإتقان.(القمر) وكان ينبغي إلخ لأنه ذكر في هذا الفصل معارضة القياسين أيضًا. (القمر)
أخرج رزين والبغوي في "شرح السنة" عن أنس رضي الله عنه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال للعجوز : إنه لا تدخل الجنة عجوز، فقالت وما لهن وكانت تقرأ القرآن؟ فقال لها : أما تقرئين القرآن: ﴿إِنَّا أَنشَأْنَاهُنَّ إِنْشَاءُ﴾ [الواقعة:٣٥] الآية. [إشراق الأبصار ٢٣]
Chapter: Divisions of the Sunnah. Explanation of a defect that attaches to a hadith (narrator). From the people of jihād (?): it does not qualify as jarḥ. And joking: it does not qualify as jarḥ, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to joke often, but he would only say truth. As he said to an old woman: 'Verily, old women do not enter Paradise.' When she turned away crying, he said: 'Tell her [the verse] of Allah: “Indeed, We have created them anew, and made them virgins, loving, matching” [Sūrat al-Wāqi‘ah 35-37].' And youthfulness, i.e., young age, as Sufyān al-Thawrī said about Abū Ḥanīfah: 'What does this young man of recent age have to say?' This is because many Companions used to narrate in their young age, with the condition of precision (iṭqān) at the time of receiving and integrity ('adālah) at the time of delivery. And lack of habituation with narration: for Abū Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) was not accustomed to narrating, yet no one equaled him in precision and firmness. And considering many issues of fiqh as many: as some muḥaddithūn criticized our scholars for that; but that is evidence of strength and quality of intellect. Abū Yūsuf (may Allah be pleased with him) used to memorize twenty thousand fabricated hadiths—what do you think about the authentic ones? When the author (may Allah have mercy on him) finished explaining the divisions of the Sunnah, he began to discuss the issue of contradiction common to the Book and the Sunnah, following Fakhr al-Islam (may Allah have mercy on him). It would have been appropriate to include them in the discussion of contradiction of rational matters in the chapter of tarjīḥ, as the author of al-Tawḍīḥ did. He said: 'He only says truth, etc.' means he stipulated the validity of joking on condition that he not say a lie nor intend to disrespect a Muslim, because these two matters are causes of sin and their doer is outside of integrity. (al-Qamar) With the condition of precision, and youthfulness is not opposed to integrity nor precision. (al-Qamar) Against our scholars: as Abū Yūsuf said, he occupied himself with fiqh and directed his effort to it, and this necessitates deficiency in the precision and firmness of hadith. (al-Qamar) 'That is, etc.': considering many fiqh issues is evidence of strength of mind, so it is used as evidence for good precision and firmness. (al-Qamar) 'It would have been appropriate, etc.' because he mentioned in this chapter also the contradiction of analogies. (al-Qamar) Razīn and al-Baghawī in Sharḥ al-Sunnah narrated from Anas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to the old woman: 'Verily, no old woman enters Paradise.' She said: 'What about them?' and she used to recite the Quran? He said to her: 'Do you not recite the Quran: “Indeed, We have created them anew” [al-Wāqi‘ah:35] etc.' [Ishrāq al-Abṣār 23]
Source pages p. 551

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the divisions of the Sunnah, specifically addressing illegitimate grounds for impugning a narrator's integrity (jarḥ). The author lists four reasons that some might consider defects but are not valid: (1) joking (muzāḥ), (2) young age (ḥidādat al-sinn), (3) lack of habit in narration, and (4) being extensively engaged in fiqh issues. Each is refuted with examples: the Prophet himself joked but only spoke truth; young age did not prevent many Companions from narrating reliably; Abū Bakr was not a prolific narrator yet was unmatched in precision; and mastering fiqh actually demonstrates intellectual strength, as seen with Abū Yūsuf's vast memory. The passage also includes a note that the author should have placed the discussion of contradiction within the chapter on tarjīḥ, as al-Tawḍīḥ did. The marginal notes (al-Qamar) add clarifications, emphasizing that joking is only blameworthy if it involves lying or disrespect, and that youth does not contradict integrity or precision. The hadith about the old woman illustrates the Prophet's permissible joking.

Key Terms
جرح (jarḥ): Impugning a narrator's integrity or memory, rendering their narration unacceptable.
عدالة ('adālah): Moral integrity; a narrator must be a trustworthy Muslim avoiding major sins and persistent minor sins.
ضبط (ḍabṭ): Precision and accuracy in narrating; ability to recall and transmit correctly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT considered a valid ground for impugning a narrator's reliability according to this passage?
A) Lying in joking
B) Young age
C) Lack of habit in narration
D) Expertise in many fiqh issues

Key Takeaway
Invalid jarḥ grounds are those that do not affect a narrator's integrity or precision; only substantive defects matter.

Ta'arud and the Hanafi Method of Taqrir al-Usul: The Case of Donkey's Leftover Water
Resolving conflicting proofs for donkey's leftover water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of taqrir al-usul when conflicting proofs cannot be reconciled, and derive the ruling for su'r al-himar.

Core Idea
When proofs conflict irreconcilably, give effect to both original rulings — su'r al-himar is mashkuk, requiring wudu plus tayammum.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar illustrates how Hanafi usul handles genuine conflict (ta'arud) that cannot be resolved by preference (tarjih). Using the example of donkey's leftover water (su'r al-himar), the author shows that when both textual and analogical proofs clash, the correct approach is to affirm both original legal presumptions: the water's inherent purity and the person's state of hadath. The result is a unique ruling: su'r al-himar is considered mashkuk (doubtful), but its practical ruling is known — wudu with it plus tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting proofs
List the textual proofs (Jabir's hadith allowing wudu, Anas's hadith declaring donkeys impure) and the analogical proofs (qiyas leaning toward purity via cat's su'r, vs. impurity via dog's su'r or milk).
The author notes that both hadith and qiyas conflict, so the conflict is multi-layered.
2
Assess possibility of tarjih
Evaluate whether one proof can be given preference. The author states that after considering all analogies, no preference is possible due to equal strength.
The passage explicitly says 'the door of preference was closed'.
3
Apply taqrir al-usul
When tarjih is closed, give effect to both original rulings: water is originally pure (istishab al-tahara), the person is originally in hadath (istishab al-hadath). Neither can be overridden by doubt.
4
Derive the combined ruling
Combining both original rulings: the water does not become impure, so it can be used for wudu; but its purifying effect is uncertain, so hadath is not certainly removed. Hence, wudu + tayammum is obligatory.
This is the practical outcome: using both water and tayammum ensures both possibilities are covered.
5
Understand the meaning of mashkuk
The ruling is not unknown; it is a determinate obligation to do both acts. This is the Hanafi position: su'r al-himar is mashkuk, requiring wudu and tayammum.
The author clarifies: 'it is called doubtful for this reason, not meaning ignorance'.

في لحومها لزم الاشتباه في سؤرها؛ لأنه متولّد منها، وأيضًا روى جابر عنه أنه عليها سُئل: "أنتوضأ بماء هو فضالة الحمر؟ قال: "نعم"، " و روى أنس له أنه عليها فهي عن ** 11 الحمر الأهلية وقال: "إنها رجس"، وهذا يدل على نجاسة سؤرها، والقياسان أيضا متعارضان؛ لأنه لا يمكن إلحاقه بالعرق ليكون طاهرًا لقلة الضرورة فيه وكثرتها في سؤر الحمار أي بعرق الحمار العرق، ولا يمكن إلحاقه باللبن ليكون نجسًا بجامع التولد من اللحم لوجود الضرورة في سور الحمار بلبن الأتان السؤر دون اللبن، وكذا لا يمكن إلحاقه بسؤر الكلب ليكون نجسا لكون الضرورة في سؤر الحمار الحمار دون الكلب ولا يمكن إلحاقه بسؤر الهرة ليكون طاهراً، لوجود الضرورة في سؤر الحمار الهرة أكثر ممّا يكون في الحمار، فلمّا تعارض هذا كله وانسد باب الترجيح وجب تقرير كل واحد من التوضي والماء على أصله فقيل: إن الماء عُرف طاهرًا في الأصل فلا يتنجس به ما كان طاهراً، ولا يطهر به ما كان نجسًا. فصل في التعارض فلا يتنجس به ما كان طاهرا فوجب استعمال الطاهر والتوضؤ به، والآدمي لما كان في أي على الحدث الأصل محدثاً بقي كذلك.
و لم يزل به الحدث للتعارض فوجب ضمّ التيمم إليه، ولا يقال: إن الماء كان في الأصل مطهرًا فما الاحتياج إلى ضمّ التيمم؟ لأنا نقول : لو أبقينا الماء مطهراً لفات أصل الآدمي وهو الحدث، فلم يكن تقرير الأصول بل تقرير الماء فقط، ولا يقال: إن المُبيح والمُحرّم إذا تعارضا ترجّح المحرّم، فيجب أن يترجح المحرّم ولا يفضي إلى الشك؛ لأنا نقول: إن هذا الترجيح كان للاحتياط، والاحتياط ههنا في جعله مشكوكًا ليتوضأ به ويتيمم. وسمى أي سؤر الحمار مشكوكاً لهذا، أي لأجل التعارض لا أن يعني به الجهل أي لا يعني به أن حكمه مجهول ليكون من قبيل لا أدري، بل حكمه معلوم ، وهو وجوب التوضؤ وضمّ التيمم إليه.
Chapter on Conflict. Statement of the occurrence of conflict between the Book and the Sunnah. Regarding their [donkeys'] meat, confusion necessarily arises about their leftover water because it is generated from them. Also, Jabir narrated from him (the Prophet) that he was asked: 'Do we perform wudu with water that is the leftover of donkeys?' He said: 'Yes.' And Anas narrated that he (the Prophet) prohibited domestic donkeys and said: 'They are filth.' This indicates the impurity of their leftover water. The two analogies are also conflicting: because it is not possible to liken it to sweat to be pure due to the lack of necessity in it and its abundance in the donkey's leftover water, i.e., by the sweat of the donkey, nor can it be likened to milk to be impure due to the common factor of being generated from meat, because necessity exists in the donkey's leftover water by the milk of the female donkey, the leftover water without milk. Similarly, it cannot be likened to the leftover water of a dog to be impure because of the necessity in the donkey's leftover water beyond the dog's, nor can it be likened to the leftover water of a cat to be pure because of the greater necessity in the cat's leftover water than in the donkey's. When all this became conflicting and the door of preference (tarjih) was closed, it became necessary to establish each of the wudu and the water on its original ruling. So it was said: The water is known originally to be pure, so it does not become impure from something that was pure, nor does it purify something that was impure. (al-Qamar: 'The water': i.e., which is the donkey's leftover water.) (al-Muhashi: 'Pure originally': i.e., the water was found originally pure, so it does not become impure by doubt, nor does it purify the one performing wudu because he was originally in a state of hadath, so the hadath is not removed by doubt, so he remains as he was, yet the possibility of removal of hadath exists. So it became obligatory to use the water and to add tayammum, as they said. And it is not objected that the prohibition of meat could be due to honor and that permissibility is not a necessary consequence of purity absolutely, because the explanation of it being filth is mentioned in the hadith of prohibition, so there is no possibility of honor. And here there is a discussion: the hadith of prohibition was narrated by al-Bayhaqi, as said by al-Qari. [Ishraq al-Absar: 24] It was narrated by al-Bukhari no. 3962, chapter of the expedition of Khaybar, and Muslim no. 1940, chapter on permissibility of sea dead animals, from Anas. [PAGE_557] So it does not become impure from what was pure, so it became obligatory to use the pure (water) and perform wudu with it. And the human since he was originally in the state of hadath, remained as such. And the hadath was not removed by it due to conflict, so it became obligatory to add tayammum to it. And it is not said: The water was originally purifying, so what is the need to add tayammum? Because we say: If we kept the water as purifying, the original ruling of the human (hadath) would have been lost, so it would have been establishing the water alone, not both rulings. And it is not said: When the permissive and the prohibitive conflict, the prohibitive is given preference, so it should be preferred and lead to no doubt; because we say: This preference is for caution, and caution here is to make it doubtful so that he performs wudu with it and tayammum. And it (the donkey's leftover water) is called 'doubtful' for this reason, i.e., due to the conflict, not meaning ignorance, i.e., not that its ruling is unknown like 'I don't know', rather its ruling is known: the obligation of performing wudu and adding tayammum.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage from Noor al-Anwar deals with the chapter on ta'arud (conflict) and presents a case study of conflicting proofs regarding the ruling on the leftover water (su'r) of a donkey. The author explains that there are conflicting textual proofs: a hadith from Jabir allowing wudu with it, and a hadith from Anas declaring domestic donkeys impure (rijis), implying impurity of their leftover water. Additionally, analogical reasoning (qiyas) is conflicting: likening the su'r to sweat (pure) vs. milk (impure) vs. dog's su'r (impure) vs. cat's su'r (pure), because of varying degrees of necessity (darurah) in dealing with these animals. Since no preference (tarjih) is possible, the Hanafi jurist must give effect to both the original purity of water and the original impurity (hadath) of the person. The water is originally pure, so it does not become impure by mere doubt, but its purifying power is also in doubt due to possible impurity. The person is originally in hadath, which cannot be removed by something with doubtful purifying power. Therefore, the ruling is to perform wudu with this water and also do tayammum, to ensure both possibilities are covered. This is the Hanafi position: su'r al-himar is considered mashkuk (doubtful), meaning the ruling is known (wudu plus tayammum), not unknown.

Key Terms
التعارض (al-ta'arud): Conflict between two proofs that are equally strong with no clear preference.
سؤر الحمار (su'r al-himar): The leftover water after a donkey drinks from it.
مشكوك (mashkuk): A ruling that is doubtful due to conflicting evidence, but its practical ruling is known (wudu + tayammum).
تقرير الأصول (taqrir al-usul): Giving effect to both original legal presumptions (istishab al-hal) when proofs conflict.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul presented, what is the ruling on su'r al-himar (donkey's leftover water)?
A) It is pure and can be used for wudu alone.
B) It is impure and cannot be used for wudu.
C) It is mashkuk: wudu with it plus tayammum is obligatory.
D) It is makruh but wudu is valid without tayammum.

Key Takeaway
When textual and analogical proofs conflict irreconcilably, the Hanafi method of taqrir al-usul mandates giving effect to both original rulings, resulting in a mashkuk ruling that combines the acts of wudu and tayammum.

Rule of Taking the Version with an Increase (Ziyadah)
Stating the rule that when one report has an extra part, it is accepted as long as the narrator is trustworthy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of ziyādah to resolve apparent contradictions between two narrations of a hadith and distinguish it from the Shafiʿi approach.

Core Idea
An increase from a trustworthy narrator is considered part of the original hadith; omission is due to imprecision.

In Usul al-Fiqh, when two narrations of the same hadith differ, the Hanafis give priority to the version with an additional element from a trustworthy narrator, treating the omission as a mistake. This lesson explores the rule through the example of tahāluf and the dispute with Imam al-Shafiʿi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule of ziyādah
What is the Hanafi rule when one narration has an extra word or phrase?
2
Examine the example of tahāluf
How does the hadith of Ibn Masʿūd illustrate this rule?
3
Contrast the Shafiʿi position
How does Imam al-Shafiʿi treat the two narrations and why?
4
Analyze the Hanafi critique
Why does the Hanafi author argue that Shafiʿi should follow his own principle of carrying the absolute to the restricted?
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in ruling between the two schools?

بيان وقوع التعارض بين الخبرين فصل في التعارض وإذا كانت في أحد الخبرين زيادة فإن كان الراوي واحدًا يؤخذ بالمثبت للزيادة كما في الخبر المروي في التحالف وهو ما روى ابن مسعود ه أنه إذا اختلف المتبايعان فيه والسلعة قائمة تحالفا وترادًا، وفي رواية أخرى عنه لم يذكر قوله: "والسلعة قائمة" فأخذنا بالمثبت للزيادة وقلنا لا يجري التحالف إلا عند قيام السلعة، فكان حذف القيد من بعض الرواة لقلّة الضبط. أي عن ابن مسعود له يؤخذ إلخ: ويقال: إن الخبر واحد، إلا أن الراوي قد يروي مع الزيادة، وقد يحذفها اتكالا على فهم تلك الزيادة من نفس الخبر. (القمر) إذا اختلف المتبايعان أي البائع والمشتري في الثمن. (القمر) وترادًا إلخ: أي يردّ المشتري المبيع والبائع الثمن. (القمر) عند قيام السلعة: ويؤيده قوله عليه: ترادا؛ إذ لو لم يكن مطلقا سواء كانت السلعة قائمة فأيّ شيء يردّ من المشتري البائع، وقال الإمام الشافعي له: إن التحالف يجري السلعة قائمة أو هالكة، وعند الهلاك يردّ المشتري قيمة المبيع إلى البائع ويردّ البائع الثمن إلى المشتري، فإن العمل بالخبرين ضروري وهذا عجيب منه فإن مذهبه حمل المطلق على المقيّد في حكم واحد، فلم لا يحمل المطلق على المقيد ههنا؟ فكان له أن يقول: إن التحالف لا يجري إلّا بشرط قيام السلعة" حملا لحديث الإطلاق على حديث التقييد كذا قال في "التنوير" . (القمر) ينبغي من بعض الرواة إلخ : المراد بالبعض هو ابن مسعود حيث روي تارةً : إذا اختلف البيعان والسلعة قائمة تحالفا وترادا، وفي رواية أخرى له: إذا اختلف البيعان تحالفا وترادًا" فقيدوا هذه الرواية بقيام السلعة جمعا بين الروايتين، وحكموا بالتحالف عند قيام السلعة لا غير بالحذف فقالوا: إنه حديث واحد وارد مع الزيادة لكن حذف الراوي تارة، فالحديث من الأصل موجب للتحالف عند قيام السلعة ساكت عما إذا لم يقم، وليس فيه حمل المطلق على المقيد كما زعم البعض، وما قال في "الكشف" من أن الحمل واجب عند اتحاد الحادثة والحكم وههنا كذلك فساقط؛ لأن الإطلاق والتقييد ههنا دخلا في السبب ولا حمل للمطلق على المقيد في صورة دخولهما على السبب. (السنبلي) أما الرواية التي ليس فيها والسلعة قائمة فما أخرج أبو داود رقم: ۳۵۱۱ باب إذا اختلف البيعان والمبيع قائم، والترمذي رقم: ۱۲۷۰، باب ما جاء إذا اختلف البيعان عن ابن مسعود قال: سمعت رسول الله يقول : إذا اختلف البيعان وليس بينهما بينة فهو ما يقول رب السلعة أو يتتاركان، وأما الرواية التي ذكر فيه هذا فما رواه ابن ماجه رقم ۲۱۸٦ باب البيعان يختلفان عن ابن مسعود يقول : إذا اختلف البيعان، وليس بينهما بينة والبيع قائم بعينه، فالقول ما قال البائع أو يترادّان البيع.
Explanation of the occurrence of conflict between two reports. Chapter on conflict. And if there is an increase in one of the two reports, then if the narrator is one, the one who affirms the increase is taken, as in the report narrated about mutual nullification (tahāluf), which is what Ibn Mas'ud narrated: that if the two parties of a sale differ [about the price] and the commodity is present, they both take an oath and then return [the sale]. And in another narration from him, he did not mention his statement: 'and the commodity is present.' So we took the one affirming the increase and said mutual nullification only occurs when the commodity is present. Thus the omission of the condition by some narrators was due to lack of precision. i.e., from Ibn Mas'ud. It is said: The report is one, except that the narrator may narrate with the increase, and may omit it relying on the understanding of that increase from the report itself. (al-Qamar) 'when the two parties differ' i.e., the seller and buyer in the price. (al-Qamar) 'and they return' etc. i.e., the buyer returns the sold item and the seller returns the price. (al-Sunbuli) 'And in another narration from him: from Ibn Mas'ud, Imam Abu Hanifa narrated: if the two parties differ and they have no evidence, they both swear and annul the sale.' Thus in al-Tanwir. (al-Qamar) 'for the increase' i.e., for the addition of the phrase 'and the commodity is present.' (al-Qamar) 'when the commodity is present': and it is supported by his statement 'they return'; for if it were absolute whether the commodity is present, then what would the buyer return to the seller? Imam al-Shafi'i said: mutual nullification occurs whether the commodity is present or destroyed; and if destroyed, the buyer returns the value of the sold item to the seller and the seller returns the price to the buyer. For acting upon both reports is necessary. And this is strange from him, because his school is to carry the absolute upon the restricted in one ruling, so why does he not carry the absolute upon the restricted here? So he should say: mutual nullification only occurs with the condition of the commodity being present, carrying the absolute hadith upon the restricted one. Thus said in al-Tanwir. (al-Qamar) 'by some narrators' etc.: The intended 'some' is Ibn Mas'ud, for he narrated once: 'if the two parties differ and the commodity is present, they both swear and return [the sale],' and in another narration from him: 'if the two parties differ, they both swear and return.' So they restricted this narration by the presence of the commodity to reconcile between the two narrations, and they ruled that mutual nullification occurs only when the commodity is present, not otherwise, and they said: it is one hadith narrated with the increase, but the narrator omitted it sometimes. So the hadith originally requires mutual nullification when the commodity is present, and is silent about when it is not present. There is no carrying of the absolute upon the restricted as some claimed. And what al-Kashf said, that carrying is obligatory when the incident and ruling are the same, and here it is similar, is invalid; because the absoluteness and restriction here entered into the cause (sabab), and there is no carrying of the absolute upon the restricted when they enter upon the cause. (al-Sunbuli) As for the narration that does not contain 'and the commodity is present,' it is what Abu Dawood narrated no. 3511, the chapter on when the two parties of a sale differ and the sold item is present, and al-Tirmidhi no. 1270, the chapter on what came about when the two parties differ, from Ibn Mas'ud who said: I heard the Messenger of Allah saying: 'When the two parties of a sale differ and they have no evidence, then it is as the owner of the commodity says, or they annul the sale.' As for the narration which includes this, it is what Ibn Majah narrated no. 2186, the chapter on the two parties of a sale differing, from Ibn Mas'ud who says: 'When the two parties of a sale differ and they have no evidence, and the sale item is in its present condition, then the statement is what the seller says, or they return the sale.'
Source pages p. 572

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi rule regarding an increase (ziyadah) in one of two conflicting reports: if a trustworthy narrator adds something not found in another narration, the addition is accepted and considered part of the hadith. The example given is the hadith of tahaluf (mutual oath and rescission) narrated by Ibn Mas'ud. In one version, the phrase 'while the commodity is present' is included, while in another it is omitted. The Hanafis accept the version with the addition and rule that the mutual oath and rescission only apply when the commodity is still in its original state (qa'imah). The omission by some narrators is attributed to lack of precision. The passage then contrasts the Shafi'i position: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the tahaluf applies whether the commodity is present or destroyed, arguing that both narrations must be acted upon. The author criticizes Shafi'i for inconsistency, because his own usul principle is to carry the absolute (mutlaq) upon the restricted (muqayyad) when they share the same ruling. Here, the absolute narration (without the condition) should be restricted by the conditional narration, leading to the Hanafi conclusion. The commentary further explains that this is not a case of carrying absolute upon restricted because the condition entered into the cause (sabab), not the ruling; hence the hadith is one with an added part that was sometimes omitted. The passage ends by citing the exact sources of the two narrations from Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah. This lesson guards against the misunderstanding that an omission in some narrations indicates that the addition is not authentic; rather, the Hanafi rule gives priority to the version with the increase from a trustworthy narrator.

Key Terms
الزيادة (al-ziyādah): An extra word or phrase found in one narration of a hadith that is not present in another narration.
التحالف (al-taḥāluf): A mutual oath between buyer and seller when they disagree on the price and have no evidence; each swears they are correct, then the sale is rescinded.
المثبت (al-muthbit): The narrator who affirms the additional wording; the one whose narration includes the increase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule presented in this passage, why do the Hanafis accept the version of the hadith that includes the phrase 'wa al-sil'atu qa'imah'?
A) Because the version with the phrase has more narrators
B) Because the narrator who included the phrase is more trustworthy and the omission is due to lack of precision
C) Because the version without the phrase is clearly fabricated
D) Because the phrase is found in the Quran

Key Takeaway
When a trustworthy narrator includes an additional element in a hadith, the Hanafi school accepts it as part of the original, and the omission is attributed to lack of precision.

Categories of the Prophet's Intentional Acts
Definition of the four categories of the Prophet's acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four categories of the Prophet's intentional acts and state which acts are for emulation.

Core Idea
The Prophet's acts (excluding slips) guide the ummah in four levels: permissible, recommended, obligatory, and necessary.

This lesson from Noor al-Anwar introduces the foundational Hanafi classification of the Prophet's intentional acts. Understanding these categories is essential for correctly deriving rulings from the Sunnah. The Prophet's every intentional act falls into one of four levels for the ummah, with the exception of slips (zalla), which are not to be emulated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
State the four categories: mubah (permissible), mustahabb (recommended), wajib (obligatory), and fard (necessary). These apply to the Prophet's intentional acts.
The text explicitly enumerates these four.
2
Define the exclusion of zalla
Explain that a slip (zalla) is a forbidden act occurring from a permissible intention without deliberate design. It is not a precedent for the ummah due to the Prophet's infallibility.
The definition is detailed in the legal definition dissector.
3
Understand intentionality
Note that only intentional acts are classified; acts done in sleep or forgetfully are not for emulation.
The passage includes this clarification.
4
Relate to the ummah
Recognize that the categories describe how the ummah should relate to each act: mubah is permissible, mustahabb is recommended, wajib is obligatory, and fard is necessity.
These are normative for followers.

Chapter on the Acts of the Prophet. Sections of the Prophet's acts: The increase by it upon the text of the Book indicating absoluteness, and similar matters are many between us and him. And only by qiyas we have specified this division to the Book, because its organization (nazm) is connected to recitation and permissibility of prayer, and to its meaning is obligation of action and absoluteness. So it is possible that one of them is abrogated without the other, and that both are abrogated, and that the organization or the meaning is abrogated while its essence remains, unlike the Sunnah, because its organization does not have attached rulings, nor is it increased upon the mashhur khabar by another khabar in the custom of the Law, so this division does not apply to it. And when the author (may Allah have mercy on him) finished the division of bayan, he began to explain the practical Sunnah, following Fakhr al-Islam, and it would have been appropriate to mention it after the verbal Sunnah consecutively as the author of al-Tawdih did. So he said: [Chapter on the Acts of the Prophet] The acts of the Prophet (peace be upon him) other than the slip (zalla) are four categories: mubah, mustahabb, wajib, and fard. He exempted the slip because the chapter is to explain the emulation of the ummah by him, and the slip is not something to be emulated. It is a name (for this category) for a forbidden act that occurred due to an intention to do a permissible act, so his intention was not initially for the forbidden. (Qamar) And the permissibility of prayer and the prohibition of touching for the junub and menstruating woman. (Qamar) The mashhur khabar etc., unlike the Book, for increase upon it is permissible with mashhur khabar. (al-Sanbali) So this does not apply etc., how can it be that the hadith is not recited revelation so that its recitation is abrogated? Rather abrogation is only in its ruling. (Qamar) Consecutively etc., i.e., he did not mention between them the exclusion, condition, and divisions of abrogating and abrogated. (al-Sanbali) The acts of the Prophet up to: what is intended is the intentional acts; for what emanates from him in sleep or in wakefulness forgetfully without intention is not suitable for emulation by agreement, because humans are not free from what they are naturally disposed to. (Qamar) Mubah and mustahabb etc., i.e., his act in relation to us is described as such. [Fath al-Ghaffar 343] Due to the intention for a permissible act etc., i.e., the doer slipped due to engagement in the permissible act he intended to a forbidden matter not intended, so this slip is not called a sin except metaphorically; for sin is the name for a forbidden act that is itself intended without intention to oppose the command, for if it were intended it would be disbelief. (Qamar) For a permissible act etc., i.e., he intended a permissible act and fell into the forbidden without intention and choice, rather the permissible became a cause for him. So his statement: 'His intention was not for the forbidden initially' means nor finally, so the intention is to negate his intention for the forbidden absolutely, because the Prophet is infallible from it, and therefore it is not permissible for him to settle upon it after occurrence. (al-Sanbali)
Source pages p. 605

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter on the acts of the Prophet (af'al al-nabi). It first explains why the previous discussion on increase (ziyada) is specific to the Quran and not the Sunnah: the Quran has both recitation (tilawa) and meaning (ma'na), each of which can be abrogated independently, while the Sunnah only has meaning. Then it moves to the categorization of the Prophet's intentional acts into four: mubah (permissible), mustahabb (recommended), wajib (obligatory), and fard (necessary). The term 'zalla' (slip) is excluded because it is not for emulation; it refers to an inadvertent fall into a forbidden act while intending something permissible. The Prophet is infallible, so such slips are not sins. The four categories are for the ummah to follow according to the nature of the act.

Key Terms
الزلة (al-zalla): A slip: a forbidden act that occurs from a permissible intention without initial design.
المباح (al-mubah): An act of the Prophet that is permissible for the ummah.
المستحب (al-mustahabb): An act of the Prophet that is recommended for the ummah.
الواجب (al-wajib): An act of the Prophet that is obligatory for the ummah.
الفرض (al-fard): An act of the Prophet that is necessary for the ummah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's intentional acts (excluding slips) are classified into four levels for the ummah: mubah, mustahabb, wajib, and fard.

Following the Prophet's Actions: The Hanafi Default of Permissibility
Usul rule on following prophetic actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that an action of the Prophet with unknown legal status is presumed permissible, and distinguish this from other scholarly positions.

Core Idea
Unknown status of a prophetic act defaults to permissibility until evidence shows otherwise.

This passage from Noor al-Anwaar categorizes the Prophet’s actions and addresses a foundational usul question: how should the Ummah follow actions whose legal status (obligation, recommendation, or permissibility) is unknown? The Hanafi school adopts a clear answer—the default is permissibility (ibaha)—based on the principle that actions are originally permissible and that following the Prophet does not require knowing the exact description of his act. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rule, contrasts it with opposing views, and shows its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three excluded categories
The text first lists actions that are not followed: those done forgetfully (e.g., salam after two rak'ahs), those habitual (eating, sleeping), and those specific to the Prophet (e.g., marrying more than four). These are excluded from the scope of the rule.
These categories are not the focus of the dispute; they are exceptions.
2
Recognize the three scholarly positions
The passage presents three views on how to treat an action of the Prophet whose legal status is unknown: (1) pause until status is known (al-Daqqaq, al-Ghazali); (2) follow unless evidence of prohibition (Malik, Ibn Shurayh); (3) presume permissibility (al-Karkhi). Note their justifications.
These positions are based on different understandings of 'following' (ittiba').
3
Understand the Hanafi chosen view
The author states the preferred Hanafi view: if we know the status (wajib, mandub, mubah), we follow accordingly, unless evidence of specificity (khusus) arises. If we do not know, we assume the act was done on the lowest rank—permissibility. This is the view of Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi.
This combines following with the default principle of ibaha asl al-ashya.
4
Apply the rule to a specific example
Consider a prophetic act like wearing a certain type of garment. If no evidence indicates obligation, recommendation, or specificity, the Hanafi rule says it is permissible for the Ummah to wear it. One may perform the act with the intention of following the Prophet without needing to know its exact categorization.
This is the practical consequence: active following without hesitation.

Source Text

فصل في أفعال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم
أقسام أفعال النبي
ولا يستقر عليه بعد الوقوع كمثل من أحنى في الطريق، فخرّ منه، ثم قام عاجلًا، فما كان قصده الخرور، وما استقر عليه كما كان من قصد من عليها بالضرب تأديب موسى القبطي، فقضى عليه بالقتل، فلم يكن القتل مقصوده ، و لم يبق عليه بل ندم، وقال: هذا من عمل الشيطان، ولكن هذا التقسيم بالنسبة إلينا، وإلا ففي حقه عليه لم يكن شيء واجبًا اصطلاحيًا؛ لأنه ما ثبت بدليل فيه شبهة، وكانت الدلائل كلها قطعية في حقه، ثم إنهم اختلفوا في اقتداء أفعال لم تصدر عنه سهوًا ، ولم تكن له طبعًا، ولم تكن مخصوصة به، من قصد من أحنى أي أحنى نفسه في بعض النسخ من أخبى. (القمر) كفه عليه يجمع في حقه وأما في حقنا فيتحقق الواجب الاصطلاحي لتصوّر ثبوت وجوب بعض أفعال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في حقنا بدليل فيه شبهة. ولك أن تقول: إنهم قالوا بجواز الاجتهاد في حقه مع احتمال الخطأ لكنه لا يُقرر عليه، وهذا يدل على ثبوت الدليل الظني في حقه ، فيتحقق الواجب في حقه أول وقت الاجتهاد، فيصح التقسيم الرباعي بالنسبة إليه أيضا، وله توجيه آخر أيضا، وهو أن المراد بالواجب ما كان صفة كمال، ولا يكون ركنا ولا شرطًا، والمراد بالخوض ما يكون ركنا أو شرطًا، فيصح التقسيم الرباعي أيضًا. فقال بعضهم: يجب التوقف فيه حتى يظهر أن النبي عليه على أي وجه فعله والندب والوجوب، وقال بعضهم يجب اتباعه ما لم يقم دليل المنع ، وقال الكر حي أي أبو الحسن الكرخي يعتقد فيه الإباحة لتيقنها إلا إذا دلّ الدليل على الوجوب والندب، والمصنف به ترك هذا كله وبين ما هو المختار عنده فقال: أي الاختلاف أي اتباعا لفخر الإسلام بيه والصحيح عندنا أن ما علمنا من أفعاله الا الله واقعا على جهة من الوجوب أو الندب أو الإباحة نقتدي به في إيقاعه على تلك الجهة حتى يقوم دليل الخصوص، فما كان واجبًا عليه يكون واجبًا علينا، وما كان مندوبا عليه يكون مندوبا علينا، وما كان مباحًا له يكون مباحًا لنا. وما لم يعلم على أية جهة فعله قلنا : فعله على أدنى منازل أفعاله وهو الإباحة . فقال بعضهم: هو أبو بكر الدقاق والغزالي من الشافعية. (القمر)
Chapter on the Actions of the Prophet, peace be upon him. Categories of the Prophet's actions: And it does not settle upon him after occurrence, like one who bent in the road and fell from it, then stood up quickly; what was intended was the fall, and what settled was as it was. And like the one who intended to strike the Copt with a blow to discipline him, but it resulted in death; the killing was not his intention, and he did not remain at ease with it but regretted and said: 'This is from the work of Satan.' But this division is relative to us; otherwise, regarding him, nothing was conventionally obligatory because nothing was established by a proof containing any ambiguity, and all proofs were definitive regarding him. Then they differed concerning following actions that did not occur from him through forgetfulness, were not habitual, and were not specific to him. (Commentary) ... Then some said: one must pause until it becomes apparent on which basis the Prophet did the action—permissibility, recommendation, or obligation. Some said: one must follow him as long as no proof of prohibition stands. Al-Karkhi said: one presumes permissibility because it is certain, unless a proof indicates obligation or recommendation. The author left all this and stated what is chosen: 'And the correct view with us is that what we know of his actions as having occurred on a basis of obligation, recommendation, or permissibility, we follow him in performing it on that basis until evidence of specificity arises. So what was obligatory upon him is obligatory upon us, what was recommended upon him is recommended upon us, and what was permissible for him is permissible for us. And what we do not know on which basis he did it, we say: he did it on the lowest rank of his actions, which is permissibility.' (Commentary) ...
Source pages p. 606

Commentary
This passage discusses how the Ummah should follow the actions of the Prophet ﷺ. The author first explains a division of actions relative to us, as opposed to the Prophet himself for whom obligations are established definitively. He then addresses three categories of actions: those done forgetfully (like the salam after two rak'ahs in Zuhr), those habitual (like eating, sleeping), and those specific to him (like marrying more than four). The main dispute is about following actions whose legal status is unknown. Three views are presented: (1) pause until the status is known (attributed to al-Daqqaq and al-Ghazali); (2) follow unless there is evidence of prohibition (attributed to Malik and Ibn Shurayh); (3) presume permissibility (Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi). The author then gives the preferred Hanafi view: if we know the status (wajib, mandub, mubah), we follow accordingly unless evidence shows it is specific to the Prophet. If we do not know, we assume permissibility. This is based on the verse 'Say: If you love Allah, follow me' (3:31) and the principle that the default in actions is permissibility. The Hanafi position balances following the Prophet with adherence to usul.

Key Terms
الواجب (al-wājib): An action established by a definitive or ambiguous proof; in the Prophet's case, obligations are definitive
المندوب (al-mandūb): An action recommended but not obligatory
المباح (al-mubāḥ): An action permissible to do or leave, with no reward or punishment
الخصوص (al-khuṣūṣ): Specificity of the Prophet: an action or ruling exclusive to him

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view in this passage, what is the ruling on performing an action of the Prophet whose legal status (obligation, recommendation, permissibility) is unknown?
A) One must refrain (tawaqquf) until the status is determined.
B) One must follow it as obligatory unless proof of specificity exists.
C) One presumes it is permissible (mubah) unless evidence of obligation, recommendation, or specificity appears.
D) One should ask a scholar before performing it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul rule: for a prophetic action of unknown legal status, the default is permissibility (ibaha), allowing the Ummah to actively follow it unless evidence of specificity or higher status arises.

Default Ruling for Unknown Prophet's Actions
Usul rule establishing default permissibility for unknown Prophet's actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi position on the default ruling for the Prophet's actions when the modality is unknown and IDENTIFY the key difference from the opposing view of tawaqquf.

Core Idea
When unsure of the Prophet's intent, assume permissibility — the lowest rank of his actions.

This passage tackles a fundamental question: when we know the Prophet performed an act but we don't know whether it was obligatory, recommended, or merely permissible, what should we do? The Hanafi school provides a clear principle that balances following the Prophet with avoiding unnecessary burden. By analyzing earlier opinions and the chosen view, we learn how to derive rulings from the Prophet's actions in a systematic way.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the core problem is determining the legal status of the Prophet's actions when the evidence does not specify whether it was wajib, mandub, or mubah.
This is a classic usul al-fiqh problem regarding the classification of actions of the Lawgiver.
2
Survey the three earlier positions
The text lists three earlier views: tawaqquf (suspension), compulsory following unless proof of prohibition, and al-Karkhi's presumption of permissibility. Understand each and how they differ.
These positions reflect different epistemological assumptions about following the Prophet.
3
Grasp the chosen Hanafi view
The author presents a two-part rule: when the modality is known, we follow in that exact modality; when unknown, we default to permissibility (ibaha) as the lowest rank of his actions.
This position combines practical following with a default that is lenient yet respectful.
4
Examine the evidence
The Hanafi position is grounded in the principle of original permissibility (al-asl fi al-ashya' al-ibaha), the Prophet's sinlessness, and the general command to follow him (Quran 3:31).
Evidence is both transmitted (Quran) and rational (necessity and minimal obligation).
5
Apply the rule
Practice distinguishing between known and unknown modalities. For example, the Prophet's daily prayers are known to be obligatory, his night prayers are recommended, and his wearing of a certain garment is unknown, hence permissible.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is that a Hanafi can freely perform an act of unknown modality without assuming it is sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في أفعال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم
أقسام أفعال النبي
فقال بعضهم: يجب التوقف فيه حتى يظهر أن النبي عليه على أي وجه فعله والندب والوجوب، وقال بعضهم يجب اتباعه ما لم يقم دليل المنع، وقال الكرخي يعتقد فيه الإباحة لتيقنها إلا إذا دلّ الدليل على الوجوب والندب، والمصنف ترك هذا كله وبين ما هو المختار عنده فقال:
والصحيح عندنا أن ما علمنا من أفعاله صلى الله عليه وسلم واقعا على جهة من الوجوب أو الندب أو الإباحة نقتدي به في إيقاعه على تلك الجهة حتى يقوم دليل الخصوص، فما كان واجبًا عليه يكون واجبًا علينا، وما كان مندوبا عليه يكون مندوبا علينا، وما كان مباحًا له يكون مباحًا لنا.
وما لم يعلم على أية جهة فعله قلنا: فعله على أدنى منازل أفعاله وهو الإباحة.
Chapter on the Actions of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Categories of the Prophet's Actions. Some said: One must pause until it becomes clear on what basis the Prophet performed it—recommendation or obligation. And some said: One must follow it as long as no evidence of prohibition arises. And al-Karkhi said: He considers it permissible (ibaha) due to certainty of permissibility unless evidence indicates obligation or recommendation. The author left all this and clarified his chosen position, saying: The correct view among us is that when we know his actions occurred in a particular manner—obligatory, recommended, or permissible—we follow him in performing it in that same manner until evidence of exclusivity arises. Thus, whatever was obligatory upon him is obligatory upon us; whatever was recommended upon him is recommended upon us; whatever was permissible for him is permissible for us. And what we do not know in which manner he did it, we say: He did it in the lowest rank of his actions, which is permissibility.
Source pages p. 607

Commentary
This is a ruling passage establishing the Hanafi methodology for following the actions of Prophet Muhammad (PBUH). The author first records three earlier positions: (1) suspension until the modality is known (attributed to some Shafi'is), (2) mandatory following unless a contrary proof exists (attributed to Malik), and (3) al-Karkhi's view assuming permissibility unless a stronger proof indicates obligation or recommendation. The author then presents the chosen Hanafi view, which is a nuanced synthesis: when the legal modality (obligation, recommendation, permissibility) of an action is known from the Prophet, we follow it precisely in that modality unless evidence shows it was specific to him. When the modality is unknown, we assume he performed it in the lowest rank—permissibility—because the Prophet never did anything impermissible (haram) or disliked (makruh), so permissibility is the default. This follows the principle of original permissibility in acts (al-asl fi al-ashya' al-ibaha) and the Quranic command to obey the Prophet (Quran 3:31). Note that this ruling applies as long as no evidence indicates exclusivity to the Prophet; if such evidence exists, we do not follow that action.

Key Terms
فعل النبي (Fi‘l al-Nabi): An action performed by Prophet Muhammad (PBUH) that may carry a legal ruling of obligation, recommendation, or permissibility.
إباحة (Ibaha): Permissibility; the lowest rank of legal value, meaning the act is allowed but not required or recommended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi view, what is the default ruling for an action of the Prophet (PBUH) when we do not know the manner in which he performed it?
A) It is obligatory (wajib) upon us.
B) It is recommended (mandub) upon us.
C) It is permissible (mubah) for us.
D) We must pause (tawaqquf) until evidence appears.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defaults to permissibility (ibaha) for Prophet's actions of unknown modality, based on the principle of original permissibility and the general command to follow him.

The Prophet's Ijtihad as Inner Revelation
Debate on whether Prophet's ijtihad is considered wahy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that the Prophet's ijtihad is inner revelation (wahy batin) and evaluate the opposing Ash'ari argument using Quran 53:3-4.

Core Idea
The Prophet's ijtihad is inner revelation because Allah ultimately approves it — even if erring, revelation corrects.

This passage tackles a foundational usul debate: does the Prophet's personal reasoning (ijtihad) count as revelation? The Ash'aris and Mu'tazila argue that all his speech is direct wahy, citing the famous verse of Surah al-Najm. The Hanafis respond with a nuanced distinction between external and inner revelation, and describe the Prophet's actual procedure of waiting for revelation before resorting to ijtihad. Understanding this dispute clarifies the scope of ijtihad and the authority of the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Recognize that the dispute is about whether the Prophet's ijtihad is a form of revelation (wahy) or purely human reasoning.
2
Examine the opposing proof
Read Quran 53:3-4 as cited by the opponents and note their interpretation: the pronoun 'huwa' refers to all the Prophet's speech.
The opponent's argument hinges on the generality of the pronoun.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response: takhsis
Understand the first Hanafi defense: the verse is specifically about the Quran, not all speech. This is a claim of specification (takhsis) based on context and qara'in.
If accepted, the verse does not apply to ijtihad.
4
Examine the alternative Hanafi defense
Even if the verse is general, the Hanafis argue that ijtihad is still 'inner revelation' because Allah ultimately approves the correct ijtihad and corrects errors via revelation.
This introduces the concept of wahy batin.
5
Describe the Prophet's procedure
Learn the three-step process: wait for revelation up to three days, then perform ijtihad; if correct, no revelation; if incorrect, revelation corrects.
This shows the priority of direct revelation and the subsidiary role of ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في أفعال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بيان أقسام الوحي والباطن ما ينال بالاجتهاد بالتأمل في الأحكام المنصوصة بأن يستنبط علة في الحكم المنصوص، ويقيس عليه ما لم يعلم حاله بالنص كما كان شأن سائر المجتهدين، فأبى بعضهم أن يكون هذا من حظه عليه؛ لأن الله تعالى قال: ﴿وَمَا يَنْطِقُ عَنِ الْهَوَى إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا وَحْيٌ يُوحَى﴾ [النجم: 3-4] أي الاجتهاد يُوحَى، فكل ما تكلّمه لا بد أن يكون ثابتا بالوحي، والاجتهاد ليس كذلك، فلا يكون هذا شأنه، والجواب: أن المراد بهذا الوحي هو القرآن دون كل ما تكلّم به، ولئن سلّم أنه عام فلا نسلّم أن اجتهاده ليس بوحي، بل هو وحي باطن باعتبار المآل والقرار عليه. وعندنا هو مأمور بانتظار الوحي فيما لم يوح إليه، أي إذا نزلت الحادثة بين يديه يجب عليه أن ينتظر الوحي أوّلاً لجوابها إلى ثلاثة أيام أو إلى أن يخاف فوت الغرض. ثم العمل بالرأي بعد انقضاء مدة الانتظار، فإن كان أصاب في الرأي لم ينزل الوحي عليه في تلك الحادثة، وإن كان أخطأ في الرأي ينزل الوحي للتنبيه على الخطاء.
Chapter on the Actions of the Prophet (peace be upon him). Explanation of the divisions of revelation, the inner of which is attained through ijtihad by reflecting on the prescribed rulings, deriving the effective cause of the prescribed ruling, and analogizing what is not known by text, as was the way of other mujtahids. Some denied that this part belongs to him because Allah said: 'Nor does he speak from desire; it is only revelation revealed' (53:3-4). For they claim that ijtihad is revealed, so everything he speaks must be established by revelation, but ijtihad is not like that, therefore it cannot be of this description. The answer is that what is meant by this revelation is the Qur'an, not everything he speaks. And if it is conceded that it is general, we do not concede that his ijtihad is not revelation; rather it is inner revelation by virtue of the outcome and the approval upon it. And with us, he is commanded to wait for revelation in what has not been revealed to him, i.e., when an event occurs before him, he must first wait for revelation for an answer for up to three days or until he fears the loss of the purpose. Then he acts by opinion after the period of waiting elapses. If he is correct in his opinion, then no revelation comes down concerning that event; if he errs in his opinion, then revelation comes down to draw attention to the error.
Source pages p. 610

Commentary
This passage discusses a key usul dispute: whether the Prophet's ijtihad (independent reasoning) is a form of wahy. The opponents (Ash'aris and most Mu'tazila) argue using the verse 'Nor does he speak from desire; it is only revelation revealed' (53:3-4) that all the Prophet's speech is wahy, so ijtihad cannot be from his own reasoning. The Hanafi response employs takhsis (specification): the verse refers specifically to the Qur'an, not all speech. Even if general, we argue that ijtihad is 'inner revelation' (wahy batin) because Allah ultimately approves it, making it equivalent to revelation in consequence. The passage also explains the Prophet's procedure: when an event occurred, he would wait for revelation initially (up to three days), then resort to ijtihad. If correct, no revelation came; if incorrect, revelation would correct him. This establishes the priority of direct revelation and the legitimacy of ijtihad as a subsidiary method.

Key Terms
وحي باطن (waḥy bāṭin): Inner revelation; ijtihad of the Prophet that is ultimately confirmed by Allah and thus attains the status of revelation in effect.
اجتهاد (ijtihād): Independent reasoning to derive a legal ruling from the sources by analogy or inference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what happens if the Prophet's ijtihad is incorrect?
A) He is punished for it.
B) Revelation descends to correct the error.
C) The ruling stands anyway.
D) He is required to repeat the ijtihad.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school affirms the Prophet's ijtihad as inner revelation, establishing a balanced methodology of textual priority and reasoned inference.

Prophetic Infallibility from Persisting in Error
Explaining the difference between prophetic and non-prophetic ijtihad infallibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between prophetic and non-prophetic ijtihad infallibility and identify the temporal rule regarding ijtihad and later revelation.

Core Idea
The Prophet is protected from persisting in error; other mujtahids are not.

In this passage, the author of the Hanafi usul text takes up a critical question: does the Prophet's ijtihad carry the same weight as that of other scholars? Using the famous incident of the captives of Badr, the passage illustrates a key distinction—while the Prophet can err in his reasoning, he is immediately corrected by revelation and does not persist in error. Other mujtahids, however, may remain on error until evidence corrects them. This lesson will guide you through the incident and the derived rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key principle
Read the opening lines: the Prophet is ma'sum from persisting in error, unlike other mujtahids. This is the core legal rule.
2
Analyze the Badr incident
The passage narrates the consultation between the Prophet and his Companions. Note the two opinions: Abu Bakr (ransom) and Umar (execution). The Prophet chose Abu Bakr's view.
This shows the Prophet used ijtihad (personal reasoning).
3
Follow the revelation
After the ransom was taken, Quran 8:67-69 was revealed, indicating that the ideal was Umar's view. The Prophet wept and acknowledged the error.
Revelation corrected the ijtihad but did not overturn the already executed ruling.
4
Understand the temporal distinction
The passage emphasizes: when a text (nass) comes after ijtihad, the ijtihad is not overturned; when text pre-exists, ijtihad contrary to it is void.
This is the key usul rule derived from the incident.
5
Apply to the concept of 'isma
The Prophet's 'isma (infallibility) is from persisting in error, not from error itself. This distinguishes him from all other mujtahids.
Other mujtahids may persist in error until corrected by evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أقسام الوحي
فصل في أفعال النبي وما تقرر على الخطأ ،قط بخلاف سائر المجتهدين، فإنهم إن أخطئوا يبقى خطؤهم إلى يوم القيامة، وهذا معنى قوله : إلا أنه عليه معصوم عن القرار على الخطاء بخلاف ما يكون من غيره من البيان بالرأي من مجتهدي الأمة، فإنهم يقرّرون على الخطأ ولا يعصمون عن القرار عليه، ونظائره كثيرة في كتب الأصول، منها: أنه لما أُسر أسارى بدر، وهم سبعون نفراً من الكفار ، فشاور النبي عليه أصحابه في حقهم، فتكلم كل منهم برأيه، فقال أبو بكر : هم قومك وأهلك، خذ منهم فداء ينفعنا وخلهم أحراراً لعلهم يُوفّقون بالإسلام بعد ذلك، وقال عمر : مكن نفسك من قتل عباس، ومكّن عليا من قتل عقيل، ومكني من قتل فلان ليقتل كل واحد منا قريبه، فقال علي: "إن الله ليلين قلوب رجال كالماء ويشدّد قلوب رجال كالحجارة، مَثَلُك يا أبا بكر له كمثل إبراهيم حيث قال: ﴿فَمَنْ تَبِعَنِي فَإِنَّهُ مِنِّي وَمَنْ عَصَانِي فَإِنَّكَ غَفُورٌ رَحِيمٌ ، ومَثَلُك يا عمر، كمثل نوح حيث قال: ﴿رَبِّ لَا تَذَرْ عَلَى الْأَرْضِ مِنَ الْكَافِرِينَ ديارا ، ثم استقر رأيه عليه على رأي أبي بكر ، فأمر بأخذ الفداء، وقال "تستشهدون في أحد بعددهم"، . . وخلى الأسراء إلا أنه عليا معصوم إلخ كيلا يلزم إتباع الأمة له في الخطاء ؛ فإنه إذا أقره الله تعالى على اجتهاده دل على أنه كان هو الصواب فيكون مخالفته حرامًا، فلزمه الإتباع في الخطاء . (القمر) القرار عليه: أي الخطأ ، ولذا جاز مخالفة مجتهد لمجتهد آخر (القمر) أسارى بدر والبدر اسم موضع بين مكة والمدينة، وعليه الأكثرون، وقيل: اسم لبئر هناك، وقيل: كانت بدر بئر الرجل يقال له بدر. قاله الشعبي، كذا في "معالم التنزيل". (القمر) أسارى جمع أسير، وقد يجئ جمعه أيضًا على وزن فعلى نحو أسْرَى ، وفَعَالى بفتح الفاء نحو أسارى، وفُعَلاء نحو أَسَرَاء، والأسير معنى الأخيذ أي المأخوذ "أقرب". (السنبلي) سبعون نفراً إلخ ومنهم العباس عمّه وعقيل بن أبي طالب (القمر) مكن نفسك إلخ: وفي التوضيح مكن حمزة من العباس (القمر) فداء: الفداء والفَدَى والفِدَى مصادر، وما يُعطى من المال عوض المَفْدِي، "فداك أبي وأمي" يريدون به معنى الدعاء أي أفديك بأبي وأمي (السنبلي في أحد إلخ جبل بالمدينة على أقل من فرسخ، وقبر هارون عليه ،به والغزوة كانت عنده في شوال سنة ثلاث. كذا في "التوشيح" شرح صحيح البخاري (القمر)
بيان أقسام الوحي
فصل في أفعال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالوا: قبلنا، فلما أخذوا الفداء نزل عليه قوله تعالى: مَا كَانَ لِنَبِيٍّ أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهُ أَسْرَى حَتَّى يُشْخِنَ فِي الْأَرْضِ تُرِيدُونَ عَرَضَ الدُّنْيَا وَاللَّهُ يُرِيدُ الْآخِرَةَ وَاللَّهُ عَزِيزٌ حَكِيمٌ لَوْلَا كِتَابٌ مِنَ اللَّهِ سَبَقَ لَمَسَّكُمْ فِيمَا أَخَذْتُمْ عَذَابٌ عَظِيمٌ فَكُلُوا مِمَّا غَنِمْتُمْ حَلالاً طَيِّباً وَاتَّقُوا اللَّهَ إِنَّ اللَّهَ غَفُورٌ رَحِيمٌ فبكى رسول الله ، وبكى الصحابة كلهم وقال لو نزل العذاب ما نجا أحدٌ منا إلا عمر ومعاذ بن سعد، فظهر أن الحق هو رأي عمر منه نه، وأن النبي عليه أخطأ حين عمل برأي أبي بكر الله لكنه لم يقرّر على الخطأ، بل تنبه عليه بإنزال الآيات، وأمضى الحكم على الفداء، وأمر بأكله، ولم يأمر بردّ الفداء وحرمته، وهذا هو الفرق بين نزول النص بخلاف الرأي وبين ظهوره بخلافه، فإن في الأول لا ينقض الرأي بالنص، وفي الثاني ينقض به.
وهذا كالإلهام أي الفرق بين اجتهاد النبي عليه وغيره من المجتهدين كالفرق بين إلهام أي اجتهاده
فقالوا قبلنا وقد وقع ذلك، فإنه قتل يوم أحد سبعون من الصحابة له كذا في "صحيح البخاري".(القمر) حتى يُثخن أي يبالغ في قتل المشركين والأسارى جمع الأسير. وعرض الدنيا أي متاعها. (القمر) كتاب من الله: أي لو لا حكم الله سبق في اللوح المحفوظ، وهو أن المجتهد لا يؤاخذ وإن أخطأ.(القمر)
إلا عمر لكون رأيه مطابقا للوحي في ذالك (السنبلي) ومعاذ بن سعد وفي "معالم التنزيل": وسعيد بن معاذ، فإنه قال يا رسول الله، الإثخان في القتل أحب إلي من استيفاء الرجال. (القمر) فظهر أن الحق إلخ وظهر أيضا أن الحكم الاجتهادي لا ينقض وإن يظهر الخطاء ، وأن ما يؤخذ بالحكم الاجتهادي حلال طيب وإن يظهر الخطاء . (القمر) وبين ظهوره أي ظهور النص، بخلاف الرأي، وقيل: أي ظهور ما وقع في الرأي بخلاف النص. (القمر) في الأول : أي في نزول النص بخلاف الرأي. (القمر) في الأول إلخ وجه عدم نقض الرأي نزول النص بعد الحكم على الرأي، ولهذا أمر بأكله، ولم يَرُدّ الفداء، ولم يأمر بحرمته، ووجه نقض الرأي في الثاني هو تقدّم النص على الرأي. (السنبلي وفي الثاني: أي ظهور النص بخلاف الرأي وقيل أي ظهور الرأي بخلاف النص ينقض الرأي به أي بالنص. (القمر)
أخرج ذلك القصة البغوي في تفسيره وابن أبي شيبة وأحمد والترمذي وحسنه وابن المنذر وابن أبي حاتم والطبراني وابن مردوية والحاكم وصححه والبيهقي في الدلائل عن الأعمش عن عمرو بن مُرّة عن أبي عبيد الله بن مسعود ده بألفاظ تقارب هذا. [إشراق الأبصار ٢٧]
Statement of the divisions of revelation. Chapter on the actions of the Prophet and his not persisting in error, unlike other mujtahids, because if they err, their error remains until the Day of Resurrection. And this is the meaning of his saying: 'Except that he is infallible from persisting in error, contrary to what comes from others of the expression of opinion from the mujtahids of the Ummah, for they persist in error and are not protected from persisting in it.' And there are many parallels in the books of usul, among them: when the captives of Badr were taken prisoner, seventy men from the disbelievers, the Prophet consulted his Companions about them, and each spoke his opinion. Abu Bakr said: 'They are your people and family; take ransom from them that will benefit us, and let them go free, perhaps they will be guided to Islam after that.' And Umar said: 'Empower yourself to kill al-Abbas, empower Ali to kill Aqil, and empower me to kill so-and-so, so that each of us may kill his relative.' ... Then the Prophet settled on Abu Bakr's opinion and ordered that ransom be taken, and said: 'You will be martyred in Uhud equal to their number.' ... When they took the ransom, the verse was revealed: 'It is not for a prophet to have captives until he has made slaughter in the land. You desire the goods of this world, while Allah desires the Hereafter...' So the Messenger of Allah wept, and all the Companions wept, and he said: 'If punishment had descended, none of us would have been saved except Umar and Muadh ibn Sa'd.' Thus it became clear that the truth was Umar's opinion, and that the Prophet had erred when he acted on Abu Bakr's opinion, but he did not persist in error; rather, he was alerted by the revelation of the verses. And he confirmed the ruling on the ransom, ordered that it be eaten, and did not order its return or prohibition. This is the difference between the revelation of a text contrary to the opinion and its appearance contrary to it: in the first case, the opinion is not overturned by the text; in the second, it is overturned.
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work explaining a key principle: the Prophet Muhammad is divinely protected (ma'sum) from persisting in error in his ijtihad, unlike other mujtahids. The author illustrates this with the famous incident of the captives of Badr. After consulting the Companions, the Prophet initially followed Abu Bakr's advice to accept ransom. Umar advised killing them. Later, revelation (Quran 8:67-69) indicated that the better course was to kill them first, but the ransom had already been taken. The Prophet wept and acknowledged Umar's view was correct. However, the ruling on the ransom was not overturned; they were allowed to eat what they had taken. This demonstrates that when revelation comes after a ruling based on ijtihad, the ruling is not invalidated (the first case). If revelation had preceded the ijtihad, the ijtihad would be overturned (the second case). The distinction hinges on whether the text (nass) comes before or after the ijtihad. The passage emphasizes that the Prophet's ijtihad is like 'ilham (inspiration) and is protected, whereas other mujtahids may err and their error persists unless corrected by dalil. The story is cited from multiple sources as an authoritative example.

Key Terms
عصمة ('isma): Divine protection of the Prophet from persisting in error after expressing an opinion (ijtihad)
اجتهاد (ijtihad): The Prophet's use of personal reasoning in matters where no explicit revelation exists

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Badr captives incident, what happened after the Prophet followed Abu Bakr's opinion to accept ransom?
A) The ransom was prohibited and returned.
B) The Prophet was punished for his error.
C) Revelation confirmed that Umar's opinion was correct, but the ransom already taken was allowed to be consumed.
D) The Prophet's ijtihad was overruled by consensus.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet is infallible from persisting in ijtihad error; other mujtahids are not, so their errors can remain unless corrected by dalil.

The Authority of Inspiration (Ilham) in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the authority of prophetic and saintly inspiration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the prophetic and saintly ilham in terms of legal authority, and apply the Hanafi rule that the Prophet's ilham is a decisive proof while a saint's ilham is not binding on others.

Core Idea
The Prophet's inspiration is decisive proof; a saint's inspiration is personal and cannot be imposed on others.

This passage from Noor al-Anwaar explains a critical distinction in Hanafi usul: the legal authority of inspiration (ilham). While the Prophet's ilham is a form of revelation (wahy) and constitutes a decisive proof (hujja qati'a) binding on all, the ilham of saints (awliya) is not infallible and thus cannot be used as a legal proof for others. There is even disagreement among Hanafi scholars about whether a saint's ilham is proof for himself. This distinction safeguards the primacy of revealed sources and prevents the subjective experiences of individuals from becoming a source of legislation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of ilham
The text distinguishes ilham of the Prophet (peace be upon him) from ilham of saints. For the Prophet, it is a subset of revelation (wahy).
2
Determine the legal authority of each
For the Prophet: decisive proof (hujja qati'a) binding on all Muslims. For saints: not a decisive proof for others; may be proof for themselves if it agrees with the Sharia.
This is the view adopted by the commentator.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., the commentator) hold that a saint's ilham is proof for himself. Others (e.g., Ibn al-Humam) argue it is not proof at all for anyone.
The text presents both opinions.
4
Apply the condition of agreement with Sharia
If the saint's ilham contradicts the Sharia, it is from Satan and has no authority whatsoever.
5
Consider practical consequences
A saint may not impose his ilham on others, nor may he prevent a mujtahid from acting on his valid ijtihad.
This prevents subjective inspiration from overriding scholarly reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في أفعال النبي
النبي
٦١٢
بيان أقسام الوحي عليه وغيره من الأولياء؛ فإنه حجة قاطعة في حقه وإن لم يكن في حق غيره بهذه الصفة، فإلهامه قسم من الوحي يكون حجة متعدّية إلى عامة الخلق، وإلهام الأولياء حجة في حق أنفسهم، إن وافق الشريعة و لم يتعدّ إلى غيرهم إلا إذا أخذنا بقولهم بطريق الآداب ثم شرع في بحث قبلنا من جهة أنها ملحقة بالسنة، واختلف فيها، فقال بعضهم: تلزم علينا مطلقا،
شرائع من
أي من
الله تعالى مع
الأنبياء السابقين
حجة قاطعة إلخ يعني أن الإلهام حجة قاطعة في حقه ، أي إلهامه دليل قطعي لا يجوز المخالفة فيه، وأما "الإلهام في حق غيره أي إلهام غيره من الأولياء فليس بهذه الصفة، أي ليس حجة قاطعة، بل ظنية لعدم العصمة فلا يجب علينا إتباعه، بل يجوز مخالفته. (القمر) فإلهامه إلخ الظاهر أن الفاء للتفسير أو للتعليل، وعلى كل تقدير فلا تطابق بين تقرير الشارح ومحصل المتن؛ فإن إلهام الولي على تقرير الشارح حجة في حق نفسه لا في حق غيره، ومحصل المتن أن إلهام الولي ليس حجة أصلاً، لا في حق نفسه ولا في حق غيره كما هو الظن من عبارة المتن، وهذا هو مختار ابن الهمام، وقد يستدل عليه بأن الإلهام ليس إلا الإلقاء في القلب، وهذا من الخيالات، فلا اعتداد ،به وهذا الاستدلال واه؛ فإن إلهام الولي ليس كخطراتنا بل إلهامه أن يقع في قلبه أمر من علمه الضروري القطعي بأنه من الله فهو حجة بلا ريب كذا قيل. (القمر) يكون حجة أي حجة قطعية بلا امتراء. (القمر) إن وافق الشريعة إلخ فيه إيماء، أي إن إلهام الولي إن خالف الشريعة المحمدية فهو ليس بحجة، لا في حق نفسه ولا في حق غيره، إنما هو من الشيطان الضال المضل. (القمر) إلى غيرهم وهكذا قال عامة العلماء ومشى عليه الإمام السهر وردي واعتمده الإمام الرازي وابن الصلاح من الشافعية، كذا في "الصبح الصادق" فليس للولي أن يدعو غيره إلى إلهامه ولا أن يمنع مجتهدا يعمل باجتهاده الصحيح وإن علم بإلهام أن اجتهاده خطأ . (القمر) ملحقة بالسنة إلخ : بهذا القول أشار الشارح إلى هذا البحث في فصل أصل السنة لا في الإجماع أو القياس أو الكتاب وقوله واختلف فيها فقال بعضهم إلخ قلت: هذا بيان الاختلاف في التعبد بالشرائع السابقة بعد بعث النبي ، وأما قبله فهل كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يتعبد بها أم لا؟ فأبى بعضهم ذالك كأبي الحسن البصري وجماعة من المتكلمين، وأثبته بعضهم مختلفين فيه أيضًا. ثم اختلف هذا البعض في أن رسول الله بشريعةِ أي نبي كان متعبدًا؟ فقيل : بشرع نوح عليها، وقيل: بشرع إبراهيم علئلا، وقيل: غير ذالك كذا في "الغاية". (السنبلي) واختلف فيها : أي في الشرائع السابقة في التعبد بها. (القمر) باقية إلى قيام الساعة لأنها من مرضياته تعالى إلا أن تلزم علينا مطلقا : بناءً على أن كل شريعة تثبت لنبي فهي ! يقوم الدليل على انتساخه، وقد قال الله تعالى: أُولَئِكَ الَّذِينَ هَدَى اللهُ فَيهْدَاهُمُ اقْتَدِهُ (الأنعام: ۹۰) فعلى هذا يلزمنا شرائع من قبلنا مطلقا، وعليه عامة أصحاب الشافعي وبعض مشائخنا ولقائل أن يقول: إن كونها من مرضياته تعالى لا يستلزم أن يبقى إلى الساعة، لِمَ لا يجوز أن تكون من مرضياته تعالى إلى حياة ذالك النبي أو إلى مدة معينة، فإنه تعالى حكيم يضل بمصالح ، ولا يُسأل مما يفعل. (القمر)
صد الله
سب
إيراد
Chapter on the actions of the Prophet. The Prophet (peace be upon him) and other saints: For him it is a decisive proof, but for others it is not with this quality. His inspiration is a division of revelation that is a proof transmitted to the general creation. The inspiration of saints is a proof for themselves, if it agrees with the Sharia, and it does not extend to others unless we take their saying by way of etiquette. Then he began a discussion of [the laws] before us, from the perspective that they are annexed to the Sunnah, and there is disagreement about them. Some said: They are binding upon us absolutely. 'Laws of' meaning from Allah through the previous prophets. 'Decisive proof' etc., meaning that inspiration is a decisive proof for him, i.e., his inspiration is a decisive evidence that it is not permissible to oppose. As for inspiration in the right of others, i.e., the inspiration of other saints, it is not with this quality, i.e., it is not a decisive proof, rather it is speculative due to the lack of infallibility, so we are not obliged to follow it; rather it is permissible to oppose it. (Al-Qamar): 'So his inspiration etc.' Apparently the 'fa' is for explanation or causation, and in any case there is no correspondence between the exposition of the commentator and the conclusion of the text: the inspiration of the saint according to the commentator's exposition is a proof for himself, not for others, but the conclusion of the text is that the inspiration of the saint is not a proof at all, neither for himself nor for others, as is apparent from the wording of the text. This is the choice of Ibn al-Humam. It may be argued that inspiration is nothing but an impression in the heart, and this is from fantasies, so it is not regarded. But this argument is weak: the inspiration of the saint is not like our random thoughts; rather his inspiration is that a matter falls into his heart from his necessary certain knowledge that it is from Allah, so it is a proof without doubt. Such has been said. (Al-Qamar): 'it is a proof' means a decisive proof without hesitation. (Al-Qamar): 'if it agrees with the Sharia etc.' There is an indication: if the inspiration of the saint contradicts the Muhammadan Sharia, then it is not a proof, neither for himself nor for others; it is only from the misguiding devil. (Al-Qamar): 'to others' and thus said the generality of scholars, and Imam al-Suhrawardi followed it, and Imam al-Razi and Ibn al-Salah from the Shafi'is relied on it. Such is in 'al-Subh al-Sadiq'. So the saint may not call others to his inspiration, nor prevent a mujtahid from acting on his correct ijtihad, even if he knows through inspiration that his ijtihad is wrong. (Al-Qamar): 'appended to the Sunnah etc.': By this statement the commentator pointed to this research in the chapter on the foundation of the Sunnah, not in consensus or analogy or the Book. And his saying 'and they differed about it' etc. I say: This is an explanation of the disagreement regarding acting upon the previous laws after the sending of the Prophet. As for before it, was the Messenger of Allah acting upon them or not? Some denied it, like Abu al-Hasan al-Basri and a group of theologians, and some affirmed it, with further disagreement among them. Then these disagreed about which prophet's law the Messenger acted upon. It was said: upon the law of Nuh (peace be upon him), and said: upon the law of Ibrahim, and said: other than that, such is in 'al-Ghayah'. (Al-Sunbulī): 'and they differed about it' i.e., about the previous laws regarding acting upon them. (Al-Qamar): 'remaining until the Day of Resurrection because they are from His pleasing acts unless they are binding upon us absolutely': based on the idea that every law established for a prophet, unless evidence of its abrogation exists, and Allah said: 'Those are the ones whom Allah has guided, so follow their guidance' (al-An'am 6:90). Upon this, the laws of those before us are binding upon us absolutely. And upon this are the generality of the Shafi'is and some of our teachers. But it can be said: That they are from His pleasing acts does not necessitate that they remain until the Hour. Why is it not permissible that they be from His pleasing acts until the life of that prophet or for a specified period? Verily, He is Wise, He does as He wills, and He is not asked about what He does. (Al-Qamar).
Source pages p. 613

Commentary
This passage covers two important usul topics: the authority of inspiration (ilham) and the binding nature of previous divine laws. First, it distinguishes between the Prophet's ilham and that of saints (awliya). For the Prophet, ilham is a form of revelation that is decisive proof (hujja qati'a) binding on all people. For saints, their ilham is not proof for others, because saints are not infallible (ma'sum). There is a disagreement among Hanafi scholars whether the saint's ilham is proof for himself: some say it is (as per the commentator), while others (like Ibn al-Humam) say it is not proof at all. However, if the saint's ilham contradicts the Sharia, it is undoubtedly from Satan. This is important for the principle that no one can impose their personal spiritual experiences on others, and a mujtahid is not to be prevented from his valid ijtihad even if a saint claims inspiration to the contrary. Second, the passage discusses the laws of previous prophets (shara'i' man qablana) and whether they are binding on the Muslim community. The text presents the view of the majority of Shafi'is and some Hanafi scholars that they are binding absolutely, based on the Quranic verse commanding to follow the guidance of previous prophets (6:90). Others argue that they are only binding if not abrogated, and that being pleasing to Allah in their time does not guarantee their permanence. The commentator notes that this discussion belongs under the sources of law as an annex to the Sunnah, not to consensus or analogy.

Key Terms
إلهام (ilham): Inspiration; a spiritual impression that a person believes to be from Allah. For the Prophet it is a form of revelation; for saints it is not.
حجة قاطعة (hujja qati'a): A conclusive proof that is certain and must be followed; cannot be opposed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the authority of the inspiration (ilham) of a saint according to the preferred Hanafi view in this passage?
A) It is a decisive proof for all Muslims.
B) It is a proof for the saint himself only, and not for others, provided it agrees with the Sharia.
C) It is not a proof at all, even for the saint himself.
D) It is a proof for others only if the saint is a mujtahid.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's inspiration is a decisive proof for all; a saint's inspiration is only personal and cannot be imposed on others.
